- 2026-06-24 - iter68 (TASKBAR FIXED - root cause found + fixed + VISUALLY CONFIRMED). The whole iter51-67 "garbage bar height ~10204" campaign roots in ONE bug: pango's insert_run (pango-layout.c) does `PangoLayoutRun *run = g_slice_new(PangoLayoutRun)` (g_slice = malloc in glib 2.82, NOT zeroed) and sets only ->item and ->glyphs; ->y_offset / ->start_x_offset / ->end_x_offset are otherwise set ONLY by apply_baseline_shift(), which runs only for baseline-shifted text. For ordinary runs, y_offset was read UNINITIALIZED at pango-layout.c (y_offset = run->y_offset), so run_logical.y = glyph_y - y_offset = -garbage; the line-extent accumulation MAX(0, -garbage+clean_h) - MIN(0,-garbage) then yields logical_rect.height = +garbage; pango_layout_get_pixel_size returns it; swaybar's height=max() ratchet locks the bar at ~10204px -> 1280x10204 surface covers the whole screen -> "no taskbar". LATENT UPSTREAM bug (relies on malloc returning zeroed memory) exposed by MakaOS's dirty free-list reuse (clean Linux pages read 0 -> y_offset=0 by luck). DIAGNOSIS PATH that nailed it: poison-on-free made it deterministic (iter65); a malloc-handout STAMP (0x50|size) vs free-poison (0x40|size) proved REUSED/UNINIT not UAF (iter66); a size-encoding stamp + visible PXMARKN stat-markers through pango_layout_run/line/get_extents_internal/empty-extents/cache (iter67-68) isolated it: run-level clean, line-level garbage, cache stored garbage, and GLE_rawy = -stamp pinned run->y_offset. FIX: zero run->y_offset/start_x_offset/end_x_offset at creation in insert_run. Persisted as Patch 2 in scripts/port-pango.sh patch_pango() (idempotent, survives clean re-extract). VERIFIED: SBDIM_h now = 18px (was 10204) across 3 boots, 0 diagnostic markers fire, and a QMP screendump shows the real sway desktop (blue wallpaper + SWAY logo) WITH a thin taskbar at the top (saved ~/sway-fixed-taskbar.png). Reverted the libc.c poison/stamp debug. REMAINING (next): remove the leftover diagnostic markers from the untracked DE source (pango-layout.c PXMARKN/PLG/GEI/GLE/EMP/LCACHE/LSTORE, common/pango.c PXBAD/RETBAD, swaybar render.c IDH_*, bar.c SBDIM/SBANCHOR) and do a clean-rebuild verification through port-pango.sh. autofix HEAD 6b959e3 -> committing port-pango.sh fix now.

- 2026-06-24 - iter70 (pango fix A/B-confirmed by user + zero-on-free hardening added). User asked to verify the fix: removed ONLY the 3-line y_offset init from a clean pristine pango, rebuilt, and the garbage bar height returned (intermittent - the uninit read picks up whatever dirty heap is in the reused block), confirming run->y_offset was the bug and the init is the fix. Re-added the fix. Then, per the user's choice, added a zero-on-free hardening to libc free(): memset the freed payload to 0 (header below payload is untouched, so the free-list link is safe). This makes malloc effectively return zeroed memory for reused blocks too, neutralizing the whole class of ported-lib uninitialized-field reads + clearing intra-process freed secrets. IMPORTANT security clarification (user raised it): the libc change is INTRA-process only; the cross-process info-leak boundary is the KERNEL's job and is ALREADY handled - vmm_get_user_pages (vmm.c:337) and isr14_page_fault (vmm.c:949) memset every anonymous frame to 0 before mapping it into a process (pmm itself does not zero, PMM_DEBUG_ALWAYS_ZERO=0, but the VMM mapping layer does, which is the correct layer). VERIFIED: fix + zero-on-free -> SBDIM_h reliably 18px across 6 boots, sway/wlroots/cairo/pango all boot clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - iter71 (swaybar red "[error reading from status command]" - root-caused to a real KERNEL pipe-poll bug + a bash-limited status command). The bar rendered (taskbar fix held) but the status area showed red error text. Chase: STPROTO marker showed PROTOCOL_ERROR; the error is set in bar.c status_in() on POLLHUP|POLLERR from the eventloop poll of the status pipe (mask=17=POLLIN|POLLHUP). TWO bugs: (1) KERNEL: pipe_read_poll (kernel/fs/pipe.c) IGNORED its `events` argument and always answered the readability question (count>0 || writers==0). fd_has_hup() calls f->poll(f, POLLHUP) and ORs the result into revents, so a POLLHUP probe returned true whenever the pipe held buffered DATA - a spurious POLLHUP that makes swaybar treat a live status command as crashed. FIXED: honor `events` - POLLHUP only when writer_refs==0. (2) The status command `while printf "%(%Y-%m-%d %X)T\n"; do read -t 1; done` exits with code 2 (confirmed via waitpid: STCHILD_exited_2): this bash build supports neither printf %()T (errors) nor read -t (no timeout), and block-buffers builtin output to a pipe. A clock loop therefore either exits (red error) or busy-fork-storms a subshell-per-tick (observed #GP). DECISION: disabled the status_command in build.sh with a comment (bar still shows workspaces; absent status_command renders no status, no red). A real clock needs a small C status helper (loop: print time; fflush; nanosleep) or a bash rebuilt with %()T/read-t - noted as a future improvement. VERIFIED: status disabled -> 0/3 #GP, 0/3 red error, taskbar 18px + workspaces across boots; the #GP was the subshell status command, NOT a kernel regression. The kernel pipe-poll fix is kept regardless (genuine correctness bug for any pipe poll consumer). Diag markers (STPROTO/STHUP/STCHILD/SBDIM etc.) remain in untracked DE source; cleanup pending. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - iter72 (reverted zero-on-free per user; added /bin/makaclock clock helper - works at the status level but a swaybar text-status bug destabilizes the bar, so left disabled). (1) REVERTED the libc zero-on-free (iter70): not needed - the pango run->y_offset fix is the real taskbar fix and works without it; zero-on-free only masks the broader uninit-read class (against "fix the fragile design"), and the cross-process leak boundary is already the KERNEL's job (vmm.c:337/949 zero anon frames before mapping into a process). (2) Added userland/apps/makaclock - a tiny native swaybar status helper (formats UTC time via gmtime_r+snprintf, one unbuffered write(2)/sec, nanosleep, never exits) to replace the broken bash clock loop (this bash lacks printf %()T and read -t and block-buffers builtin output). makaclock WORKS at the status level: swaybar reads it (STAVAIL_33 = "MakaOS ... UTC\n"), no red error, no exit. BUT it REGRESSES the bar: with a TEXT status swaybar reads, the bar gets the layer (SB_O6) but never configures (no SBDIM_h) or commits (no SB_O8) - committed in only 1/4 boots vs 3/3 with status disabled, plus an occasional #GP. - 2026-06-24 - iter73 (chased the swaybar text-status bar-destabilization + did the diag-marker cleanup; clock still blocked by a sway layer-shell race). Per the user's "both": (A) Root-caused the text-status-breaks-bar bug. Instrumented render_frame: the computed bar height is SANE (RFH=18/6, the pango fix holds), but output->height stays 0 (RFOH=0) - sway never sends the first layer-surface CONFIGURE, so the bar never commits a buffer. A live text status (makaclock) triggers extra render_frame()s during bar setup; each recomputes a (sometimes-oscillating 6<->18) height and re-issues set_size+commit, and sway intermittently never configures back. Tried swaybar-side guards via a new output->requested_height: (i) "only re-request on height change" -> 2/5 commit (eliminated the earlier #GP); (ii) "don't re-request at all while awaiting the first configure" -> 0/6 (WORSE - re-requests are actually NEEDED to coax sway's configure out). So it is a sway COMPOSITOR layer-shell first-configure reliability race, not a clean swaybar fix - deeper than scope. Delaying makaclock's first output 3s (status arrives after setup) gave 3/4, confirming the init-window race. DECISION: reverted the swaybar guard experiments by re-extracting pristine sway source (swaybar/bar.c, render.c, status_line.c, include/swaybar/bar.h, common/pango.c) - which ALSO completed (B) the diag-marker cleanup (removed ALL SB_*/SBDIM/STPROTO/RFH/PXBAD/RETBAD/GTSBUG/IDH probes; swaybar binary now has 0 diag strings). makaclock stays BUILT (/bin/makaclock) but status_command DISABLED so the taskbar renders reliably. VERIFIED: clean build boots 0 #GP / 0 panic across boots; functionally identical to the earlier status-disabled builds that committed the bar 4/4 and screendumped the taskbar (~/sway-taskbar-FIXED.png). zero-on-free reverted (iter72). NEXT (deferred): sway layer-shell first-configure race -> enables the makaclock clock. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - iter74 (CLOCK ROOT CAUSE found + fixed: kernel pipe_read ignored O_NONBLOCK; ALSO found my own earlier swaybar roundtrip-loop was a harmful misfix). Picked up iter73's deferred "live text status destabilizes the bar" and traced it to the end. Findings: (1) ROOT CAUSE of the frozen clock is a KERNEL bug: pipe_read (kernel/fs/pipe.c) NEVER checked O_NONBLOCK. On an empty pipe with a live writer it ALWAYS blocked via WAIT_EVENT_HOOK, so a non-blocking read returned data-or-blocked-forever, never -EAGAIN. swaybar sets its status_command read_fd O_NONBLOCK (status_line.c:180) and its status_handle_readable TEXT path loops getline() until EAGAIN; with the bug getline() blocked FOREVER on the empty status pipe between makaclock's 1/sec writes, so status_in() never returned, swaybar's event loop never reached loop_poll again, the bar never re-rendered, and the clock froze. This is ALSO the mechanism behind iter72/73's "text status destabilizes the bar" - it was the getline-block, NOT a layer-shell race. PROOF: instrumented status_line.c - GLPRE (about to getline) fired, GLPOST (getline returned) NEVER fired => getline blocked; traced into the kernel and found pipe_read had no O_NONBLOCK branch (unlike unix_sock_recv which does). FIX: pipe_read now returns total>0?total:-EAGAIN when count==0 && writer_refs!=0 && (self->flags & O_NONBLOCK), mirroring unix_sock_send/recv. Genuine correctness bug for ANY non-blocking pipe reader, kept regardless of the clock. (2) MISFIX FOUND: a prior swaybar bar_run "roundtrip loop" (wl_display_roundtrip x50 before adding the status fd, added in an earlier iteration to coax the configure) was actively HARMFUL - A/B test showed it made wl_display_flush return ENOTCONN(107) right after setup (sway resets the connection), so swaybar EXITED. Removed it; pristine swaybar (no roundtrip) reaches loop_poll cleanly (PCALL/PRET/STIN fire). The clean rebuild re-extracts pristine swaybar, so this is gone. (3) makaclock CONFIRMED correct: instrumented its loop - MCLKTOP/MCLKW/MCLKS fire for iters 0..9+, so time()/snprintf/write/sleep all work; makaclock writes every second as intended. build.sh re-enables `status_command /bin/makaclock` (paired with the pipe fix). VERIFICATION LIMIT: end-to-end visual tick NOT cleanly confirmed - after 40+ automated boots the test host degraded (load was 8, now recovering) and the desktop startup is dominated by separate pre-existing non-determinism (sway sometimes does not spawn swaybar; intermittent #GP/#XM SIMD-FP crashes before the desktop loads - suspect host/KVM-under-load + the known present-path/layer-shell WIP). The clock-FREEZE mechanism is fixed and proven; the desktop START reliability is the remaining separate problem. NEXT: (a) clean-rebuild + verify the tick on a fresh/unloaded host; (b) the sway startup #GP/#XM + layer-shell first-configure reliability; (c) leftover untracked diag markers in build/third_party/sway (GLPRE/GLPOST/STIN/PCALL/CFG/RTOC/HFRAME/SFDH etc.) - removed by a clean sway re-extract. main untouched; committing pipe.c + build.sh to autofix.

- 2026-06-24 - iter82 (TOFU ROOT FIXED at the scan level: libc opendir over-allocated 1.07MB and FAILED, so fontconfig never scanned the font dirs). Root: opendir() (userland/libc/libc.c) did `malloc(4096 * sizeof(k_dirent_t))` = 4096 * 268B = ~1.07MB BEFORE calling _sys_readdir. In a port's heap (fontconfig/swaybar) that single large malloc fails -> opendir returns NULL WITHOUT ever issuing SYS_READDIR -> the directory silently looks empty -> fontconfig indexes 0 fonts -> FcFontMatch no-match -> pango .notdef fallback -> TOFU. This is exactly why iter81's kernel [rddiag] (in ext2_readdir) fired 0x: ext2_readdir was never reached. Also a CLAUDE.md scalability violation (1MB per opendir regardless of dir size). FIX: grow-on-demand in opendir - start at 64 entries (~17KB), double on truncation (sys_readdir re-reads from the start, so a larger max simply re-reads); memory now tracks the dir's actual size. VERIFIED at the scan level: rebuilt (build.sh rebuilds libc.a -> port-sway.sh relinks swaybar -> build.sh assembles; NO_QEMU=1 so the chain doesn't block on QEMU) and booted via bootclean.sh - [rddiag] NOW fires: /usr/share/fonts count=1 (truetype), /usr/share/fonts/truetype count=1 (dejavu), /usr/share/fonts/truetype/dejavu count=22 (all TTFs). So fontconfig can now index the DejaVu fonts. NOT yet visually confirmed readable (the boot that scanned fonts did not render the bar this time - the separate ~2/3 intermittency; makaclock also did not load). NEXT: catch a boot where the bar renders + fonts are scanned, screendump to confirm the text is readable DejaVu (not tofu); then verify the clock ticks (two screendumps). REVERTED the [rddiag] debug kprintf from kernel/fs/ext2.c. Committing the opendir fix. main untouched.

(c) Therefore best stays NULL only if 0 fonts are iterated. Confirmed with FCNSETS/FCSETS in FcFontSetMatchInternal: FCNSETS_1 + FCSETS_0 (x6) = the match gets ONE set with ZERO fonts. (d) But FcConfigAddCache added 22 fonts to config->fonts[FcSetSystem] (FCADDREF_22 x2). So the config the match searches is NOT the config that got the 22 fonts. A non-NULL-but-EMPTY config->fonts[FcSetSystem] means FcConfigBuildFonts ran on the match's config but its config->fontDirs were EMPTY (FcConfigBuildFonts: FcFontSetCreate empty -> FcConfigSetFonts -> FcConfigAddDirList(config->fontDirs); empty fontDirs => empty set). So the match's config never loaded /etc/fonts/fonts.conf's <dir> entries, while the built config (FCADDREF_22) did. (FcConfigSetCurrent builds fonts when a config becomes current, so the current config should have them - yet the match's doesn't, so the match uses a non-current/private/empty config, or there is config re-creation. Note: sway, swaybar, swaybg each STATICALLY link libfontconfig.a = separate fontconfig state per process.) NEXT: add getpid() into the FCADDREF + FCMATCH/FCSETS markers (fontconfig can call getpid) to determine if the build and the empty-match are the SAME process - if different, swaybar's own fontconfig has empty fontDirs (it does not load fonts.conf) while another process's does; if same, a within-process config re-creation/identity bug. Then FIX: make the match's config load fonts.conf / share the built config; robust candidate = ship a prebuilt fc-cache so matching does not depend on the live per-process config build. All FCFAM/FCMATCH/FCREQ/FCADDCACHE/FCADDREF/FCNSETS/FCSETS/FCTMISS markers are in untracked fontconfig source - revert before committing a fix. main untouched.

- 2026-06-24 - iter89 (FONT FIX VISUALLY CONFIRMED + present-path memory overturned + freeze narrowed to the post-startup frame loop). So the clock can't visibly tick and the full bar/wallpaper never finish compositing. The stalled serial timestamps were just "no logging when idle," not a stopped clock - so makaclock's sleep(1) DOES wake and it writes a new HH:MM:SS every second (makaclock.c is a correct forever-loop, unbuffered write+sleep). (5) Read the whole status->redraw chain and it looks CORRECT in code: makaclock write -> kernel pipe_write wakes read_file->waitq (pipe.c:121) -> sys_poll registers the task on f->waitq and re-checks readiness (syscall.c:3801) -> swaybar status_in (bar.c:506) -> status_handle_readable text path getline-until-EAGAIN returns true (status_line.c:118) -> set_bar_dirty -> render_frame. - 2026-06-24 - iter90 (THE CLOCK WORKS: readable + ticking. Root-caused + fixed the tiny/cramped bar text). After iter89 proved the font/tofu fix and the frame loop, the bar text was confirmed (by the user, on-screen) as unreadable: microscopic, glyphs cramped/overlapping, half off the right edge. (d) But text was STILL tiny/cramped after the dpi fix -> the real culprit: pango's create_hb_font (pangofc-font.c) called hb_ft_font_set_funcs() BEFORE hb_font_set_scale(). hb_ft_font_set_funcs sizes the backing FT_Face from the hb font's CURRENT scale at call time, so attaching the FT funcs before the scale was set left the FT_Face at its default size -> every glyph metric + advance came out microscopic and collapsed (cramped). This was a latent bug in the earlier MakaOS "shape via FreeType cmap" tofu patch (it inserted hb_ft_font_set_funcs right after hb_font_create). FIX: reorder so the scale + ptem are set first, then attach the FT funcs. (1970 epoch because MakaOS has no RTC; it counts up from boot.) Both pango fixes are encoded durably in scripts/port-pango.sh patch_pango (hb_ft scale-first reorder + get_resolution 96dpi guard), verified by a clean rm+re-extract+re-patch. - 2026-06-24 - audit T1/F3 FIXED: dcache resurrect-from-zero UAF (kernel/fs/dcache.c). dcache_lookup bumped a hashed dentry's refcount 0->1 with a bare fetch_add while the shrinker freed refcount-0 dentries; a lookup resurrecting a dentry between the shrinker's refcount read and its RCU-deferred free left a freed slot referenced/on-LRU (UAF). refcount 0 = ALIVE here (not dead), so vfs_tryget does not apply; fixed with a DCACHE_REF_DYING sentinel - shrinker CAS 0->DYING (skip on fail), lookup CAS-bumps from any non-DYING value (DYING => treat as miss + keep walking). Added dcache_race_selftest (SELFTESTS=1): 2 lookers + shrinker + reinstalls over a 16-key set, 50000 iters, asserts no child_ino corruption - PASSES post-fix, existing dcache/chaselev/slab/kheap selftests still pass, boot healthy, normal (non-SELFTESTS) build compiles. The race window is tiny so the stress test is a regression guard; primary confirmation is the TOCTOU code proof. Related sub-issue noted (not yet fixed): dcache_invalidate frees via call_rcu without checking refcount (invalidate-vs-holder), far rarer. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - audit F4 FIXED: unvalidated user-pointer memcpy across 6 syscalls (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). The FS auditor flagged sys_readdir; verifying it uncovered a systemic pattern - sys_readdir(x2), sys_stat, sys_unlink, sys_getcwd, sys_chdir, sys_mkdir all did raw __builtin_memcpy directly on user pointers (the path arg, and for readdir/getcwd the OUTPUT buffer) with no validation. A bad pointer faulted the kernel (DoS); the readdir/getcwd writes took a user-supplied destination -> a kernel address gave an arbitrary kernel write (priv-esc primitive). Routed all 7 sites through the existing copy_from_user/copy_to_user (_access_ok + prefault -> -EFAULT), matching the file's own sys_poll/sys_stat-sibling pattern; added a forward decl near _access_ok so syscalls above the definition can use them. Left alone: the guarded spawn-attr copy (already had _access_ok) and getcwd's kernel-HHDM write (kernel-owned frame). Test: copy_user_selftest (SELFTESTS=1) asserts copy_from_user/copy_to_user reject kernel/non-canonical/past-ceiling/NULL pointers with -EFAULT and do not fault - PASSES; all prior selftests still pass; boot reaches userland (readdir/stat/chdir are hammered during init -> confirms no regression for valid pointers); normal build compiles. Also re-scoped T3 (AF_UNIX UAF) in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md: it is NOT a quick fix (the STREAM send blocks + caches/derefs peer across iterations), treat like T2. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - audit F5/T5 FIXED: signal_send non-atomic sigstate.blocked RMW (kernel/proc/signal.c + kernel/syscall/syscall.c). signal_send's SIGKILL-unblock (`blocked &= ~bit`) is a non-atomic read-modify-write on the TARGET task's mask from the SENDER's CPU, racing the owner's own RMWs in sys_sigprocmask (|=/&=) and signal_setup_frame (|=) -> torn update (SIGKILL clear lost, or a mask bit corrupted). pending was already atomic; only blocked RMWs were not. Fixed all four RMW sites with atomic_and/atomic_or (smp.h): signal.c signal_send + signal_setup_frame x2, syscall.c sys_sigprocmask SIG_BLOCK/SIG_UNBLOCK. Left the SIG_SETMASK full store + init stores plain (aligned 32-bit store is atomic on x86; SETMASK masks SIGKILL out, so it can't clobber signal_send's clear). No bespoke test: tiny-window cross-CPU data race + signal_send logs per call (a faithful high-iteration test floods serial) - honest regression-guard reasoning like T1. Confirmed: both builds compile, normal build boots to userland (login/shell exercise sigprocmask), SELFTEST build all 8 selftests PASS, no PANIC. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - audit F6 FIXED: ext2_readdir dirent name over-read (kernel/fs/ext2.c). The dirent walk validated only that the 8-byte header fit (off+8<=blk_bytes) then copied up to name_len (<=255) bytes from de->name[]; a corrupt/short on-disk dirent near the block tail (e.g. header at off=4088, name starting at the 4096 slot end) read past the 4096-byte bcache slot -> out-of-bounds read leaking adjacent kernel memory into the returned filename. A valid ext2 dir never hits this, but a corrupt/malicious dir block does. Fixed by extracting a pure helper ext2_dirent_namelen_clamp(off,name_len,blk_bytes) = min(name_len, bytes-left-after-header) and clamping the name there before the copy + dot/dotdot checks. Deterministic test ext2_readdir_clamp_selftest (SELFTESTS=1) exhaustively checks the boundary arithmetic incl. the 4088/4090 over-read cases (clamp to 0) - PASSES; all 8 prior selftests still pass; normal + SELFTEST builds compile; clean boot (ext2_readdir is hammered by path resolution/ls). main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - audit F7 FIXED: eventfd POLLOUT starvation (kernel/io/eventfd.c). The eventfd file exposed only read_wq as f->waitq with f->secondary_waitq=NULL, but POLLOUT (write readiness) wakeups fire on a separate write_wq when a reader drains a full eventfd. Since sys_poll/sys_select register a waiter on both f->waitq and f->secondary_waitq, a task polling a FULL eventfd for POLLOUT registered only on read_wq and was never woken when space opened -> starvation. One-line fix: f->secondary_waitq = &s->write_wq. Extended the existing eventfd_selftest with Case 5: force count=EVENTFD_MAX (count is u64; eventfd_new's init_val is only u32 so set it directly), assert poll reports POLLIN but not POLLOUT, and assert secondary_waitq == &write_wq. All 9 boot selftests PASS, 0 FAILED/PANIC; both builds compile; shipping disk rebuilt clean. Low reachability (full eventfd = 2^64-2) but a clean correct fix. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - SECOND AUDIT PASS (un-audited subsystems via 4-agent fan-out: ELF, TTY/PTY, AHCI/bcache, futex/io_uring) found 4 clean findings; fixed the two cleanest+highest-value this iter. F8: ext2 dir_lookup name over-read (kernel/fs/ext2.c) - the F6 readdir clamp MISSED the parallel dirent walk in dir_lookup, which underlies every path resolution (open/stat/exec) so it is MORE reachable than readdir; same OOB-read-past-bcache-slot on a corrupt dirent. Fixed by routing through the existing ext2_dirent_namelen_clamp helper (forward-declared since dir_lookup precedes the definition); covered by ext2_readdir_clamp_selftest. F9: io_uring OP_READ/OP_WRITE passed the user-controlled sqe->addr straight to vfs_read/vfs_write/pread with NO validation (every other opcode routes through a sys_* wrapper) - OP_READ with a kernel addr = arbitrary kernel WRITE, OP_WRITE = arbitrary kernel READ -> CRITICAL LPE. Fixed: new exported user_buf_check(addr,len) = _access_ok (mm-independent range LPE guard) + user_buf_prefault (unmapped-user-ptr panic prevention), called before both ops; copy_user_selftest extended to assert user_buf_check rejects kernel/non-canonical/ceiling/NULL. - 2026-06-24 - F10 FIXED: PTY ioctl arbitrary kernel R/W (kernel/drivers/tty/pty.c). pty_master_ioctl/pty_slave_ioctl cast the raw user `arg` to kernel pointers and read/wrote through it (TCGETS/TIOCGWINSZ/TIOCGPGRP/TIOCGPTN = arbitrary kernel WRITE; TCSETS/TIOCSWINSZ/TIOCSPGRP = arbitrary kernel READ) - a CRITICAL LPE from any process that opens /dev/ptmx or /dev/pts/N. The console tty0 path was fixed in the prior audit but PTY was missed. Fixed by routing both through one shared pty_tty_ioctl_common(tty,request,arg) using copy_from_user/copy_to_user (DRY - master+slave act on the same slave tty; also fixed the slave's "TODO: send SIGWINCH" by unifying). pty_ioctl_selftest (SELFTESTS=1): pty_open_master then assert all 7 ioctls x 3 bad pointers (kernel/non-canonical/NULL) return -EFAULT -> PASSED. 10 selftests PASS, 0 FAILED/PANIC; both builds compile. main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - F11 (was T2) FIXED: CoW/fork PTE+refcount race (kernel/mm/vmm.c vmm_clone_user_ex). The clone wrote the parent PTE read-only + pmm_ref_inc WITHOUT vma_lock, while the CoW-break fault handler makes the same rc-based decision (rc==1 -> just make writable, no copy; else copy) UNDER mm->vma_lock. A sibling thread of the parent faulting the page after the clone set it RO but before the ref_inc reads rc==1 -> parent+child share a WRITABLE frame with a skewed refcount -> later double pmm_ref_dec frees a still-mapped frame (UAF). In-tree comments document real victims (foot font loaders, sway glib worker). CRITICAL. Fixed: take src_mm->vma_lock per-PTE around the read-decide-write (read src_pt[si] -> VMA lookup -> RO write + ref_inc); per-PTE not whole-walk so concurrent faults on OTHER pages still progress; the fault handler uses plain spin_lock(&mm->vma_lock) so matched it (no irqsave - faults are exceptions, not IRQs). Verified no self-deadlock: task_fork (process.c:414) and sys_thread (syscall.c:1185) call the clone holding no vma_lock; the clone touches only page-table/HHDM memory so it can't fault under the lock. Tiny-window race -> no deterministic test (consistent with F2/F3/F5); code proof + clean boot that fork-execs /bin/login + /bin/svcmgr (exercises the clone) with no deadlock/corruption + all 10 selftests PASS + both builds compile. Note: a small added cost is fork holding vma_lock per CoW PTE (brief). main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - F12 FIXED: ELF e_phoff integer-overflow OOB read (kernel/proc/elf.c). elf_load_into's sole phdr-table bounds guard `e_phoff + (uint64_t)phnum*56 > size` added unchecked 64-bit values; a malicious e_phoff near UINT64_MAX (e.g. 0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFC8 = -56, phnum=1) wrapped the sum to 0 (<= size), passed the check, then the phdr iteration read `data + e_phoff` = data-56, i.e. 56 bytes BEFORE the header buffer (OOB heap read whose bytes are trusted as a program header driving segment VA/offset). Reachable by any process that execs a crafted binary. Fixed: extracted pure overflow-safe elf_phtab_in_bounds(e_phoff,phnum,size) = (phnum!=0) && e_phoff<=size && phnum*56<=size-e_phoff (phnum<=65535 so phnum*56 can't overflow), replacing the inline check. elf_phtab_bounds_selftest (SELFTESTS=1) checks the -56 wrap + off==size + exact-fit + one-past + phnum 0/73/74 boundaries -> PASSED. 11 selftests PASS, 0 FAILED/PANIC; both builds compile; valid ELFs (login/svcmgr/net) still load at boot (exec exercises elf_load_into) so no regression. Logged a DoS-leaning follow-up: p_vaddr not range-checked + seg_end overflow (elf.c:157). main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - F13 FIXED: ELF PT_LOAD segment-range overflow / unchecked vaddr (kernel/proc/elf.c, F12 follow-up). elf_load_into mapped each PT_LOAD with seg_start=(p_vaddr+load_bias)&~PAGE_MASK and seg_end=(p_vaddr+load_bias+p_memsz+PAGE_MASK)&~PAGE_MASK, then mm_vma_add(seg_start,seg_end). p_vaddr was never range-checked and the seg_end rounding could wrap: a p_vaddr+load_bias+p_memsz near UINT64_MAX makes seg_end < seg_start -> a bogus/inverted VMA, and a kernel-half / non-canonical p_vaddr -> a mapping that can never be faulted in. Reachable by exec of a crafted binary (DoS-leaning: bad VMA bounds, not a kernel write). Fixed by adding pure overflow-safe elf_seg_range_ok(vaddr,load_bias,memsz,user_top) = (vaddr+bias doesn't wrap) && (vbase < user_top) && (memsz <= user_top - vbase), called per PT_LOAD right after the p_memsz==0 skip (before seg_start/seg_end are derived) with user_top=VMM_USER_STACK_TOP; on failure it tears down (mm_destroy/vmm_free_user/pmm_buddy_free) and returns 0, matching the loop's existing error paths. Extended the elf self-test with 9 segment-range cases (whole-half memsz, normal fixed-load, PIE bias, kernel-half base, vaddr+bias wrap, exact-fit last page, base==top, one-byte-below-top, one-past-top) -> the combined "[elf_test] SELF-TEST PASSED (phdr table + segment range bounds)" PASSES. 11 selftests PASS, 0 FAILED/PANIC; both builds compile; valid ELFs (login/svcmgr) still fork-exec at boot (no regression for well-formed segments). main untouched.
- 2026-06-24 - F14 (T3 part A) FIXED: AF_UNIX vfs_file_t use-after-free + socketpair double-free (kernel/net/unix_sock.c). unix_sock_close kfree'd the vfs_file_t (self) synchronously while only RCU-deferring the unix_sock_t via call_rcu(unix_sock_free_rcu). But a peer holds a RAW back-pointer to that file through peer->file (s->file, set at open), and unix_poll_wake() derefs peer->file->waitq -- called from free_rcu (waking the peer on disconnect), send_ex, recv, and connect. So the file had a SHORTER lifetime than the RCU-alive sock that still points at it: any of those ->file derefs after a close was a use-after-free. Everyday Wayland disconnect pattern (libwayland/pthread churn socketpairs constantly). Root-caused the muddled ownership: ALSO found a real double-free in unix_sock_pair's ENOMEM path -- `unix_sock_close(a); kfree(a);` freed the same vfs_file_t twice (close already owns a's teardown). Fixed by establishing one clean invariant: the vfs_file_t lives exactly as long as its unix_sock_t. Moved the file free out of unix_sock_close into unix_sock_free_rcu (frees the sock, then the file, after the grace period); removed the eager kfree(self); removed the double-free kfree(a). No bespoke deterministic test: this is the F2/F3/F5/F11 tiny-window-UAF + error-path-double-free class, and call_rcu_expedited makes any observe-before-grace-period test racy while a reliable UAF detector would itself risk a UAF. Verified by code proof (the lifetime-invariant argument) + clean boot: SELFTESTS build -> 17 selftests PASS incl. socketpair-selftest and scm_rights-selftest (both exercise the modified create/send/recv/close+free path), 0 FAILED/PANIC, 5 [unix] close teardowns ran through the new deferred-free path, /bin/login fork-exec'd, qemu status running (no triple-fault). The mostly-black framebuffer is the pre-existing documented virtio-gpu present-path WIP, unrelated. STILL OPEN (recorded in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md as T3 part B): the peer-SOCK UAF -- send_ex/recv/connect deref the peer unix_sock_t itself across a blocking sleep with no rcu_read_lock; needs sock refcounting (tryget-under-rcu, Linux af_unix model) or a two-phase RCU free. F14 is a prerequisite for it (sock-lifetime now pins file-lifetime). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F15 (T3 part B) FIXED: AF_UNIX peer-SOCK use-after-free (kernel/net/unix_sock.c + .h, main.c). unix_sock_send_ex BLOCKS (WAIT_EVENT_HOOK on a full peer buffer) while caching peer = s->peer and derefing the cached peer across the sleep (cbuf_write(peer), peer->buf_count in the HOOK condition, unix_wake/poll_wake(peer)) with NO rcu_read_lock; recv's post-drain unix_wake(s->peer), poll's s->peer->buf_count, shutdown's peer wakes, and sendfd's s->peer->ancillary mutation had the same unprotected shape. A concurrent close() RCU-frees the peer unix_sock_t during the block/deref -> UAF on the sock object itself (distinct from F14, which was the vfs_file_t). Fixed with the Linux af_unix lifetime model: added uint32_t refcount to unix_sock_t (init 1 = owning vfs_file_t); a PURE CAS-from-nonzero unix_refcount_tryget(uint32_t*) (refuses to resurrect from 0); unix_get/unix_put (put RCU-defers the free at the 1->0 transition); and unix_pin_peer(s) = read s->peer + tryget under rcu_read_lock (memory-safe: the peer is RCU-freed so its refcount word is valid for the reader section). send_ex now pins the peer for the WHOLE call (held across sleeps), puts at every exit (single stream_out label); the synchronous derefs (recv drain wake, poll buf_count, shutdown) take a brief rcu_read_lock, and sendfd (which mutates the peer's ancillary queue across a vfs_dup) pins the peer. KEY prerequisite invariant: unix_sock_close now notifies the connected peer SYNCHRONOUSLY -- pins the peer, and for a SYMMETRIC stream connection (peer->peer == s) clears the back-pointer + marks DISCONNECTED + wakes, then drops the owner ref -- so a reader observes NULL, never a dangling pointer to freed memory; the notify was moved OUT of unix_sock_free_rcu (which now only frees backlog/dgram/ancillary/file/struct). The peer->peer==s guard also fixes a latent bug where closing a DGRAM socket that connect()'d to a target would wrongly null the target's own peer linkage. Also added "|| !s->peer || state==DISCONNECTED" to the send_ex HOOK condition: without it, a peer-close during a full-buffer block woke the sender but the buf_count condition stayed false (peer gone, never drains) -> sleep-forever lost-wakeup; now the sender wakes and returns EPIPE. Refcount accounting is simple (no connection refs; only the single owner ref + always-balanced transient pins). Deterministic test unix_refcount_selftest (always compiled; called from main.c under MAKAOS_BOOT_SELFTESTS): pure tryget(1)->2, tryget(2)->3, tryget(0)->stays-0; live-socket get/put balance (1->2->1); pin_peer on a connected pair returns the peer with refcount bumped 1->2 then back -> PASS. 18 selftests PASS (was 17), 0 FAILED/PANIC/fault; socketpair-selftest + scm_rights-selftest still PASS (exercise the modified send/recv/close/sendfd); /bin/login fork-exec'd; qemu stayed running through userland AF_UNIX churn (Wayland hammers socketpair/close/poll). Both builds compile; shipping disk rebuilt clean. Scoped out (separate, not part B): the SOCK_DGRAM default-destination dangling pointer (store path + ns_find re-resolve, or a connection ref) -- documented in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F16 (sched_find_pid UAF, part A) FIXED: rcu-unsafe pid lookup + deref across the syscall/signal paths (kernel/proc/signal.c + .h, kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/main.c). sched_find_pid -> pid_ht_find drops its OWN rcu_read_lock before returning a bare task_t*; every caller then dereferenced that pointer OUTSIDE any RCU section, so a concurrent exit+task_destroy (which RCU-defers the free via call_rcu_expedited(task_free_rcu)) could free the task in the lookup->deref window -> use-after-free. Reachable via kill(2), the exit-time SIGCHLD-to-parent path (every process exit), and getpgid/setpgid/getsid. Root-cause fix = hold rcu_read_lock across lookup+use (matches the codebase's pcb_find/ns_find pattern; tasks are RCU-freed). Also a DRY win: sys_exit (syscall.c) and do_exit (signal.c) had IDENTICAL `parent = sched_find_pid(ppid); if (parent && !zombie) signal_send(parent, SIGCHLD)` blocks. Added one helper signal_send_pid(pid, sig) = { rcu_read_lock; t = sched_find_pid(pid); if (t && !zombie) signal_send(t, sig); rcu_read_unlock; return 0/-ESRCH } (signal.c, declared in signal.h next to signal_send_group/pgrp). Routed both SIGCHLD-to-parent sites + sys_kill's lookup case (kept the self fast-path that needs no lookup) through it; wrapped sys_setpgid (lookup + pgid mutation incl. task_idx_pgid_changing/changed), sys_getpgid, sys_getsid field reads in rcu_read_lock with a single unlock path. Verified signal_send is rcu/lock-safe (atomic bit + sched_wake->rq_lock, no sleep; sched.h documents rq_lock is below task_idx locks, no cycle) so holding the reader section across delivery is sound; task_idx_pgid_* are just hash insert/remove (non-sleeping). Added #include errno.h to signal.c (ESRCH). Deterministic signal_send_pid_selftest: signal_send_pid(0xFFFFFFFE, 15) takes the not-found path (no side effects) and must return -ESRCH; reaching the assert proves the rcu_read_lock section balances (a leak would leave preempt disabled and wedge the CPU) -> PASSED. 19 selftests PASS (was 18), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd (so the exit->SIGCHLD-to-parent path ran through signal_send_pid during boot's fork/exit churn); qemu ran healthy through userland (shell job-control exercises getpgid/setpgid). Both builds compile; shipping disk rebuilt clean. PART B STILL OPEN (documented in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md): the /proc (proc_open/proc_readdir x3) + virtfs.c:171 callers whose rcu section must span a multi-return gen()/proc_fd_open use. ALSO this pass: deep-read T4 (TCP per-PCB lock) and recorded a VERIFIED design in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md (contexts; ipv4_send doesn't sleep so the lock can wrap tcp_send_segment; clean data-plane lock ordering; the child<->listener two-lock accept-queue hazard that makes the FULL-switch lock a dedicated-iteration job needing a TCP-loopback self-test since boot drives no TCP) -- not committed as a fix because a TCP locking change is not boot-verifiable and the two-lock hazard needs its own careful pass. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F17 (sched_find_pid UAF, part B) FIXED: the /proc + virtfs pid-lookup callers (kernel/fs/proc.c, kernel/fs/virtfs.c). Completes F16. proc_open (proc_fd_open / gen() snapshot), proc_readdir (proc_pid_readdir / proc_fd_readdir), proc_stat (t->files_shared in the fd/<n> branch), and virtfs's proc-node owner lookup (t->cred.euid/egid) all called sched_find_pid and dereferenced the returned bare task_t* OUTSIDE any RCU section -> same UAF window as F16 (a concurrent exit+task_destroy RCU-frees the task). Verified the preconditions for an rcu-discipline fix: (1) none of the deref helpers sleep -- grep of proc.c found no sched_sleep/sched_block/sched_yield/WAIT_EVENT/mutex/sema, and the gen_*/readdir/fd_open paths use only kmalloc/strbuf (non-blocking) -- so holding rcu_read_lock (== preempt_disable) across them does not violate the no-sleep-in-rcu rule; (2) none store t beyond their call (gen_* return a heap snapshot, proc_fd_open returns a vfs_file_t with its OWN fd ref via vfs_tryget, readdir fills the caller's out[] array); (3) rcu_read_lock is a nestable preempt_depth counter (preempt.h), so proc_fd_open's inner rcu_read_lock nests cleanly under the outer one. Fix: wrapped each caller in rcu_read_lock spanning the lookup + every t deref. The three proc.c functions have many post-lookup returns, so restructured each to a SINGLE exit (goto open_out / rd_out / stat_out with a result var; the post-directory-check region wrapped in a { } block so the gotos don't cross the `const char* sub` initializer) -- guarantees the section is never leaked (a leaked rcu/preempt section would leave preempt disabled and wedge that CPU). virtfs reads t->cred into locals immediately, so a tight 3-line wrap; added #include "rcu.h" to virtfs.c (was not in its include chain). No new deterministic test (pure rcu-wrapping of existing call sites, tiny-window UAF -- F2/F3/F5/F16 class): verified by build (the goto/scope restructure compiles with no "jump crosses initialization") + clean boot (19 selftests PASS, 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd, qemu ran healthy through ~15s of userland with no fault/hang -- an rcu-section leak from a missed unlock would wedge a CPU, so a clean multi-second userland run is positive evidence the sections balance). The exact branch logic of each function is preserved (only `return X` -> `rc = X; goto`). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. sched_find_pid UAF now FULLY closed (F16 syscall/signal paths + F17 /proc/virtfs paths). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F18 (T4 defense-in-depth; the per-PCB lock stays OPEN) FIXED: TCP tx/rx ring-drain underflow (kernel/net/tcp.c, kernel/main.c). The tcp_recv ACK path did `txbuf_head = (txbuf_head + acked) & MASK; txbuf_used -= acked` and tcp_recv_data did the same for rxbuf, with NO clamp. Single-threaded the SEQ_GT/SEQ_LE guards keep acked <= txbuf_used, but under the still-open T4 data race (snd_una/txbuf_used RMW'd from another CPU with no per-PCB lock) -- or a malformed/out-of-window segment -- `acked` can exceed `txbuf_used`, underflowing the u32 to ~4e9, which then wedges the sender's `while txbuf_used >= TCP_TXBUF_SIZE` wait forever (or drives a wild length). Fixed by extracting ONE shared pure helper tcp_ring_consume(head,used,n,mask) that clamps n to *used before advancing head / decrementing used (single source of truth for both ring drains; DRY), used at the txbuf ACK drain and the rxbuf read drain. This is defense-in-depth: it does NOT fix the T4 race (the lock does), but it bounds the race's WORST outcome from catastrophic (underflow -> permanent producer wedge / wild length) to a transient mis-account. Deterministic tcp_ring_consume_selftest (normal drain, head-wrap, OVER-consume -> clamp-to-used, exact-drain-to-empty, already-empty) -> PASSED. 20 selftests PASS (was 19), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd; qemu healthy. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. CRITICALLY, this pass also deep-verified the T4 LOCK design and found two constraints that REVISE it (recorded in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md so the dedicated lock iteration is correct, not a deadlock): (1) spin_lock does NOT disable preemption, so the per-PCB lock must be spin_lock_irqsave (else preempted-holder + same-CPU-spinner deadlock); (2) virtio_net_tx does a synchronous polling wait (up to 10M spins) holding s_tx_lock, so the per-PCB lock must NOT wrap tcp_send_segment (IRQs-off across a whole tx poll is unacceptable) -- the transmit must move OUTSIDE the lock, which requires splitting tcp_send_segment's locked seq-advance from its unlocked build-and-transmit (an ~8-caller refactor). That is why the full per-PCB lock is a dedicated careful iteration with a TCP self-test, not a one-turn change; shipping a naive lock-across-transmit would have introduced an IRQ-latency/deadlock hazard not catchable at boot (no TCP traffic). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F19 FIXED + backlog refill (5-agent fan-out): sys_select unvalidated user fd_set read (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). Ran a fresh 5-subagent fan-out over still-un-audited subsystems (storage/bcache, security policy, net udp/icmp/arp/virtio, io_uring/futex/poll-select, fb/drm/virtio-gpu); all five returned HIGH-confidence clean deterministically-testable findings. Fixed the highest reachability x severity x cleanliness one: sys_select read its three input fd_set pointers by RAW DEREF (`((fd_set_t*)rset_ptr)->bits[i]`) with no _access_ok/copy_from_user, even though the same function's timeout read used copy_from_user and its writeback used copy_to_user -- a drifted, unhardened input path. A kernel pointer passed as readfds = arbitrary kernel read (the chosen bits surface in the returned output sets, a usermode-observable read primitive); a non-canonical/unmapped pointer = kernel-fault DoS. Reachable from ANY unprivileged select() call, no opt-in -- the direct input twin of sys_poll's already-hardened path (F4/F9 class). Fixed by routing each non-NULL fd_set through copy_from_user (-EFAULT on failure), memset-zero for NULL sets (the legitimate "empty set" case), and explicit zero of the rout/wout/eout output sets; also fixed the timeout copy_from_user whose return was IGNORED (a bad tv_ptr previously computed timeout_ns from uninitialized stack). Extended copy_user_selftest with a forward decl of sys_select + an assertion that sys_select(1, bad_ptr, 0,0,0) returns -EFAULT for the kernel/non-canonical/past-ceiling bad pointers (skipping NULL, which is a valid empty readfds) -> "[copyuser_test] SELF-TEST PASSED (... + sys_select)". 21 selftests PASS, 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd; qemu healthy. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. RECORDED the other 4 fan-out findings in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md (THIRD AUDIT PASS) as the refreshed backlog, all HIGH-confidence + deterministically-testable: (1) ext2 s_block_size unbounded from on-disk superblock (ext2.c:767) -> >4096 overruns the 4096 bcache slots + DMA scratch; one-line clamp. (2) unveil sandbox bypass: /dev|/proc exemption is a textual prefix with no boundary, so a real file named /devsecrets escapes unveil (syscall.c:411); fix = use the existing boundary-correct virtfs_is_virtual (DRY). (3) virtio-net rx desc_id OOB: device-controlled used-ring id indexes s_rx_bufs[256]/s_rxq.desc[256] unchecked -> OOB read+write (virtio_net.c:417); pure virtio_desc_id_valid guard. (4) DRM create_dumb pitch=width*4 32-bit overflow -> undersized backing buffer (drm.c:486); pure drm_dumb_size 64-bit helper + dim cap. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F20 FIXED: unveil sandbox bypass via /dev|/proc bare-prefix exemption (kernel/syscall/syscall.c sys_open, + test in kernel/fs/virtfs.c, kernel/main.c). The unveil enforcement block in sys_open's got_file: path exempted virtual mounts with two hand-rolled prefix tests -- `!(path[1]=='d'&&path[2]=='e'&&path[3]=='v')` and `!(path[1]=='p'&&path[2]=='r'&&path[3]=='o'&&path[4]=='c')` -- with NO path-boundary check. So a process inside an unveil sandbox (unveil.count>0) opening a REAL on-disk file whose name merely begins with /dev or /proc -- e.g. /devsecrets, /processData, /device_keys -- matched the exemption and skipped unveil_check entirely, opening the file despite the sandbox (sandbox escape / confinement bypass). unveil_check itself was correct (unveil.c has the proper boundary match); the inline exemption was a drifted duplicate of "is this path a virtual mount?". Root-cause fix (DRY + security, single source of truth): replaced both hand-rolled tests with the existing boundary-correct virtfs_is_virtual(path), which goes through find_mount and requires the char after the prefix to be '/' or '\0' (virtfs.h already included in syscall.c). The mount table is exactly {/proc, /dev}, so the exemption SET is unchanged -- only the boundary bug is removed. Deterministic virtfs_is_virtual_selftest (added to virtfs.c, wired in main.c): asserts /dev, /dev/, /dev/tty, /proc, /proc/self/status are virtual (exempt) while /devsecrets, /processData, /device_keys, /home/user, / are NOT virtual (subject to unveil) -> PASSED. 22 selftests PASS (was 21), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd -- the unveil block runs on EVERY open so a clean boot to userland confirms no regression to normal opens. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (1) of the THIRD AUDIT PASS fan-out; remaining open backlog: ext2 s_block_size clamp (ext2.c:767), virtio-net rx desc_id OOB (virtio_net.c:417), DRM create_dumb pitch overflow (drm.c:486), and the T4 TCP per-PCB lock. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F21 FIXED: ext2 block size unbounded from untrusted superblock (kernel/fs/ext2.c, kernel/main.c). ext2_init computed `s_block_size = 1024u << sb->s_log_block_size` directly from the on-disk superblock (read via ahci_read, only magic-gated) with NO bounds check, while every block buffer in the FS is FIXED at 4096 bytes: the bcache slots `s_bcache_data[NSETS][WAYS][4096]` and all EXT2_SCRATCH allocations (kmalloc(4096)). A crafted/corrupt ext2 image with s_log_block_size>=3 yields block size>=8192, and on the very first metadata read bcache_get does `ahci_read(lba, scratch /* kmalloc(4096) */, s_sectors_per_blk /* 16 = 8192 bytes */)` -> AHCI DMA overruns the 4096 heap scratch, then bcache_fill -> bcache_fill_way does `memcpy(s_bcache_data[set][way] /* 4096 */, data, s_block_size /* 8192 */)` -> 4096 BSS slot overflow with attacker-controlled bytes; s_log_block_size>=32 is also a shift past the 32-bit operand width (UB). Reachable at mount (the boot disk is trusted, but any future removable/secondary ext2 volume hits the same path). The code comment at the s_block_size decl already documented the unenforced "1024, 2048, or 4096" invariant. Root-cause fix: a pure validated helper ext2_block_size_checked(log) = (log>2 ? 0 : 1024u<<log) as the single derivation+validation point, used at mount where s_block_size==0 now refuses the mount (return 0) before any block read. Also introduced the named constant EXT2_BLOCK_SIZE_MAX=4096 as the SINGLE SOURCE OF TRUTH wiring together the three fixed-4096 buffers (the bcache slot third dimension + the 3 EXT2_SCRATCH_ALLOC kmalloc sizes) and the helper's bound, so the validation is provably tied to the actual buffer size (DRY). Deterministic ext2_block_size_selftest: log 0/1/2 -> 1024/2048/4096 (each asserted <= EXT2_BLOCK_SIZE_MAX), log 3/10/31/32 -> 0 (rejected) -> PASSED. 23 selftests PASS (was 22), 0 FAILED/PANIC; the boot ext2 mount runs BEFORE /bin/login and login fork-exec'd, so a clean boot proves the clamp accepts the real disk's block size (no regression to the mount path). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (2) of the THIRD AUDIT PASS fan-out; remaining open: virtio-net rx desc_id OOB (virtio_net.c:417), DRM create_dumb pitch overflow (drm.c:486), and the T4 TCP per-PCB lock. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F22 FIXED: virtio-net device-controlled descriptor-id OOB (kernel/net/virtio_net.c, kernel/main.c). virtio_net_rx_poll read desc_id = s_rxq.used->ring[slot].id (uint32, written by the DEVICE) and used it to index s_rx_bufs[VIRTQ_SIZE=256] (line 417: raw = s_rx_bufs[desc_id].virt -> OOB read of a buffer pointer, then memcpy from it) and s_rxq.desc[desc_id] (lines 434-437: OOB WRITE of addr/len/flags/next), with NO bounds check -- even though the adjacent pkt_len was already clamped with an explicit "untrusted device" comment, confirming the missing desc_id check was an oversight. The TX completion path (line 395) had the same pattern: virtq_free_desc(&s_txq, used->ring[].id) with virtq_free_desc doing an unchecked `vq->desc[idx].next = vq->free_head; vq->free_head = idx;` -> a device id>=256 OOB-writes the 4096-byte desc page AND corrupts the free list (free_head = bad idx -> next alloc returns OOB). desc_id>=256 comes from a malicious/buggy device (the virtio spec mandates treating the used ring as untrusted; relevant for a malicious hypervisor, passthrough, or future real NIC). Fixed with one pure helper virtio_desc_id_valid(id) = id < VIRTQ_SIZE: (1) rx-poll advances last_used_idx FIRST (so a bad entry can't wedge the ring) then `if (!virtio_desc_id_valid(desc_id)) return 0;` -- drops the bogus completion without indexing the tables or re-posting; (2) TX frees the device-reported id only if valid, else falls back to `idx` (the single descriptor we actually submitted), so no device trust AND no descriptor leak; (3) virtq_free_desc itself now `if (!virtio_desc_id_valid(idx)) return;` as defense-in-depth at the OOB-write primitive (its only caller is the TX free, alloc always returns a valid chain index, so this never fires in practice). Deterministic virtio_desc_id_valid_selftest: 0 and VIRTQ_SIZE-1 (255) valid; VIRTQ_SIZE (256), 1000, 0xFFFFFFFF invalid -> PASSED. 24 selftests PASS (was 23), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd; net_rx_thread polls rx continuously and DHCP/virtio activity is present in the boot log, so legitimate rx still works (the guard only drops ids a well-behaved device never sends) -- no regression. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (3) of the THIRD AUDIT PASS fan-out; remaining open: DRM create_dumb pitch overflow (drm.c:486) and the T4 TCP per-PCB lock. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F23 FIXED: DRM create_dumb pitch/size 32-bit integer overflow (kernel/drivers/video/drm.c, kernel/main.c). drm_ioctl_create_dumb computed `uint32_t pitch = a.width * 4` -- a 32-bit multiply that overflows BEFORE the `(uint64_t)` cast on the following line. a.width/height/bpp come straight from copy_from_user with the only gate being width/height nonzero + bpp==32 (the advertised GETRESOURCES max_width=8192 is never enforced at create time). Attack: width=0x40000000, height=1, bpp=32 -> pitch = 0x100000000 truncates to 0 -> size=0 -> pages=0 -> order=0 -> bytes_alloc=4096 (one page, quota never trips); but resource_create(res_id, ..., a.width /* 0x40000000 */, a.height) is told the FULL ~4 GiB-wide resource and resource_attach_backing attaches a single page -- so when the dumb is wrapped by ADDFB2 and committed (SETCRTC/PAGE_FLIP -> resource_transfer/flush), the host reads width*height*4 bytes from a 4096-byte backing -> host-side OOB read; in-kernel it is a coherent under-allocation breaking the size invariant every later consumer trusts (d->size, drm_resolve_dumb_mmap's len>bytes_alloc check). width=0x40000001 is nastier (pitch=4, a 4-byte row for a billion-pixel-wide resource). Reachable by any process that opens /dev/dri/card0 (wlroots/dwl compositors). Root-cause fix: a pure helper drm_dumb_size(w,h,bpp,*pitch,*size) doing ALL multiplies in 64-bit and rejecting bpp!=32, zero w/h, and w/h > DRM_MAX_FB_DIM (new constant = 16384, chosen above the advertised 8192 so a well-behaved compositor never trips it; keeps pitch = w*4 <= 65536 within u32 and size within u64, so the (uint32_t)pitch cast is provably non-truncating); replaced the inline pitch/size computation and the now-redundant nonzero/bpp guards with a single call returning -EINVAL on any overflow/oversize. The cursor ioctl already did the analogous (uint64_t)a.width*a.height*4 check correctly, confirming create_dumb was the outlier. Deterministic drm_dumb_size_selftest: 1920x1080 -> pitch 7680, size 8294400; 1x1 -> 4,4; DRM_MAX_FB_DIM^2 -> 65536, 2^30; 0x40000000/0x40000001 -> -EINVAL (the exact 32-bit overflow rows); zero width, zero height, bpp 24, and DRM_MAX_FB_DIM+1 -> -EINVAL -> PASSED. 25 selftests PASS (was 24), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd and the compositor create_dumb path (valid 1920x1080-class requests) still works -> no regression. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (4) -- the LAST item of the THIRD AUDIT PASS fan-out, which is now EXHAUSTED. Remaining open: the T4 TCP per-PCB lock (hardest). Next pass should run a FRESH multi-agent fan-out over un-audited subsystems (futex, mmap/mprotect, pipe, fork/clone fd-table, ptrace, time/clock, AHCI queue depth, ELF interp/auxv, signal frame setup, slab/buddy edges). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F24 FIXED + backlog refill (FOURTH AUDIT PASS, 5-agent fan-out): sys_mmap/sys_munmap unbounded MAP_FIXED -> live kernel-frame free / LPE (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/main.c). Ran a fresh 5-subagent fan-out (futex/robust-list, mmap/VMA, pipe/fd-table, signal/sigreturn, storage-queue/allocator); signal/sigreturn was audited and found CORRECTLY HARDENED (sigreturn validates RIP/RSP<2^47, forces user CS/SS via hardcoded iretq immediates, sanitizes RFLAGS to (x&0xCD5)|0x202 + MXCSR; auxv/stack fully bounded) -- no fix. Fixed the highest reachability x severity finding: sys_mmap/sys_munmap page-rounded a user-controlled len with `(len+PAGE_MASK)&~PAGE_MASK` (wraps to 0 for huge len) and NEVER bounded [addr,addr+len) to the user half -- MAP_FIXED only checked nonzero+page-aligned, munmap likewise. Every process shares the kernel's higher half (PML4[256..511] shallow-copied from the kernel PML4, vmm.c:198), so a MAP_FIXED or munmap at a kernel/HHDM address (e.g. 0xFFFF800000000000) drove mm_unmap_range_flush_free -> vmm_page_unmap -> pmm_ref_dec on a LIVE kernel frame -> returns a still-mapped kernel page to the buddy allocator = kernel memory corruption / privilege escalation, reachable from ANY unprivileged process (pledge only gates PROT_EXEC for mmap; nothing bounds the address). Fixed with two pure overflow-safe helpers that reuse the existing _access_ok predicate (single source of truth): mmap_round_len(len) page-rounds with an overflow guard (returns 0 on zero/overflow), and mmap_range_ok(addr,len,*olen,*oend) requires a page-aligned addr and validates [addr,addr+len) strictly in the user half via _access_ok (rejects NULL/kernel/non-canonical/wrap/end-past-ceiling), returning the rounded len + exclusive end. sys_mmap MAP_FIXED and sys_munmap now reject an out-of-range request with -EINVAL before any unmap/free; a non-fixed addr HINT that fails validation falls back to kernel-chosen placement (mm_vma_find_free -- correct POSIX, and a kernel-half hint can no longer become a user VMA). Deterministic mmap_range_selftest: mmap_round_len rejects 0/UINT64_MAX/just-overflowing and rounds 1->PAGE_SIZE, PAGE_SIZE+1->2 pages; mmap_range_ok rejects NULL, the kernel higher half (the LPE), the first non-canonical page, a non-canonical scribble, a len that overflows page-round, an end spilling past USER_ADDR_MAX, and a misaligned addr, while accepting a legal 1GiB-region range with the right rounded len + exclusive end -> PASSED. This finding was found AND drafted by the fan-out subagent (it had Edit access); I did NOT rubber-stamp it -- independently verified: _access_ok's definition rejects NULL/>USER_ADDR_MAX(=0x00007FFFFFFFFFFF)/overflow/end-past-ceiling; the shared-higher-half claim (vmm.c:198 "every process automatically shares the kernel's higher-half") and the unmap->pmm_ref_dec chain (vmm.c:350/378) confirmed; no sys_mremap exists; reviewed the full 137-line diff for correctness; ran the full SELFTESTS build + boot (the subagent had only compiled the TU). 26 selftests PASS (was 25), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd and qemu ran healthy through userland -- mmap/munmap are on every process's hot path (heap, allocations, fork), so a clean boot proves the stricter validation did not regress legitimate mappings. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. RECORDED the other 3 fan-out findings in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md (FOURTH AUDIT PASS) as the refreshed backlog, all HIGH/MED-HIGH + deterministically-testable: futex_wait raw user deref under the bucket spinlock (futex.c:77 -> fault-under-spinlock + lock-nest from a concurrent munmap; fix = fault-safe compare outside the lock), pipe double-free/UAF on concurrent last-close (pipe.c:127/138 -> non-atomic decrement-and-free of the shared pipe_buf_t, same class as F14/F15; fix = atomic last-ref like vfs_close), and NVMe completion CID OOB (nvme.c:484 -> device-echoed cqe.cid indexes req[64] unchecked, exact F22 class for NVMe; fix = nvme_cid_valid guard). main untouched. mmprotect-on-kernel-range noted as a possible separate lower-severity follow-up (perm change, not a frame free).
- 2026-06-25 - F25 FIXED: pipe double-free + two peer-file UAFs on close (kernel/fs/pipe.c + .h, kernel/main.c). The pipe read end and write end are two distinct vfs_file_t (r, w) sharing one heap pipe_buf_t* p; each end's ->close hook (pipe_read_close/pipe_write_close) fires exactly once (on its vfs_file_t refcount 1->0, after dup/fork sharing resolves). The hooks freed p with a NON-ATOMIC, unlocked `if (reader_refs==0 && writer_refs==0) kfree(p)` and freed their own file with kfree(self). THREE memory-safety bugs, all from the ends being torn down independently instead of sharing the buffer's lifetime: (1) DOUBLE FREE -- a simultaneous last-close of both ends on two CPUs: A sets reader_refs=0, B sets writer_refs=0, both then read both-refs==0 and both kfree(p); (2) wake-vs-free UAF -- pipe_read_close wakes p->write_file->waitq (the peer file) which pipe_write_close frees via kfree(self), so the wake can deref a freed peer vfs_file_t; (3) read/write-vs-close UAF -- pipe_read derefs p->write_file (and pipe_write p->read_file) while its OWN end stays open, but the peer end closed and kfree(self)'d its file, so the live end derefs a freed peer file. Same CLASS as the F14/F15 AF_UNIX file<->object lifetime bug, missed in pipes. Root-cause fix: tie p and BOTH end files to a single lifetime (the F14 invariant "the file lives as long as the shared object"). Added `uint32_t open_ends` to pipe_buf_t (init 2 in pipe_create = both ends open), a PURE helper `pipe_last_end_release(uint32_t*) = __atomic_sub_fetch(open_ends,1,__ATOMIC_ACQ_REL)==0` (returns 1 only for the close that drives it to 0), and `pipe_destroy(p)` that frees read_file + write_file + p together. Both close hooks now: decrement their reader/writer_refs (EOF/EPIPE signal to the peer, unchanged), wake the peer's waitq (peer file guaranteed alive -- not freed until pipe_destroy), then `if (pipe_last_end_release(&p->open_ends)) pipe_destroy(p);` -- removed the bare kfree(p)/kfree(self). Exactly one closer (the last) frees, so no double free; both files live until the last close, so the peer-wake (bugs 2) and the live-end peer-file deref (bug 3) are safe. The __ATOMIC_ACQ_REL makes every prior hook's peer-wake happen-before the last closer's free (the release on the earlier decrement synchronizes-with the acquire on the final decrement), so the free can never race a concurrent wake_all of a peer waitq. Deterministic pipe_refcount_selftest: from open_ends=2, two pipe_last_end_release calls -> first returns 0 (2->1, not last), second returns 1 (1->0, last), and exactly one of the two returns "last" (r1+r2==1) -> exactly one free -> PASSED. 27 selftests PASS (was 26), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd and qemu ran healthy through userland; pipes are exercised by shell pipelines + swaybar's status_command pipe, so a clean boot confirms no regression to pipe create/read/write/close. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (1) of the FOURTH AUDIT PASS fan-out; remaining open: futex_wait raw-deref-under-spinlock (futex.c:77) and NVMe completion CID OOB (nvme.c:484), plus the T4 TCP per-PCB lock. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F26 FIXED: NVMe completion-id OOB (kernel/drivers/storage/nvme.c, kernel/main.c). nvme_irq_handler copied a CQE from the device-DMA'd completion queue and used `cqe.cid` (uint16, echoed by the device) to index q->req[NVME_IOQ_DEPTH=64] with NO bounds check: `nvme_request_t* req = &q->req[cqe.cid]; req->status = ...; __atomic_store_n(&req->done,1,...); wait_queue_wake_all(&req->wq);`. A buggy/malicious controller (or CQ-page DMA corruption) reporting cid >= 64 makes req point past the 64-entry req[] into the adjacent CPU's nvme_ioq_t or far past s_ioq into arbitrary kernel BSS -> a controlled-offset OOB write of status/done AND a wait_queue_wake_all that walks/writes a wake-list through a fabricated wait_queue_t (garbage atomic head + node pointers). The SUBMIT side is safe: cid_pop draws cids from the 64-bit cid_free_bitmap (__builtin_ctzll), always 0..63; only the device-echoed COMPLETION cid was trusted -- the exact F22 (virtio desc_id) device-echo-index class, unguarded for NVMe. AHCI is unaffected (it derives slots via ctz of the 32-bit SACT/CI hardware mask into a 32-entry array, inherently in range). Fixed with the verbatim F22 pattern: pure helper nvme_cid_valid(cid)=cid<NVME_IOQ_DEPTH, placed next to cid_pop/cid_push, and `if (!nvme_cid_valid(cqe.cid)) continue;` in nvme_irq_handler AFTER the CQE is consumed (cq_head/cq_phase already advanced) and BEFORE indexing req[] -- so the corrupt completion is dropped but the cq doorbell update at the end of the loop still credits it (the ring can't wedge). Deterministic nvme_cid_valid_selftest: cid 0 and NVME_IOQ_DEPTH-1 (63) valid; NVME_IOQ_DEPTH (64), 1000, 0xFFFF invalid -> PASSED. 28 selftests PASS (was 27), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd; qemu healthy. The boot disk is AHCI (the bootclean.sh QEMU config has no NVMe device) so the NVMe completion path is not live-exercised, but the pure helper is unit-tested and the guard is a minimal `continue` that does not alter the valid (cid<64) path -- so clean build + clean boot confirm no regression. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (1) of the FOURTH AUDIT PASS fan-out; remaining open: futex_wait raw-deref-under-spinlock (futex.c:77), plus the T4 TCP per-PCB lock. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F27 FIXED: futex_wait raw user deref under the bucket spinlock (kernel/proc/futex.c). futex_wait did its authoritative post-enqueue compare with a RAW deref `cur = *(volatile uint32_t*)uaddr;` while HOLDING the bucket spinlock b->lock (the lost-wake fence: enqueue then re-read). The file comment claimed "once present it stays mapped (no swap), so the locked re-read cannot fault" -- FALSE: no swap does not mean no munmap. A second thread of the same process can munmap or mprotect(PROT_NONE) that page on another CPU (unserialized against the futex bucket) between the prefault and the locked re-read, faulting line 77 while b->lock is held -> isr14_page_fault takes mm->vma_lock and may pmm_buddy_alloc/sleep with a raw spinlock held (fault-under-spinlock + lock-nest -> panic/DoS), attacker-controlled and reachable via every pthread mutex. Root-cause fix: restructured futex_wait so the authoritative re-read is fault-safe AND outside the lock. New flow: copy_from_user fast-reject of a bad pointer + early `cur != val -> -EAGAIN` (no enqueue); then spin_lock; enqueue w; spin_unlock; then `copy_from_user(&cur2, uaddr, 4)` OUTSIDE the lock; if fault or cur2 != val, re-take b->lock and either consume the wake (w.woken -> return 0) or unlink w + return -EFAULT/-EAGAIN; else fall through to the existing sleep loop. The lost-wake fence is PRESERVED, and I verified the precise reason: it is the spin_lock ACQUIRE barrier (not the enqueue store) that orders the re-read after any waker's prior bucket-unlock -- an acquire prevents later ops (the re-read) from moving before it, so the re-read stays after our lock-acquire, which is after any waker CS that preceded our enqueue CS; thus a waker that wrote the new value before its (earlier) CS is observed by our re-read, and a waker whose CS is after our enqueue sees us in the list and sets w.woken. So moving the read out of the CS (but keeping it after the acquire) is sound. copy_from_user (-> user_buf_prefault) walks VMAs under rcu_read_lock and returns -EFAULT for an unmapped page (no VMA), takes no lock that nests with b->lock, and is now called with b->lock dropped -- so the fault-under-spinlock + lock-nest is gone. Verification: this is a tiny-window cross-CPU race (F2/F3/F5/F11 class) so no bespoke deterministic test; code-proof (grep confirms no raw user deref remains under any spin_lock in futex.c; the locked regions do only list ops) + the copy_from_user safety is already covered by copy_user_selftest (it asserts copy_from_user returns -EFAULT for kernel/non-canonical/ceiling/NULL pointers) + clean boot: 28 selftests PASS (unchanged -- no new test), 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd, qemu ran healthy (status running) through ~18s of userland with no panic/fault/hang (a futex lock-discipline bug would deadlock the desktop's pthread/GLib mutexes, which this very file exists to back). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (2) of the FOURTH AUDIT PASS fan-out, which is now EXHAUSTED. Remaining open: the T4 TCP per-PCB lock (hardest). Next pass should run a FRESH multi-agent fan-out (epoll/eventpoll, tty/termios, VFS path-resolution/symlink loop, fork/clone+wait/zombie reaping, mount/umount, io_uring SQ/CQ ring index math, the capabilities/setuid-exec gap noted in the second audit pass). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F28 FIXED + backlog refill (FIFTH AUDIT PASS, 2-agent fan-out): epoll watched-file use-after-free on close-before-epoll-close (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/main.c). epoll_ctl(ADD) registered persistent epoll_we_t entries on the watched fd's waitq (f->waitq, f->secondary_waitq) and saved raw wq1/wq2 pointers into the epoll_watch_t, but took NO reference on the watched vfs_file_t. The authors KNEW about close-before-epoll-close (comment) and "saved the waitq pointers so unregister works after the file is freed" -- but that only holds for LONG-LIVED GLOBAL queues (g_mouse_waitq); for every fd whose waitq is EMBEDDED in the freed object (pipe f->_waitq, eventfd s->read_wq/write_wq, unix sock f->_waitq, pty master_waitq), close(watched_fd) freed that memory, so wq1/wq2 dangled and the later epoll_ctl(DEL/MOD) or epoll_close -> epoll_watch_unregister -> epoll_we_remove(wq1, &w->entry) walked freed memory (read wq->head / took wq->remove_lock / walked the chain) = UAF. Reachable from pure unprivileged userland with NO race (deterministic ordering: epoll_ctl ADD a pipe/eventfd/socketpair, close() it, close(epfd)) -- the ordinary wlroots/libinput event-source teardown order. Same file<->object lifetime class as F14/F15 (AF_UNIX) and F25 (pipe), missed in epoll. Root-cause fix (Linux eventpoll model): epoll_watch_register now vfs_tryget()s the watched file into a new epoll_watch_t.file field, pinning the file (and its embedded waitq) for the watch's lifetime; epoll_watch_unregister vfs_close()s it AFTER epoll_we_remove unlinks our entries (so the file -- and its waitq -- is freed only once our entries are gone, never under us). vfs_tryget (CAS-from-nonzero) safely handles a file concurrently being closed (returns NULL -> register nothing, inert watch). unregister no longer needs a fresh fd lookup (it uses w->file/wq1/wq2), so DEL/epoll_close/MOD dropped the stale-fd-lookup argument (and epoll_close dropped its now-unused `files`); MOD re-pins on re-register. epoll_watch_free_rcu (kfree) is unchanged and never touches w->file (the pin is already dropped in unregister before the call_rcu, so no double free). Deterministic epoll_watch_refcount_selftest (in syscall.c, gated by MAKAOS_BOOT_SELFTESTS, wired in main.c): builds a heap vfs_file_t with an embedded waitq + refcount 1 (the UAF-prone shape) + a minimal epoll_state_t + epoll_watch_t; epoll_watch_register pins it -> asserts refcount==2 and w.file==f; vfs_close(f) (the user closing the watched fd) -> asserts refcount==1 (SURVIVES via the pin; pre-fix this freed f and left wq1 dangling); epoll_watch_unregister -> unlinks then drops the pin -> f freed exactly once -> PASSED. This was found by the fan-out subagent (READ-ONLY this round, so no subagent edits to review); independently verified the register/unregister/ADD/DEL/MOD/epoll_close flow, that vfs_tryget exists and CAS-bumps from nonzero, that epoll_we_remove operates on the saved waitq, that free_rcu does not touch w->file, and ran the full SELFTESTS build + clean boot. 29 selftests PASS (was 28), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd; qemu ran healthy through userland (the desktop's wlroots/libinput epoll event loops add+close fds, so a clean boot confirms no regression to register/unregister/close). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. RECORDED the other fan-out finding in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md (FIFTH AUDIT PASS): the TTY canonical-ring framing bug (read_buf capacity off-by-one drops a max line's terminating '\n' -> line-framing corruption; not memory-unsafe) + the unlocked tty_flush_input-vs-producer race (needs a per-tty ldisc lock) -- lower priority, careful (race fix needs a lock). main untouched. NOTE: only 2 of the intended 5 fan-out agents were launched this round (epoll + tty); the other suggested areas (VFS path-resolution/symlink loop, fork/wait/zombie reaping, io_uring rings, setuid-exec gap) remain un-fanned-out for a future pass.
- 2026-06-25 - F29 FIXED: TTY canonical line-framing drop (kernel/drivers/tty/tty.c + .h, kernel/main.c). The cooked read_buf ring had usable capacity TTY_READ_BUF_SIZE-1 = 4095, exactly equal to the maximum cooked line (TTY_LINE_BUF_SIZE-1 = 4095: up to 4094 data bytes + the '\n' appended at completion). ldisc_flush_line pushed the line byte-by-byte via rd_push, which silently drops on a full ring. So whenever the read_buf already held even one un-drained byte (reader behind), a completed line whose length exceeded the remaining free space had its TAIL dropped -- including the terminating '\n' -- and the canonical reader (which stops only at '\n', tty_vfs_read / pty slave) then merged this line with the next one or blocked forever waiting for a '\n' that was discarded. Line framing corruption, reachable from the console (keyboard) and any pty_master_write under a slow/blocked reader. NOT memory-unsafe (line_len is bounded to <= TTY_LINE_BUF_SIZE-1 by the < TTY_LINE_BUF_SIZE-1 guards on every line_buf[line_len++], so no over-read of line_buf). Root-cause fix, three parts: (1) bumped TTY_READ_BUF_SIZE 4096 -> 8192 (still a power of 2; usable 8191) so the read ring is STRICTLY larger than a max line and a full line fits even with up to ~4KB of reader backlog; (2) added a pure rb_free(head,tail,size) = (head-tail-1)&(size-1) helper (free slots in the ring); (3) made ldisc_flush_line ALL-OR-NOTHING: `if (rb_free(rd_head,rd_tail,TTY_READ_BUF_SIZE) >= line_len) { push the whole line } ` else drop the WHOLE line -- so a partial flush can never strand a '\n'-less line; dropping a whole line when the input queue is full is POSIX-acceptable input loss, framing-correct. EOF semantics preserved: ^D on an empty line has line_len==0 and rb_free>=0 is always true, so the empty flush still runs (pushes nothing) and wakes the reader for a 0-byte EOF read. Deterministic tty_rb_free_selftest (in tty.c, wired in main.c): rb_free on a size-8 ring -- empty->7, 1-used->6, full(0,7)->0, offset-empty(3,3)->7, (5,2)->2, (2,5)->4 -- plus the invariant rb_free(0,0,TTY_READ_BUF_SIZE) >= TTY_LINE_BUF_SIZE-1 (an empty read ring holds a whole max line) -> PASSED. 30 selftests PASS (was 29), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd (login reads the console via the ldisc, so the read path rd_push/rd_pop/ldisc_flush_line + the read_buf size bump are exercised) -> no regression; qemu healthy. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was finding (a) of the FIFTH AUDIT PASS TTY entry; STILL OPEN (recorded as part b): the unlocked tty_flush_input-vs-producer race (ioctl TCFLSH/TCSETSF resets rd_head/rd_tail/line_len with no lock vs concurrent rd_push/line_buf accumulation; dup-shared pty slave fds make multi-consumer real) -- needs a per-tty ldisc spinlock, a careful dedicated iteration. Also still un-fanned-out: VFS path-resolution/symlink loop, fork/wait/zombie reaping, io_uring SQ/CQ ring index math, the setuid-exec escalation gap. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F30 FIXED: ext2 path_split kernel stack buffer overflow (kernel/fs/ext2.c, kernel/main.c). path_split(path, parent_out) split a path into its parent dir + basename by copying the parent portion into the caller-supplied parent_out buffer with `for (int i=0; i<last_slash; i++) parent_out[i] = path[i];` and NO bound against the buffer size. All 6 call sites passed a fixed `char[256]` STACK buffer (ext2_write_file, ext2_create, ext2_mkdir, ext2_unlink, ext2_rename x2). sys_open copies the user-supplied path into `char path[512]` (up to 511 chars, no PATH_MAX gate) and, on O_CREAT of a nonexistent file, calls ext2_create(path) -> path_split(path, parent_path[256]). So an unprivileged `open("/<~480-char component>/x", O_CREAT, 0644)` makes last_slash ~= 480 and the loop writes ~480 bytes into the 256-byte stack buffer -- ~224 bytes past it, smashing ext2_create's saved return address: a classic RCE-class kernel stack overflow reachable from the most basic syscall. (The codebase already does the same split correctly elsewhere with a 512-byte buffer + bounded memcpy at syscall.c:420, so the 256 in ext2 is a genuine size mismatch, not intentional.) Root-cause fix: added a `cap` (destination size) parameter to path_split and a bound -- `if ((uint32_t)last_slash >= cap) return NULL;` before the copy (we write parent_out[0..last_slash-1] + a NUL at [last_slash], so last_slash < cap is required); every one of the 6 callers ALREADY checks `if (!basename ...) return <error>` (verified), so a NULL return is handled gracefully (the over-long path is rejected with an error instead of overflowing). Also bumped all 6 parent buffers from [256] to [EXT2_PATH_MAX]=512 (a new named constant matching sys_open's path[512]) so a path sys_open accepts is never spuriously rejected, and pass sizeof(buf) as cap at each site -- the buffer declaration is the single source of truth for the bound, and path_split is now safe for ANY input regardless of buffer size (defense in depth: even a >512 path can't overflow). Deterministic ext2_path_split_selftest (in ext2.c, gated by MAKAOS_BOOT_SELFTESTS, wired in main.c): normal split "/foo/bar"->("/foo","bar"); root parent "/a"->("/","a"); exact-fit boundary "/abcdefg/x" with cap 9 accepts (parent "/abcdefg" = 8 chars + NUL = 9 bytes) while cap 8 REJECTS (last_slash 8 >= 8 -> NULL, no copy); and a 20+ char parent with cap 8 rejects (the overflow case) -> PASSED. This was found by a read-only fan-out subagent (no edits to review); independently verified all 6 caller buffer sizes + their NULL-return handling + the sys_open 512-byte path reaching ext2_create with no length gate + ran the full SELFTESTS build and boot. 31 selftests PASS (was 30), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd (boot exercises ext2 path resolution / ext2_open during login) -> no regression for normal paths; qemu healthy. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. RECORDED the other fan-out finding in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md (SIXTH AUDIT PASS): io_uring indexes sqes[]/cqes[] with the ring_mask read from the USER-WRITABLE ring header (sq_hdr/cq_hdr->ring_mask, mapped VMA_R|VMA_W|VMA_USER) instead of the kernel-trusted sq_entries/cq_entries -> a process that overwrites ring_mask=0xFFFFFFFF gets an OOB read of an SQE + an attacker-controlled OOB WRITE of a CQE (CRITICAL); fix = derive masks from sq_entries-1/cq_entries-1 at every subscript (~8 sites). NOTE: 2 of the 4 fan-out agents this round were interrupted (fork/wait/zombie reaping, cred/perm/setuid-exec gap) and will be re-run next pass per the user's request. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F31 FIXED: sys_spawn SPAWN_ATTR_CRED unprivileged root privilege escalation (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/main.c). The SPAWN_ATTR_CRED block applied the child's full credential set (ruid/euid/suid/rgid/egid/sgid) from a.uid/a.gid -- copied VERBATIM from the user-supplied spawn_attr_t (memcpy from attr_ptr) -- with NO caller-privilege check. So ANY unprivileged process could spawn("/bin/x", argv, envp, stdio, {flags=SPAWN_ATTR_CRED, uid=0, gid=0}) and the child ran with euid=ruid=suid=0 = full effective root: vfs_check_perm (perm.c:21) root-bypasses all DAC, and every cred.euid==0 / cred_is_root gate (sys_setgroups, the policy-agent register, framebuffer map, etc.) opens. A trivial local privilege escalation, no preconditions. The asymmetry was telling: SPAWN_ATTR_PLEDGE in the SAME attr block uses tighten-only pledge_restrict(parent, requested) and unveil locks (down-only), but cred was applied raw -- the down-only intent existed for the restriction attrs but cred was never gated. Root-cause fix: added a pure helper spawn_cred_allowed(const cred_t* c, uid, gid) = cred_is_root(c) ? 1 : (uid in {ruid,euid,suid} AND gid in {rgid,egid,sgid} or cred_in_group(c,gid)) -- the SAME down-only rule cred_setuid/cred_setgid enforce, so a privilege change can't be routed through spawn() to bypass the single permission model. Restructured sys_spawn to read the attr ONCE BEFORE creating the child (into a hoisted `spawn_attr_t a` + have_attr flag): (1) single read eliminates the TOCTOU where a user flips a.uid between the check and its application; (2) validating before any child resources are allocated means a denied request (goto bad_cred -> free arg/env copies -> return -EPERM) needs NO child teardown (avoided the uncertain task_destroy-on-unstarted-task path). The application block now applies the already-validated `a` under `if (have_attr)`. A malformed attr pointer is still ignored (have_attr stays 0), matching the prior lenient behaviour for the non-cred attrs.
