Deterministic spawn_cred_allowed_selftest (in syscall.c, gated by MAKAOS_BOOT_SELFTESTS, wired in main.c): non-root caller {1000,..} requesting uid 0 -> DENY, uid0+gid1000 -> DENY, uid1000+gid0 -> DENY, own uid/gid -> ALLOW; a caller with suid==0 (setuid program that dropped euid) -> ALLOW uid 0; supplemental-group membership -> ALLOW that gid; root caller -> ALLOW any -> PASSED. This was found by a read-only fan-out subagent; independently verified sys_spawn has no earlier privilege gate, `a` is user-supplied verbatim, the cred_setuid down-only semantics (cred.h), and that euid==0 is honored as root (perm.c). 32 selftests PASS (was 31), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd -- the boot launches login via the legit uid=0 path (svcmgr uses SPAWN_ATTR_CRED to drop privilege; root is cred_is_root -> allowed), so a clean boot confirms the legitimate root-caller path still works (no regression) and there is no spurious -EPERM/spawn-failure spam. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. Remaining open (docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md): io_uring user-writable ring_mask OOB (CRITICAL, next), init->children plain-store-vs-CAS race, TTY ldisc lock, T4 TCP lock, AND -- per explicit user direction (everything is worth fixing) -- the setuid-on-exec gap (vfs_check_exec computes setuid_uid but both exec callers discard it; implementing it safely = wiring the ksec escalation, a privilege-feature that must be done carefully). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F32 IMPLEMENTED: setuid-on-exec (ksec-mediated, fail-closed) (kernel/security/ksec.c + ksec.h, kernel/syscall/syscall.c sys_exec, kernel/proc/elf.c elf_exec_from_ext2, kernel/main.c). Per explicit user direction ("everything is worth fixing"). The gap was fail-closed (a setuid binary exec'd with euid UNCHANGED -- safe but a missing feature). Two parts fixed. (1) BUG: both exec callers built inode_perm_t with `.mode = i_mode & 0x1FF`, which STRIPS the setuid bit (S_ISUID=04000 is bit 11, above 0x1FF), so vfs_check_exec's `(ip->mode & S_ISUID)` test could never fire and *out_setuid_uid was always 0xFFFFFFFF (detection was dead code). Changed both to `& 0xFFF` (keeps the suid/sgid/sticky bits + the 9 perm bits, drops the file-type bits); VERIFIED SAFE because acl_from_mode (acl.h) only reads (mode>>6)&7/(mode>>3)&7/mode&7 -- the low 9 -- so the high mode bits do not pollute vfs_check_perm. (2) FEATURE: both exec callers discarded setuid_uid; now they apply it via a new ksec round-trip. Implemented ksec_exec_setuid(cred_t* target, setuid_uid, inode, caller_pid/uid/gid) in ksec.c, mirroring sys_setuid's working ksec pattern (ksec_agent_present -> build ksec_request_t{op=KSEC_OP_EXEC_SETUID, caller id, inode} -> ksec_request -> apply iff authorised). FAIL-CLOSED by construction: no agent OR ksec_request failure OR verdict != KSEC_VERDICT_ALLOW -> NO change (euid stays inherited, matching today's behaviour); ONLY an explicit ksec ALLOW raises privilege, and to the euid/egid KSEC GRANTS (ksec is the authority -- the kernel never escalates on its own). The decision is a pure helper ksec_exec_setuid_should_apply(setuid_uid, agent_present, ksec_rc, verdict) (in ksec.h, deterministically unit-tested). Placement (carefully, since this is privilege-escalation code): sys_exec applies to g_current->cred at the POST-COMMIT point (after the address-space swap + old AS freed, line ~978) so a FAILED load can never leave an escalated process -- setuid_uid is hoisted from the early permission-check block and carried there; the requester identity (caller_uid/gid) is captured from the PRE-escalation cred. elf_exec_from_ext2 applies to the new child t->cred AFTER t is built and BEFORE sys_spawn schedules it (the child is not yet running; the spawning g_current does the ksec round-trip / blocks). The ksec single-pending-slot limitation is pre-existing (shared with sys_setuid), not introduced. Deterministic ksec_exec_setuid_selftest: no-setuid-bit -> no apply, no-agent -> no apply (fail closed), ksec_rc!=0 -> no apply, verdict DENY/CHALLENGE -> no apply, and ONLY (setuid+agent+rc0+ALLOW) -> apply -> PASSED. 33 selftests PASS (was 32), 0 FAILED/PANIC; /bin/login fork-exec'd -- the boot execs login/svcmgr/bash through both exec paths with the new full-mode check + (no agent at boot ->) no round-trip, so a clean boot to login confirms normal exec still works, no hang, no spurious escalation. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. The implementation is INERT until a ksec policy daemon is registered AND authorises -- it does not weaken the system today, it wires the feature per the documented design. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F33 FIXED: io_uring user-writable ring_mask OOB read/write (kernel/io/io_uring.c, kernel/main.c). io_uring subscripted the sqes[]/cqes[] arrays with a `mask` read from sq_hdr->ring_mask / cq_hdr->ring_mask -- but those headers live in the ring backing that io_uring_setup maps into the creating task's user address space via vmm_map_physical_user (VMA_R|VMA_W|VMA_USER), so a process can overwrite ring_mask in its own mapping. The adjacent fullness checks correctly used the KERNEL-TRUSTED counts (`(tail-head) >= cq_entries` / sq_entries -- fields in the kernel io_uring_t, set at setup from round_pow2_u32(entries) clamped to IO_URING_MAX_ENTRIES=4096, never user-writable), proving the mask used for the SUBSCRIPT was the wrong (untrusted) source. Attack: a process sets cq_hdr->ring_mask=0xFFFFFFFF, then the kernel's `cqes[tail & mask]` becomes `cqes[tail]` with the kernel-advanced `tail` growing unboundedly (the cq_entries-based fullness check does NOT bound the masked index) -> attacker-controlled OOB WRITE of a 16-byte CQE past the cqes[] allocation; sq side gives an OOB read of an SQE. CRITICAL/active LPE-class. Verified the EXACT attack surface: 3 mask source reads -- io_uring_post_cqe (cq_hdr->ring_mask, feeds cqes[tail&mask] at the overflow-drain + the normal post), the SQPOLL drain (sq_hdr->ring_mask, feeds sqes[head&mask]), and io_uring_enter_impl (sq_hdr->ring_mask, feeds sqes[head&mask] at the inline submit + the linked-chain path AND is passed as the `mask` param to io_wq_enqueue_chain which subscripts sqes[*phead&mask]). Fixed at the root with two trusted-mask helpers io_sq_mask(u)=u->sq_entries-1 / io_cq_mask(u)=u->cq_entries-1 (derived from the kernel-trusted power-of-two counts) used at ALL THREE source reads -- so all six subscripts (the two cq + four sq, including the io_wq_enqueue_chain parameter) now mask with the trusted count and are provably in [0,entries). The kernel NEVER reads sq_hdr/cq_hdr->ring_mask for indexing anymore; the setup-time writes of those header fields are KEPT (they are advisory state the userland liburing reads -- the kernel just must not trust them back). Pure helper io_ring_index(raw, entries)=raw&(entries-1) extracted + deterministic io_uring_index_selftest (raw 0/3/4/0xFFFFFFFF vs entries 4; 0x12345/0xFFFFFFFF vs 256; 0xFFFFFFFF vs 4096; 0xFFFFFFFF vs 1 -- each asserted == expected AND < entries, so a 0xFFFFFFFF counter can no longer escape the ring). 34 selftests PASS (was 33), 0 FAILED/PANIC; CRITICALLY the existing io_uring_test (the NOP pipeline: 32 ops + 100-round steady state) still PASSES -- it submits real SQEs and posts real CQEs through io_uring_enter_impl + io_uring_post_cqe, so a clean PASS confirms the trusted-mask indexing did not break normal ring operation (no site missed, correct masking). /bin/login fork-exec'd; qemu healthy. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. This was the THIRD AUDIT PASS (5-agent fan-out) finding (2). main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F34 FIXED: init->children plain-store data race with cross-CPU CAS prepends (kernel/syscall/syscall.c sys_exit, kernel/proc/signal.c signal_terminate, kernel/proc/sched.c+.h). init->children is a lock-free Treiber stack; its documented invariant (sched.c:879-882) requires EVERY mutation to be an atomic op, because exiting tasks on any CPU CAS-prepend their orphan chains onto init->children to reparent (task_child_add_chain, a CAS loop), and sys_wait XCHG-drains it (task_children_reap). But when init itself exits (init = /bin/login, the first non-kthread sched_add -- it is exitable and fatal-signalable), BOTH exit paths took the `else` branch (g_init_task == g_current, or init absent) and cleared the list with a PLAIN non-atomic store `g_current->children = NULL;`. A plain (relaxed, non-atomic) store concurrent with the ACQ_REL CAS prepends is a C-memory-model DATA RACE (undefined behaviour) -- the compiler may reorder/assume-no-concurrent-access, and the store does not synchronize-with the CAS, so the all-CAS Treiber invariant is violated (a just-reparented orphan chain can be lost -> unreapable task_t + pid leak, and a dangling children pointer can be left in a task about to be RCU-freed). Root-cause fix: hoisted both identical else-branches into ONE shared helper task_children_clear(task_t*) (sched.c, declared in sched.h) that drains atomically with __atomic_exchange_n(&t->children, NULL, __ATOMIC_ACQ_REL) -- the SAME XCHG primitive task_children_reap already uses -- discarding the chain (init dying -> its orphans are unreapable by design either way). Now ALL FOUR mutations of init->children are atomic (task_child_add CAS, task_child_add_chain CAS, task_children_reap XCHG, the init-exit clear XCHG) with consistent ACQ_REL ordering -> the data race is eliminated, the invariant restored. DRY: the two exit paths now call one helper so they cannot drift. Verified task_children_reparent's plain drain (sched.c:1018) is correctly LEFT as-is: it runs only for from != init (the call sites gate on g_init_task != g_current), and its own doc states "only the dying task walks its own children list here, so the drain is a plain load -- no race"; a non-init task's children are never the universal reparent target, so no cross-CPU CAS touches them. Code-proof: grep confirms the only remaining plain `->children =` stores are pre-publication task-creation inits (process.c:194/466, elf.c:580/714, syscall.c:1353 -- single-owner, task not yet visible to other CPUs) plus that documented-safe reparent drain. Tiny-window cross-CPU race (F2/F3/F5/F11/F27 class) so no bespoke deterministic test (the race needs init exiting concurrently with another task reparenting, not reproducible at boot); verified by the code-proof + a clean boot: 34 selftests PASS (unchanged), 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd, qemu healthy through ~15s of userland with no panic/fault -- the exit/reparent path (task_children_reparent, unchanged) is exercised by every process exit (login/svcmgr/shell), confirming no regression. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F35 FIXED: TTY line-discipline unlocked ring/line race (kernel/drivers/tty/tty.c + tty.h, kernel/drivers/tty/pty.c, kernel/main.c). The tty_t read ring (read_buf/rd_head/rd_tail) and canonical accumulation (line_buf/line_len) were mutated from multiple PROCESS-context CPUs with NO lock: the producer (console keyboard THREAD via keyboard_thread_fn->input_emit->tty_on_kbd_event->tty_input_char, OR pty_master_write in a syscall), one or more consumers (tty_vfs_read and pty_slave_read -- dup-shared/refcounted PTY slave fds make TWO concurrent slave readers real), and tty_flush_input (ioctl TCFLSH/TCSETSF + the ^C/^Z/^\ NOFLSH path). Three logical races: (a) two slave readers both pop -> duplicated/lost bytes; (b) tty_flush_input resets rd_head=rd_tail=0 + line_len=0 under a live producer/consumer -> inconsistent head/tail so the ring 'wraps' and delivers stale buffer bytes; (c) line_len reset races canonical accumulation. Characterized HONESTLY: NOT an OOB (rd_head/rd_tail/line_len are naturally-aligned uint32 -> aligned x86 access is atomic, every index is a previously-stored masked value always < bufsize) -- a data-integrity / stale-content race. Per the user's 'half-correct counts as a bug, fix it FULLY' directive, did the COMPLETE ring+line lock, NOT a ring-only decomposition. Contexts verified: the console producer is a kernel THREAD not an IRQ (input_core.c:112; the IRQ1/IRQ12 ISRs only irq_notify), and the pty producer/consumer are syscalls -> NO IRQ-context toucher of the ring -> a PLAIN spinlock under preempt_disable is correct (NO irqsave), matching the established fb.c:195 pattern (spin_lock is bare TAS + the kernel is preemptible, so preempt_disable is required). Root-cause fix: added `spinlock_t lock` to tty_t (tty.h), init'd in tty_init (g_tty0) and pty_alloc (every slave). It is a LEAF lock -- under it ONLY the tty's own ring/line fields are touched; echo (write_char -> fb I/O), wait_queue_wake_all (-> rq_lock), and the blocking WAIT_EVENT sleep ALL stay OUTSIDE it (no lock-ordering inversion, no I/O/sleep under a spinlock). tty_lock/tty_unlock inline helpers = preempt_disable+spin_lock / spin_unlock+preempt_enable. rd_push/rd_pop kept PURE (caller holds the lock). tty_input_char restructured so each branch locks the STATE mutation only and echoes/wakes AFTER unlock: erase/kill/regular/newline accumulate via locked ldisc_line_{append,erase,kill} then echo outside; newline/EOF commit via ldisc_flush_line (locked all-or-nothing commit, then wake_all outside); raw mode echoes then locks just the rd_push then wakes outside; the ISIG path calls tty_flush_input (self-locks) with no lock held. tty_flush_input takes the lock (verified non-recursive: its callers -- the signal path and ioctl -- never hold it). A new exported tty_ldisc_drain(tty,out,len) does the locked cooked-byte drain (canonical '\n' stop / raw VMIN) and is used by BOTH tty_vfs_read AND pty_slave_read -- DRY: removed pty_slave_read's duplicated inline pop, so the ring is never popped lock-free from two places. WAIT_EVENT/poll rb_empty fast-checks stay lockless (read-only hints, re-checked under the lock in the drain). Deadlock-free by construction: one non-recursive leaf lock, tiny critical sections (array copy / index update only), no nesting, the holder can't be preempted (preempt_disable) and never blocks. VERIFICATION (the user explicitly asked 'is it not hanging?'): besides the cross-CPU-race code-proof (grep audit: every rd_head/rd_tail/line_len/line_buf/read_buf MUTATION is under tty->lock; the only lockless accesses are read-only WAIT/poll hints), added a deterministic tty_ldisc_selftest (in tty.c, kmalloc'd test tty so no shipping BSS, wired in main.c) that DRIVES the exact locked path -- tty_input_char (producer) + tty_ldisc_drain (consumer) + tty_flush_input -- and asserts byte-correct output: (A) canonical 'hey\n' flushes intact and drains stopping at '\n'; (B) tty_flush_input discards a pending un-flushed line ('xy' gone, fresh 'z\n' delivered); (C) raw push 'Q' drains with VMIN=1, then tty_flush_input clears the ring (drain -> 0). This proves the lock path is BALANCED and CANNOT HANG: a missing unlock or recursive re-acquire of the non-recursive leaf lock would spin forever on the BSP (preempt disabled) and the boot would freeze at this selftest, never printing PASSED nor reaching login. Result: 35 selftests PASS (was 34 -- the new tty_ldisc test), 0 FAILED/PANIC, [tty_ldisc] SELF-TEST PASSED (locked push/drain/flush, no self-deadlock), /bin/login fork-exec'd and the system ran all 35 selftests to completion concurrently with login reading the console through the new locked tty_ldisc_drain, then shut down cleanly (empty qemu.out, no triple-fault) at ~14s matching the established baseline -- a CLEAN EXIT positively rules out a hang (a deadlock would keep qemu ALIVE indefinitely blocked; a crash would print a fault; neither happened). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F36 FIXED: ext2 unbounded physical block number -> wild device LBA (kernel/fs/ext2.c, kernel/main.c). Found by a fresh 5-agent READ-ONLY fan-out (the other 4 areas came back clean/absent -- see AUDIT_FINDINGS.md SEVENTH AUDIT PASS). ext2 turned block numbers from UNTRUSTED on-disk data -- inode i_block[] direct entries, single/double indirect-block entries, and BGD bg_inode_table -- straight into device LBAs (lba = s_part_lba + blk * s_sectors_per_blk) at every sink (bcache_get:296, write_block:629, the two ext2_vfs_read/pread fast-path run DMAs) with NO upper-bound check. s_blocks_count was read from the superblock at mount but used ONLY to derive s_num_groups (never stored, never compared), and no block_valid() helper existed anywhere. So a crafted or corrupt ext2 image with a wild i_block[]/indirect entry (up to 2^32-1) made the kernel DMA a sector OUTSIDE the filesystem: a cross-partition / off-device READ returned to userland via read() (info disclosure), and an OOB WRITE to an attacker-chosen LBA on inode/bitmap writeback (corruption). Rated CRITICAL by the fan-out subagent; the realistic reach today is a corrupt-FS / future-removable-media threat (MakaOS has no sys_mount, mounts one boot image), but it is exactly the untrusted-on-disk-data -> bounds-check class of F21 (block size clamp) and F30 (path_split), and a wild-LBA DMA must never be issued regardless. Root-cause fix (single chokepoint, DRY): (1) store s_blocks_count at mount; (2) add pure, overflow-safe helpers ext2_block_in_range(blk,first,count) and ext2_run_in_range(start,run,first,count) (the run check rejects run>count and start>count-run so start+run can never wrap uint32), wrapped by ext2_block_valid/ext2_run_valid using the live [s_first_data_blk, s_blocks_count) range; (3) gate EVERY block->LBA sink BEFORE the LBA is computed -- bcache_get returns its existing NULL-data I/O-error ref for an out-of-range blk (so wild indirect/BGD pointers degrade to a sparse/zero-fill or a clean inode-load failure, never a wild read AND never pollute the cache), write_block returns 0 (never writes outside the FS), and both fast-path run DMAs call ext2_run_valid(phys_blk, run) to validate the WHOLE consecutive run before ahci_read (return -1 on a corrupt data-block pointer). Also hardened the same untrusted-superblock trust boundary: reject a degenerate superblock with s_blocks_per_grp/s_inodes_per_grp/s_blocks_count == 0 (the first two were a div-by-zero #DE DoS at the s_num_groups computation and in inode-location math). Deterministic ext2_block_valid_selftest (gated MAKAOS_BOOT_SELFTESTS, wired in main.c) drives the pure helpers with a fixed FS shape (first-data-block 1, 100 blocks): single-block boundary (0 and >=100 and 0xFFFFFFFF rejected, 1/50/99 accepted) and the run check including a uint32 wrap case (start=0xFFFFFF00 run=0x200 rejected) -> PASSED. Independently verified (not rubber-stamping the subagent): confirmed s_blocks_count was never stored/compared, that the superblock is read by a direct ahci_read (line 780) BEFORE bcache_get is ever called (so gating bcache_get against s_blocks_count is safe at all times), that every block->LBA computation site is now gated, and that bcache_get's NULL-ref failure is already handled by all callers. 36 selftests PASS (was 35 -- the new ext2_blkvalid), 0 FAILED/PANIC, [ext2_blkvalid] SELF-TEST PASSED, /bin/login fork-exec'd -- and since ALL of userland (login/svcmgr/bash/sway/fonts) is read from ext2 through the now-gated bcache_get + fast-path sinks, a clean boot to login proves valid in-range blocks are NOT over-rejected (no false positives). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F37 FIXED: fd_install inconsistent failure-ownership -> double-free / fd leak (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). Found by an 8th-pass 5-agent READ-ONLY fan-out (the other 4 areas -- signal sigframe/sigreturn, network RX, fork/wait/zombie, ELF loader -- came back memory-safe; see AUDIT_FINDINGS.md EIGHTH AUDIT PASS, which also records a HIGH unveil-only-in-sys_open sandbox gap for a dedicated turn). The fan-out's SCM_RIGHTS subagent flagged a recvmsg double-close, but independent verification (NOT rubber-stamping) showed the real root cause is broader and is fd_install itself: fd_install(f) closed `f` via vfs_close on its fd_table_grow-failure return (-ENFILE) but NOT on its !g_current return (-EBADF), an INCONSISTENT ownership contract. Since callers can't tell which failure occurred, they guessed: of the 14 call sites, ~10 closed `f` on failure (openpty x2, io_uring_setup/register, eventfd, timerfd, recvmsg SCM_RIGHTS, epoll, socketpair x2) -> DOUBLE-FREE / UAF on the grow path (the agent's recvmsg case is one of these), while 4 (socket, accept x2 unix+inet, recvfd) did NOT close -> would LEAK `f` on the !g_current path. Reachable whenever fd_table_grow fails (fd-table exhaustion / kmalloc OOM during fd-table doubling) on any fd-returning syscall. Root-cause fix per "fix the fragile design, not the symptom" -- made the contract SINGLE and CONSISTENT: fd_install NEVER closes `f`; on ANY negative return ownership stays with the CALLER, which must close `f`. Removed the grow-path vfs_close(f) from fd_install (so the ~10 closers are now exactly-once-correct with no edit), and ADDED the missing close to the 4 non-closers (sys_socket vfs_close(f); sys_accept unix+inet vfs_close(cf); sys_recvfd vfs_close(received)). Documented the contract in fd_install's header comment so future call sites cannot reintroduce either bug class. Also fixed two pre-existing socketpair (sys_socketpair) resource leaks in the same function while there: on fd1-install failure pair[0] was already installed at fd0 but only its in-flight ref was dropped and the table slot leaked -> now sys_close(fd0) frees the slot+ref; and on copy_to_user failure BOTH installed fds were leaked despite a comment claiming "close both" -> now sys_close(fd0)+sys_close(fd1). Verification: this is an OOM-only failure path (fd_table_grow returning false), NOT reproducible at boot, so no bespoke deterministic selftest (F34 precedent); verified by an EXHAUSTIVE CODE-PROOF -- grep-enumerated all 14 fd_install call sites and confirmed each closes `f` exactly once on its negative branch (openpty master->close/slave->close + slot clear; socket/accept/recvfd/io_uring/eventfd/timerfd/recvmsg vfs_close; epoll epoll_close; socketpair vfs_close/sys_close), and that fd_install closes on none -> no path double-frees and no path leaks -- plus a clean boot: 36 selftests PASS (unchanged -- no unit-testable pure helper here), 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd, no socket/accept errors. The fd_install SUCCESS path is exercised by every fd opened at boot (files, sockets, the wayland accept() path), so a clean boot to login confirms the contract change did not regress normal fd allocation. sys_close is defined at syscall.c:503, well before the socketpair call sites. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F38 FIXED: unveil() sandbox enforced only in sys_open -> every other path syscall bypassed it (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/security/unveil.c, kernel/main.c). The EIGHTH-pass VFS subagent found unveil_check (kernel/security/unveil.c -- itself correct: empty table=full visibility, prefix match with a directory-boundary guard so /home/bob does not match /home/bobby) had exactly ONE call site: sys_open. So a process that had unveil()'d itself (OpenBSD-style self-sandboxing, e.g. after dropping into a restricted view) could STILL unlink/rename/mkdir/truncate/exec/stat/access paths OUTSIDE its unveiled view -- a full sandbox bypass for everything except open(). Root cause = a missing shared enforcement point. Fix (one shared mechanism, DRY): added a static unveil_ok(path, need) gate in syscall.c that encapsulates the exact policy sys_open used inline (skip when unveil.count==0 = no rules; exempt virtfs_is_virtual /dev,/proc; else unveil_check), refactored sys_open onto it (behaviour-preserving), and wired it into ALL the real path syscalls: sys_unlink, sys_rename (BOTH src and dst), sys_mkdir, sys_truncate, sys_exec, sys_stat, sys_access. CRITICAL correctness detail (verified via fs_lookup): the path MUST be normalized before the gate or `..` escapes the prefix (unveil /home/bob, then unlink /home/bob/../../etc/passwd whose UNnormalized string still prefix-matches /home/bob -> bypass). fs_lookup(char* path) calls normalize_path() IN PLACE (virtfs.c:383), so sys_open/stat/access (which route through fs_lookup) get a normalized path for free and the gate goes right AFTER fs_lookup; the mutating syscalls (unlink/rename/mkdir/truncate/exec) do NOT call fs_lookup (they go straight to ext2_*), so each now calls normalize_path() explicitly before the gate (and, since normalize can shorten the string, their parent-split loops were changed from `i<pathlen` to iterate to the NUL terminator). Permission bits per the unveil.h model: UNVEIL_CREATE for directory-entry create/remove (unlink/rename/mkdir, matching how open uses CREATE for O_CREAT), UNVEIL_WRITE for content change (truncate), UNVEIL_EXEC for exec, UNVEIL_READ for stat/access; deny returns -ENOENT (hide the path's existence, like sys_open). Folded in one MED raw-deref fix while there: sys_rename copied the user src/dst paths with raw __builtin_memcpy (no _access_ok -> #PF panic / kernel read on a bad pointer) -> now copy_from_user. VERIFICATION: the security property (sandbox now blocks the other syscalls) is not provable by a clean boot alone (the boot userland does not unveil, so the gates are no-ops for it), so (1) a deterministic unveil_gate_selftest (in unveil.c, wired in main.c) builds an unveil_table_t, grants /home/bob rwc, and asserts: empty-table allows anything; exact + inside-prefix match allowed; the boundary /home/bobby DENIED; a not-granted bit (EXEC) DENIED; out-of-view /etc/passwd and the parent /home DENIED -> proves the gate logic every wiring relies on; (2) an exhaustive CODE-PROOF -- grep confirms unveil_ok is called at all 9 sites (open/exec/stat/unlink/rename x2/mkdir/access/truncate) and each is AFTER normalization (explicit normalize_path for the 6 mutating, fs_lookup in-place for open/stat/access); (3) clean boot to login: 37 selftests PASS (was 36 -- the new unveil test), 0 FAILED/PANIC, [unveil] SELF-TEST PASSED, /bin/login fork-exec'd and the full userland (login/svcmgr/bash/sway, which do heavy exec/stat/open) runs through the now-gated path syscalls -> a clean boot proves valid paths are NOT wrongly denied (the boot processes have no unveil rules, count==0, so the gate short-circuits to allow). Not gated, recorded in AUDIT_FINDINGS.md: chmod/chown are no-op stubs; chdir is navigation-only (its resolved file ops are gated on the absolute path so it is not a bypass). REMAINING (separate focused pass, recorded): sys_open/exec/truncate/access still copy the path via a raw `while(upath[i])` deref (bounded 511 but no _access_ok -> kernel #PF DoS on a bad pointer); needs a shared strncpy_from_user-style helper (sys_rename is already converted this turn). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F39 FIXED: raw user-path-pointer deref in the NUL-terminated path syscalls (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/main.c). The MED finding deferred from F38: sys_open, sys_exec, sys_spawn, sys_access, sys_truncate (and a dead copy in sys_chmod) copied the user path with a RAW `while (i < 511 && upath[i]) { raw[i]=upath[i]; i++; }` byte-loop -- a direct dereference of the user pointer with NO _access_ok / prefault. A path pointer in the kernel half, the non-canonical gap, or an unmapped user page #PF-panicked the kernel inside the copy loop (a trivial unprivileged DoS), and a kernel-range pointer copied KERNEL memory into the path buffer (then used for fs_lookup -> potential info influence). The other path syscalls (unlink/mkdir/stat/rename) already used copy_from_user (rename was converted in F38). Root-cause fix (DRY, one shared mechanism): added a static int64_t copy_path_from_user(char* dst, const void* uptr, uint64_t dstsz) built ON TOP of the existing validated copy_from_user (which does _access_ok -- rejects NULL / >USER_ADDR_MAX kernel+non-canonical / overflow -- plus user_buf_prefault, a per-page VMA-checked fault-in). Because a path's length is unknown up front, the helper copies ONE PAGE-BOUNDED CHUNK at a time and stops at the NUL: a chunk never straddles into the next page, so a path that ends inside a mapped page never forces copy_from_user to touch the (possibly unmapped) following page -- correct strncpy_from_user semantics, at most 2 chunks since a path <= 512 < PAGE_SIZE. Returns the length (>=0), -EFAULT for a bad pointer, or -ENAMETOOLONG if no NUL within dstsz-1 (no silent truncation onto a wrong file, unlike the old loop). Converted all 5 real sites (open/exec/spawn/access/truncate); sys_chmod's copy was DEAD CODE (the ksec SETUID_BIT request sends inode/dev, never the path string) so it was removed outright rather than made safe. Forward-declared the helper at the top (its first use, sys_open, precedes its definition which sits next to copy_from_user). VERIFICATION: deterministic copy_path_user_selftest (in syscall.c, modeled on copy_user_selftest, wired in main.c) calls copy_path_from_user with the same bad-pointer battery -- kernel HHDM address, non-canonical 0xDEAD..., USER_ADDR_MAX+0x1000, NULL -- and asserts EACH returns -EFAULT (not a fault, not acceptance); the VALID-copy path (correct chunking + NUL + length) is not unit-testable at boot (no user mapping in the init_kthread context) but is exercised by EVERY exec/open/stat during boot, so a clean boot to login proves it copies real paths correctly. 38 selftests PASS (was 37 -- the new copypath_test), 0 FAILED/PANIC, [copypath_test] SELF-TEST PASSED, /bin/login fork-exec'd (login/svcmgr/bash/sway are all exec'd + open/stat hundreds of files through copy_path_from_user -> clean boot = no regression to valid path copies). Code-proof: grep confirms no raw `while (i < 511 && upath` / `while (plen < ... && upath` path-copy deref remains in syscall.c. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F40 FIXED: DRM MODE_ATOMIC unbounded per-object property count (kernel/drivers/video/drm.c, kernel/main.c). drm_ioctl_atomic bounds a.count_objs (<= DRM_MAX_SCANOUTS) but NOT the per-object property count counts[i] (copied from the user count_props_ptr). The inner loop `for (uint32_t j = 0; j < counts[i]; j++)` does 2 copy_from_user per iteration, so counts[i]=0xFFFFFFFF drives up to ~4 billion iterations = an unprivileged DoS / multi-second syscall, and the skip-object path `props_off += counts[i]*sizeof(u32)` / `values_off += counts[i]*sizeof(u64)` can overflow the 64-bit offsets (then copy_from_user's _access_ok rejects the wild offset -> -EFAULT, so not OOB, just the DoS). Reachable via DRM_IOCTL_MODE_ATOMIC on /dev/dri/card0 with attacker-controlled count_props_ptr contents. Root-cause fix: bound each counts[i] to DRM_MAX_PROPS_PER_OBJ (256 -- a real CRTC/plane carries well under 32 properties, so 256 is generous headroom that no compositor exceeds while capping the loop hard) immediately after the counts[] copy, returning -EINVAL otherwise; with counts[i] <= 256 and count_objs <= DRM_MAX_SCANOUTS the offset math also cannot overflow. Pure helper drm_atomic_count_ok(count) = count <= DRM_MAX_PROPS_PER_OBJ + deterministic drm_atomic_count_selftest (0 / 1 / exactly-256 accepted; 257 / 0xFFFFFFFF rejected). 38 selftests PASS (the new drm_atomic; the running tally had drifted -- main.c has exactly 38 selftest calls and the serial has 38 PASS lines, reconciled), 0 FAILED/PANIC, [drm_atomic] SELF-TEST PASSED, /bin/login fork-exec'd, clean boot. The valid path (real atomic commits with small counts) is unaffected by the generous cap. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F41 FIXED: wait() per-thread instead of per-process (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/proc/sched.c, kernel/proc/process.c, kernel/main.c). User direction: "FIX IT! DONT DEFER!" -- I had flagged this MED as too invasive; did the complete fix instead. The per-task children Treiber stack was anchored on g_current, and sys_fork/sys_spawn did task_child_add(g_current, child) while sys_wait did task_children_reap(g_current, ...). So in a multithreaded process (MakaOS userland has pthreads), a child forked by thread T1 sat on T1's private children list and thread T2's wait() drained T2's (empty) list -> -ECHILD; the zombie reparented to init on T1 exit (so no UAF/leak, but wrong POSIX -- any thread should reap any process-child). Root-cause fix: anchor the children list on the thread-group LEADER (the task whose pid == tgid) so a process has ONE children list shared by all its threads. Added tg_leader(task_t*) -> returns t if t->tgid==t->pid (single-threaded / we ARE the leader) else pid_ht_find(t->tgid), with a g_current fallback so it never returns NULL/dangling. It MUST run inside rcu_read_lock: pid_ht_find is RCU-protected and the caller's read section pins the returned leader across the subsequent task_child_add / task_children_reap (no use-after-free -- the F16/F17 pattern). Wired at all 3 anchor sites: sys_fork + sys_spawn (rcu_read_lock; task_child_add(tg_leader(g_current), child); rcu_read_unlock) and sys_wait (same around task_children_reap). CRITICAL invariant fix: task_children_reparent's drain was a PLAIN store (documented safe because "only the dying task walks its own list") -- but with leader-anchoring, OTHER threads can concurrently CAS-prepend onto the leader's children while the leader exits and reparents, so the drain is now __atomic_exchange_n(ACQ_REL) (the F34 all-atomic Treiber invariant -- every mutation of any children list is now CAS/XCHG). Closed the one rare straggler-leak (a surviving thread forks onto an already-exited group leader in the window before that leader is reaped) with a safety-net reparent-to-init in task_destroy (atomic XCHG of the reaped task's children -> init; a no-op for normal reaps since children are drained at exit; skipped for init itself). Single-threaded processes are unchanged: task_init_common sets tgid == pid for EVERY task (verified, kthreads included), so tg_leader returns self with no pid_ht lookup -- which is why the boot (all single-threaded leaders) is unaffected. VERIFICATION: deterministic tg_leader_selftest (in syscall.c, wired in main.c) builds fake task_t's -- a leader L (pid=tgid=0x7F100), a second thread T (pid 0x7F101, tgid 0x7F100), a zombie child C (pid 0x7F200) -- registers L in the pid hash (synthetic high pids, no concurrent RCU reader), asserts tg_leader(T)==L && tg_leader(L)==L, then "thread T forks C" via task_child_add(tg_leader(T), C) and "thread T waits" via task_children_reap(tg_leader(T), C->pid) -> asserts it reaps C; PASSED. The multithreaded-fork-cross-thread-reap runtime path is not boot-reproducible (no boot program forks in one thread and waits in another), so the selftest proves the leader-anchoring logic + a clean boot proves no regression to the heavy SINGLE-threaded fork/exit/wait at boot (login forks bash, svcmgr spawns login/net, every exit -> task_destroy safety net runs). [tgleader] SELF-TEST PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd, clean boot. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F42 FIXED: sys_thread did not zero its task_t (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). sys_thread (the pthread/clone-with-shared-mm path) was the ONE task constructor that did `task_t* t = kmalloc(sizeof(task_t))` and then set fields individually with NO `__builtin_memset(t, 0, sizeof(*t))` first -- unlike task_fork, task_create_user, and task_create_kthread, which ALL memset right after the kmalloc (process.c:252/286/417) before task_init_common sets the named fields (task_init_common itself does not memset; the callers do). So every task_t field that sys_thread does not explicitly assign inherited slab-poison/garbage from the freelist; the moment any new field is added to task_t (especially a pointer / list head like the children/child_next anchors, or a lock, or a refcount) and a caller forgets to set it in sys_thread, that field is a wild value -> UAF / crash / corruption. A fragile, drift-prone design (one constructor diverging from the established zero-then-init invariant). Root-cause fix: added `__builtin_memset(t, 0, sizeof(*t));` immediately after the `if (!t) return -ENOMEM;` and BEFORE the first field write (t->pid = pid_alloc()), exactly matching the three sibling constructors -- nothing is set before the memset (the kmalloc'd block is uninitialized), so there is no clobber. Verification: an init-correctness fix (not unit-testable without standing up a full thread, and zeroing-then-initializing is trivially correct) -> code-proof (the memset now matches the 3 siblings; placed before all field inits) + clean boot (39 selftests still pass, 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd; the thread path is exercised if any pthread-using userland launches, and a wrongly-placed memset would have clobbered sys_thread's inits and broken thread creation). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F43 FIXED: AHCI submit functions did not self-guard their PRDT/page bounds (kernel/drivers/storage/ahci.c). Two latent defense-in-depth gaps where ahci_submit_hhdm / ahci_submit_sg trusted their inputs instead of bounding them like do_rw_direct does. (1) ahci_submit_hhdm builds the PRDT in `while (rem > 0 && nprdt < 248u)`; if a transfer needed more than 248 PRD entries (~992 KB page-fragmented) the loop exited with rem != 0 and the function called issue_cmd ANYWAY -> a truncated DMA command (the tail of the buffer has no PRD entry), silently corrupting the read/write. do_rw_direct already guards this with `if (rem) return 0;` (ahci.c:635) -- ahci_submit_hhdm was the un-guarded twin. Fixed: after the build loop, `if (rem) { free the slot we reserved via __atomic_fetch_or(&s_free_mask, 1u<<slot, RELEASE) + wait_queue_wake_all(&s_slot_avail_wq); rc = 0; break; }` -- CRITICAL detail: unlike do_rw_direct (which uses fixed slot 0 and can just `return 0`), ahci_submit_hhdm slot_alloc's its slot, and a slot is only OR'd back into s_free_mask by the IRQ completion handler AFTER issue_cmd; since we bail BEFORE issue_cmd, the IRQ would never free it, so the early-exit must free the slot itself (matching the IRQ handler's free+wake pattern at ahci.c:321-322) then break to the s_submit_busy release path. (2) ahci_submit_sg fills a fixed `phys_addr_t phys_pages[130]` stack array with `for (i = 0; i < npages; i++) phys_pages[i] = ...` -- if npages > 130 this is a STACK BUFFER OVERFLOW (and build_prdt_pages would also overrun the 248-entry PRDT). The sole caller (ahci_read_user) clamps npages <= 130, but the function trusted it; now ahci_submit_sg self-guards `if (npages > 130u) return 0;` before the fill loop (before slot_alloc, so no slot to free). Both gaps are latent today (ext2 pre-clamps transfers to AHCI_DMA_SECTORS=1024 sectors -> <= ~130 PRDs; ahci_read_user clamps npages <= 130), but the submit primitives no longer trust their inputs (fail cleanly with rc=0 instead of truncating or smashing the stack), the same fragile-design class as F36. VERIFICATION: these are guards on currently-unreachable over-large transfers (not unit-testable without driving the HBA), so code-proof (the `if (rem)` matches do_rw_direct's return convention and frees the slot per the IRQ handler's pattern; the `if (npages > 130)` matches the phys_pages[130] / 248-PRDT bound) + clean boot: 40 selftest PASS lines, 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd. The AHCI read path is exercised on EVERY ext2 file read at boot through BOTH submit_hhdm (kernel buffers: ELF loader, page cache) and submit_sg (user buffers: ahci_read_user fast path), so a clean boot to login (which reads login/svcmgr/bash/sway + fonts) proves the guards do NOT trip on legitimate <=1024-sector / <=130-page transfers. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F44 FIXED: TCP per-PCB data-plane lock (the documented T4 ring-accounting race) (kernel/net/tcp.c, kernel/main.c). The last real Phase-1 backlog bug. The per-PCB ring fields -- txbuf_used/txbuf_head + snd_una (advanced by the RX ACK drain in tcp_input on the net RX kernel thread, and by tcp_send on a user syscall CPU) and rxbuf_used/rxbuf_tail/rcv_nxt (written by the RX data path, drained by tcp_recv_data) -- were RMW'd from multiple CPUs with NO per-PCB lock, mitigated only by F18's tcp_ring_consume underflow clamp (so the worst case was a transient mis-account / producer wedge, not OOB). Implemented the recommended-first "data-plane-only" decomposition (the full state-machine + handshake/accept-queue lock remains a separate item -- see AUDIT_FINDINGS.md T4 REMAINING). Added a per-PCB `spinlock_t lock` (init in tcp_pcb_alloc) taken via tcp_pcb_lock = preempt_disable + spin_lock. CHOSE preempt_disable + plain spin_lock over the prior note's spin_lock_irqsave because: RX TCP processing runs in the net RX KERNEL THREAD (virtio_net's IRQ handler only irq_notify's -- no IRQ handler touches a PCB), so preempt_disable already prevents the same-CPU preempted-holder deadlock the note worried about (the F35/fb.c pattern), AND because the lock guards ONLY the field RMWs the transmit (tcp_send_segment -> ipv4_send -> virtio_net_tx's synchronous 10M-spin tx-poll) stays entirely OUTSIDE the lock, which sidesteps the "irqsave across a ms-scale tx poll" hazard the note flagged. Locked 4 sites: (1) RX ACK txbuf drain (tcp_ring_consume + snd_una/snd_wnd/rto) -- lock, then pcb_wake OUTSIDE; (2) RX in-order data write (kernel skbuff -> kernel rxbuf copy is safe under the lock; rxbuf_tail/used/rcv_nxt) -- lock, then pcb_wake + ACK-send OUTSIDE; (3) tcp_send -- RESERVE pattern: a new pure tcp_ring_reserve(tail,used,want,size,mask,&start) clamps want to free space + advances tail/used UNDER the lock returning the start index, then the user-payload copy happens OUTSIDE the lock (src may be USER memory -> must not fault under a spinlock; the RX side only advances txbuf_head, never the reserved tail range -> safe + multi-producer-correct), with `if (chunk==0) continue` re-entering the buffer-full wait; (4) tcp_recv_data -- mirror reserve: snapshot rxbuf_head + tcp_ring_consume UNDER the lock, copy to the (user) dst OUTSIDE, wrapped in a for(;;) with an `avail==0 -> unlock + re-wait` raced-empty re-check for multi-consumer (dup'd fd) safety. sched_sleep (buffer full/empty waits) is always OUTSIDE the lock. Leaf lock: pcb->lock never nests with s_pcb_wlock (send/recv/RX walk PCBs under rcu_read_lock; only insert/remove take s_pcb_wlock) and never wraps a transmit/wake/sleep -> no ordering cycle, no I/O/sleep under the spinlock. VERIFICATION: the locked send/recv/RX paths are NOT exercised at boot (the boot net stack does DHCP=UDP, no TCP data), so per the contract the LOCK PLACEMENT is code-proven (every txbuf_used/rxbuf_used/snd_una mutation is now under tcp_pcb_lock; wakes/sends/copies/sleeps are outside) and the ARITHMETIC is unit-tested -- new deterministic tcp_ring_reserve_selftest (normal reserve, tail wrap, clamp-to-free-space, full->0, wrap+clamp) PASSED, alongside the existing tcp_ring_consume_selftest -- plus a clean boot proving no net-stack-init regression: 41 PASS lines, 0 FAILED/PANIC, [tcp_reserve] SELF-TEST PASSED, /bin/login fork-exec'd. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Phase 1 backlog is now COMPLETE except the 3 fail-closed ksec FEATURE gaps (not bugs -- they ADD privilege-grant paths; flagged for the user rather than silently wired).
- 2026-06-25 - F45 FIXED: TCP listener accept-queue child<->listener race (T4 follow-up) (kernel/net/tcp.c, kernel/main.c). The next genuine backlog bug after F44. The completed-connection FIFO on a LISTEN pcb (accept_queue[TCP_BACKLOG] + accept_head/accept_tail/accept_count) was mutated WITHOUT a lock from two CPUs: the RX kernel thread enqueues a child that finished its handshake (tcp_input SYN_RCVD -> ESTABLISHED) while accept() (tcp_accept, on a user syscall CPU) dequeues. The uint8_t accept_count RMW (producer count++ vs consumer count--) tears -> lost count update (a queued child becomes invisible to accept, or count under/overflows), and the head/tail indices + the accept_queue[] slot can tear -> a child dequeued twice or a slot overwritten before it is taken = use of a wrong/freed child pcb. The documented T4 "two-PCB" hazard (SYN_RCVD mutates the LISTENER's queue while holding the CHILD) is sidestepped: the accept_queue belongs to the LISTENER, so locking the LISTENER's own pcb->lock at both sites is a SINGLE lock -- no child<->listener two-lock cycle. Root-cause fix (safe-primitives style -- extract + reuse + test): pulled the ring into two pure helpers accept_q_push(lst,child)->bool (false if backlog full -> child dropped, as before) and accept_q_pop(lst)->child|NULL, the ONLY mutators of the queue, each requiring the caller to hold the listener's lock. tcp_input takes tcp_pcb_lock(lst) around accept_q_push then pcb_wake(lst) OUTSIDE the lock (wake takes rq_lock); tcp_accept takes tcp_pcb_lock(listener) around accept_q_pop. The lock is the per-PCB spinlock from F44 (preempt_disable + spin_lock; RX is a kernel thread not an IRQ handler; leaf lock, never nests with s_pcb_wlock, never wraps a transmit/wake/sleep). The poll-side `accept_count > 0` read (is_acceptable) stays a lockless hint (poll re-checks; accept() re-validates under the lock). VERIFICATION: TCP accept is not boot-exercised (boot net = DHCP/UDP), so per the contract a deterministic tcp_accept_q_selftest (kmalloc'd fake listener + distinct non-dereferenced marker pointers) drives accept_q_push/pop: empty->NULL, fill to TCP_BACKLOG=8 then reject-when-full, FIFO drain to empty, and wrap-around push+pop 3*BACKLOG times across the modulo -- PASSED -- plus code-proof (accept_queue is now mutated ONLY through the two helpers, both under the listener lock; the only lockless access is the poll hint) + clean boot (the listen/accept code compiles and the net stack inits; 43 PASS lines, 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd). T4 REMAINING after F45: snd_nxt (needs the tcp_send_segment seq-advance/transmit split) and the connection state-machine transitions -- single-writer-dominant / benign-read races, recorded. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F46 FIXED: ext2 32-bit device-LBA computation could wrap to a wrong sector (kernel/fs/ext2.c, kernel/main.c). bcache_get (block read) and write_block both formed the device LBA as `uint32_t lba = s_part_lba + blk * s_sectors_per_blk` -- a 32-bit multiply+add -- then passed it to ahci_read/ahci_write, both of which take a uint64_t lba (the HBA supports 64-bit LBAs). blk is validated by ext2_block_valid (blk < s_blocks_count), but s_blocks_count comes straight from the superblock (ext2_init, only a ==0 reject) and is NOT bounded to the real partition size, so a crafted ext2 image can declare it up to ~2^32; an inode block pointer near that bound passes validation, and `blk * s_sectors_per_blk` (spb in {2,4,8}) overflows uint32 and WRAPS -- the truncated LBA points at a different, VALID sector, so the read/write silently hits the WRONG sector within the device (info leak on read, corruption on write); the same bug breaks any genuinely large (>2 TB-class) filesystem. Root-cause fix (safe-primitives + DRY -- the two sites duplicated the computation): extracted a tagged primitive ext2_blk_lba(part_lba, blk, spb) = (uint64_t)part_lba + (uint64_t)blk * spb, forming the LBA in 64-bit so the product cannot wrap (blk < 2^32, spb <= 8 -> product < 2^35, +part_lba < 2^36, all within u64; no overflow CHECK is needed, so NO ckd_mul -- the fix is computing in the correct WIDTH), plus a static ext2_blk_to_lba(blk) wrapper over the file-statics, mirroring the existing ext2_block_in_range/ext2_block_valid pure+wrapper split. Both call sites now do `uint64_t lba = ext2_blk_to_lba(blk)`; lba is used only in the ahci_* call (the next line re-derives from blk), so the widen has no downstream u32 assumption. Out of scope (separate layer, recorded): ahci_read/write do not bound lba against device capacity -- a genuinely out-of-range huge LBA is the HBA's to reject; the wrap-to-a-valid-wrong-sector was the dangerous case and is eliminated. VERIFICATION: the common small-blk path is exercised every boot (ext2 mount + /bin/login read through bcache_get) and is byte-identical to the old code for small blk (no wrap), proving no regression; the WRAP boundary is covered by a new deterministic ext2_blk_lba_selftest driving blk*spb == 2^32 (a u32 product truncates to 0), past-2^32 with a partition base, max blk 0xFFFFFFFF, and mixed spb=4 -- PASSED. 44 selftest calls, 0 FAILED/PANIC, /bin/login fork-exec'd. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F46 COMPLETED: the first F46 commit converted only bcache_get + write_block; a verify-all-angles "same class elsewhere" sweep found TWO MORE sites of the identical u32 LBA-wrap bug -- `uint32_t lba = s_part_lba + phys_blk * s_sectors_per_blk` in the two inode_build_run DMA read paths (kernel/fs/ext2.c ~1202 and ~1299, the ELF-loader / bulk-read fast path that DMAs a whole contiguous run via ahci_read/ahci_read_user). The first grep keyed on `blk * s_sectors_per_blk` and these use `phys_blk`, so they were missed -- exactly the incompleteness verify-all-angles warns about. phys_blk is an untrusted inode/indirect pointer validated only by ext2_run_valid (phys_blk < s_blocks_count, possibly huge for a crafted image), so the u32 product wrapped the same way. Converted both to `uint64_t lba = ext2_blk_to_lba(phys_blk)` (the F46 primitive); the adjacent `sectors = run * s_sectors_per_blk` is left as-is (cap-safe: run is clamped to dma_cap = AHCI_DMA_SECTORS / spb first, so the product <= AHCI_DMA_SECTORS). ALL FOUR ext2 LBA sites now go through ext2_blk_to_lba (grep confirms zero `uint32_t lba` remain). VERIFICATION: the run-read path is exercised every boot (the ELF loader reads /bin/login through inode_build_run -> line 1202) and is byte-identical for small phys_blk, so the clean boot proves it; the wrap boundary stays covered by ext2_blk_lba_selftest. 0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 44 selftests. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F47 FIXED: AHCI sector->byte transfer sizing could wrap u32 and bypass the DMA size guards (kernel/drivers/storage/ahci.c, kernel/main.c). The F46 sibling sweep continued into the storage driver: ahci_submit_hhdm, ahci_submit_sg, and ahci_read_user each formed the transfer length as `uint32_t bytes = count * 512` and then bounded the DMA by a BYTE-derived guard -- ahci_read_user's `npages = (first_off + count*512 + PAGE-1)/PAGE; if (npages > 130) return 0`, submit_hhdm's 248-entry PRDT `if (rem) return 0`, submit_sg's npages<=130 -- while issue_cmd is handed the RAW sector count. If count >= 2^23 (8M sectors), `count*512` overflows u32 and WRAPS to a small byte value: the byte guard sees a tiny transfer and passes, but the HBA is still told to move the huge count into a buffer/PRDT sized for the tiny one -> DMA overrun (OOB write). LATENT, not currently reachable: every caller today passes count <= AHCI_DMA_SECTORS = 1024 (ext2 run reads clamp run to AHCI_DMA_SECTORS/spb; bcache/superblock <= 8), so the wrap is unreachable via existing callers -- but a guard that an integer overflow can defeat is a real hole (the F40-class defense-in-depth), and ahci_read_user/ahci_read/ahci_write are exported. Root-cause fix (safe-primitives + DRY -- three sites shared the bare multiply + a byte guard): extracted a tagged primitive xfer_bytes_ok(sectors, sector_size, max_bytes, *out) that forms the length in u64 (cannot wrap) and returns false on 0 sectors or length > max_bytes (so *out is only ever set to a value <= max_bytes, fitting u32 losslessly). Applied: submit_hhdm with max=0xFFFFFFFF (pure wrap-prevention, the existing PRDT rem-check still caps fragmentation, so no behavior change for any valid transfer); submit_sg with max=130*PAGE_SIZE (matches its existing npages<=130 guard, placed before slot_alloc so a reject leaks no slot); ahci_read_user with max=130*PAGE_SIZE - first_off, which is the EXACT algebraic equivalent of the old npages<=130 (ceil((first_off+tb)/PAGE) <= 130 <=> tb <= 130*PAGE - first_off), so the now-redundant `if (npages > 130) return 0` was DELETED (the primitive subsumes it). do_rw_direct's `n * 512` is left as-is (n is capped at 65535 before the multiply -> max 33.5M, no wrap; it is the chunking loop for large transfers). VERIFICATION: all three modified paths are exercised every boot (ext2 reads /bin/login + svcmgr + net via ahci_read -> submit_hhdm and the run-read via ahci_read_user -> submit_sg, all with valid count <= 1024) and are byte-identical there, so the clean boot proves no regression (a too-tight bound would fail to load); the OVERFLOW reject path is covered by a new deterministic xfer_bytes_ok_selftest driving sectors*512 == 2^32 (a u32 product truncates to 0), the exact byte boundary, just-under-wrap, and a 2^30 large no-wrap -- PASSED. 0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 45 selftests. (One boot hung in the unrelated chaselev work-stealing-deque stress test -- pure in-memory, no disk I/O; a clean re-boot reached login + all selftests, confirming flakiness, not this change.) SAME-CLASS sibling RECORDED, not yet fixed: nvme_rw `bytes = nlb * s_ns_lba_size` (kernel/drivers/storage/nvme.c) has the identical pattern guarded by its `>8KB not supported` check, but nvme is not the boot device so a fix there is not boot-verifiable this pass. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F48 FIXED: nvme_rw transfer-size wrap (the F47 nvme sibling) + extracted the bounded-multiply generic (kernel/include/checked.h, kernel/main/checked.c, kernel/drivers/storage/nvme.c, kernel/drivers/storage/ahci.c). nvme_rw formed `uint32_t bytes = nlb * s_ns_lba_size` then used it to choose the 1-vs-2-PRP (<= 8 KiB) layout, while the command's sector count went out as `cmd.cdw12 = (nlb-1) & 0xFFFF` -- a 16-bit-MASKED count. A huge nlb (e.g. 2^23) wraps `nlb*512` to a small/zero byte value: the >8KB guard is skipped (single PRP, 1 page), but cdw12 carries a large masked count, so the device DMAs far past the one PRP -- e.g. nlb = 2^23 -> bytes = 0 (single 4 KB PRP) but cdw12 = 0xFFFF -> 65536-sector (32 MB) transfer -> OOB. LATENT like F47 (the only callers are the boot nvme stress test with nlb = 8). Done RIGHT, not duplicated: the shared core of this and ahci's xfer_bytes_ok is "form a*b in u64 (two u32s cannot wrap) and accept iff <= max" -- a genuinely cross-cutting bounds+arith generic, so it was extracted as `mul_within_u32(a, b, max, *out)` in checked.h (single source). ahci's xfer_bytes_ok is now a thin wrapper (`sectors != 0 && mul_within_u32(...)`, an exact behavioral match -- verified branch by branch), and nvme_rw uses `mul_within_u32(nlb, s_ns_lba_size, 8192, &bytes)` then keeps its existing pg_off-aware first_chunk/prp2 logic verbatim (so the bound is identical for valid transfers and the overflow is rejected before cdw12 is ever formed). do_rw_direct (n capped 65535) and the ahci sites are unchanged behaviorally. VERIFICATION: mul_within_u32 boundary cases added to checked_selftest (normal, exact == max, over, the 2^23 wrap that a u32 product truncates to 0, just-under-wrap, 0*b) -- `[checked] SELF-TEST PASSED (... + mul_within)`; ahci's xfer_bytes_ok_selftest still PASSED (wrapper is equivalent); clean boot exercises every ahci path (ext2 reads /bin/login) byte-identically -> no regression. The nvme path itself is not boot-exercised (no nvme block layer + nvme not boot device), so its correctness rests on the generic's selftest + the unchanged glue. 0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 45 selftests. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F49 FIXED: virtio-gpu scanout backing could be under-allocated by a w*h*4 u32 wrap -> GPU/paint-loop OOB (kernel/drivers/video/virtio_gpu.c, kernel/main.c). vgpu_setup_scanout_buffer sized the framebuffer as `uint32_t bytes = w * h * 4` (two u32 multiplies) and allocated a buddy block of that many bytes, but then told the GPU the resource is the FULL w*h (virtio_gpu_resource_create_2d + set_scanout) and the present paint loop writes w*h pixels into the backing. w and h are `s_scanouts[0].w/h` -- the device-reported scanout mode, copied verbatim from the virtio-gpu device config (resp.pmodes) with NO bound (untrusted, same class as the F22/F26/F36 device/on-disk values). A large or crafted mode wraps w*h*4 in u32 (e.g. 0x10000 x 0x10000 -> w*h = 2^32 -> 0): a tiny backing is allocated, but the GPU resource and the paint loop both access the full (huge) w*h -> out-of-bounds read/write of host kernel memory. Root-cause fix (safe-primitives, reusing the F48 generic): extracted a tagged primitive vgpu_fb_bytes(w, h, *out) that forms w*h*4 via mul_within_u32 (u64, cannot wrap) capped at VGPU_MAX_FB_BYTES = 256 MiB (covers 8K = 33 MB, ~8x headroom), rejecting a 0 dimension or an over-cap mode. vgpu_setup_scanout_buffer now returns 0 on reject -- both callers (virtio_gpu_present_test, virtio_gpu_fbcon_init) already propagate that return, and the present paint loop only runs after setup succeeds, so a rejected mode paints nothing. fbcon_init's `*out_pitch = w * 4` is transitively safe once w*h*4 <= 256 MiB (w <= 64 M -> w*4 <= 256 M < 2^32). Class swept (F46 lesson): the drm.c size math (drm_dumb_size F23, the addfb/atomic `a.width*a.height*4` and mode-clock paths, drm.c:493/2267/2294/1233/1600) ALREADY computes in u64 -> not in scope; fb.c's glyph offset (`row*16*pitch + col*8*4`) uses kernel-controlled console cursor positions bounded by the scroll logic, not device/user input -> out of class. VERIFICATION: the real boot mode is 1280x800 (4 MB, far under the cap) so it is byte-identical -- the clean boot inits the GPU (`[virtio-gpu] scanout 0: 1280x800`), sets scanout 0, and reaches login through the framebuffer console, proving no regression; the wrap / over-cap / 0-dimension reject paths are covered by a new deterministic vgpu_fb_bytes_selftest (normal, 8K valid, exact 256 MiB cap, one-row-over reject, the 2^32 wrap a naive u32 truncates to 0, zero-w, zero-h) -- `[vgpu_fbsz] SELF-TEST PASSED`. 0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 46 selftests. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F50 FIXED: a crafted ext2 s_inode_size let an inode straddle the bcache slot -> OOB read + OOB write (kernel/fs/ext2.c, kernel/main.c). inode_load_into does `__builtin_memcpy(out, r.data + off, sizeof(ext2_inode_t))` and inode_disk_write does `__builtin_memcpy(scratch + off, in, sizeof(ext2_inode_t))`, both with off = (local * s_inode_size) % s_block_size, where local = (ino-1) % s_inodes_per_grp. s_inode_size is the on-disk superblock field (u16), taken with ONLY a `> 0` check (ext2_init: `s_inode_size = (rev>=1 && s_inode_size>0) ? s_inode_size : 128`). For a well-formed fs s_inode_size is a power of two that divides s_block_size, so inodes tile a block and off + 128 <= block_size. A crafted superblock can set any 1..65535 value: e.g. s_inode_size = 4032 (not a power of two, does not divide 4096) makes local=1 -> off = 4032, and the 128-byte memcpy runs from byte 4032 of the 4096-byte slot -> 64 bytes OOB. On the read side (inode_load_into) that leaks adjacent bcache/heap bytes into the returned inode (exposed via stat etc.); on the write side (inode_disk_write, inode writeback) it is a 64-byte OOB WRITE past the scratch buffer = heap corruption. Both sites share the offset math, so the single ROOT fix is to validate s_inode_size once at mount (do-it-right: reject the invalid filesystem, do not patch each memcpy). Added a pure tagged primitive ext2_inode_size_valid(inode_size, block_size) = (inode_size >= sizeof(ext2_inode_t)) && (inode_size <= block_size) && power-of-two; ext2_init refuses the mount (return 0) when it fails. Proof the invariant holds: power-of-2 + <= block_size (itself a validated power of two from ext2_block_size_checked) means inode_size divides block_size, so off is a multiple of inode_size in [0, block_size - inode_size]; with inode_size >= sizeof(ext2_inode_t) = 128, off + 128 <= block_size - inode_size + 128 <= block_size. sizeof(ext2_inode_t) is 128 (the struct is __attribute__((packed)), confirmed by a host probe), so every real fs (s_inode_size a power of two >= 128, e.g. 128 or 256) still mounts. Sibling of ext2_block_size_checked (which already gates s_log_block_size the same way). Other inode/bgd struct memcpys at r.data+off are NOT in this class: read_bgd uses a FIXED 32-byte ext2_bgd_t stride that divides the block; the dirent walks (dir_lookup, ext2_readdir) bound off+8 <= blk_bytes and clamp name_len; the file-data copies clamp to_copy to block_size - off_in_blk. VERIFICATION: the clean boot MOUNTS ext2 with the real disk's s_inode_size (valid) and loads /bin/login through inode_load_into, proving the valid path is unbroken (a too-strict check would fail the mount and there would be no login); the reject cases that the old `> 0` check let through are covered by a new deterministic ext2_inode_size_valid_selftest (standard 128, large 256, inode==block 4096, smallest block 1024, and rejects: 0, 64 (< sizeof), 192 + 130 (not pow2), 4032 (the straddle case), 8192 (> block)) -- `[ext2_isz] SELF-TEST PASSED`. 0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 47 selftests. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F51 FIXED: the socket recv/send/accept/connect/bind syscall handlers deref'd the raw user buf/sockaddr pointer = arbitrary kernel R/W LPE (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). HIGH severity, unprivileged + fully local (AF_UNIX socketpair, or loopback UDP). sys_recvfrom / sys_sendto / sys_accept / sys_connect / sys_bind took the user buf_ptr / addr_ptr straight from the syscall registers (only !NULL-checked) and passed them to code that dereferences them DIRECTLY: tcp_recv_data does `dst[i] = pcb->rxbuf[...]` into buf_ptr (kernel/net/tcp.c:789), the UDP path memcpy's skb->data into buf_ptr (kernel/net/socket.c), unix_sock_recv cbuf_read's into buf_ptr; socket_accept writes the peer sockaddr through addr_ptr; connect/bind read sa->sin_*/sun_path. NONE routed through _access_ok / user_buf_check / copy_*_user, unlike the rest of the kernel -- sys_read prefaults (syscall.c:279) and io_uring OP_READ/WRITE call user_buf_check (io_uring.c:858/878); the socket path was the gap. The `copy`/`len` clamps only bound the COUNT and keep the kernel-side source in range; they do nothing for the DESTINATION pointer. Exploit: `recvfrom(s, (void*)KADDR, n, 0, NULL, NULL)` with KADDR any kernel address writes up to n attacker-chosen bytes (the datagram payload) to KADDR -> overwrite cred.euid / a function pointer / a PTE -> LPE; `send`/`sendto` with buf_ptr=KADDR is the mirror arbitrary kernel READ onto the wire (KASLR/secret leak); accept/connect/bind read/write a sockaddr at an attacker-chosen kernel address (smaller). Found by a read-only fan-out audit, then confirmed against the real code (sys_recvfrom -> socket_recv -> tcp_recv_data `dst[i]=`). Fix (do-it-right + the whole class, F46 lesson -- ALL FIVE handlers): validate every raw pointer with user_buf_check (= the existing _access_ok range guard, which rejects addr > USER_ADDR_MAX i.e. kernel/non-canonical and permanently kills the kernel-write primitive, + user_buf_prefault, which maps the user pages so the direct memcpy cannot #PF-panic) BEFORE the deref: buf_ptr with `len`; addr_ptr with sizeof(sockaddr_un_t) on the AF_UNIX branch / sizeof(sockaddr_in_t) on the AF_INET branch (the family is chosen by is_unix_sock(f), kernel-known, so the size is correct per branch). Forward-declared user_buf_check for the handlers above its definition. NULL addr_ptr paths preserved (`addr_ptr && ...`). This also fixes the io_uring OP_SEND/RECV/CONNECT/ACCEPT opcodes, which forward to these handlers. VERIFICATION: the boot does userspace DHCP over an AF_INET DGRAM socket via sendto/recvfrom and STILL gets its lease (`[net] ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15 GW 10.0.2.2`), proving the valid recv/send path is unbroken with the added validation (a false-reject would have lost the lease); user_buf_check's _access_ok range guard is covered by access_ok_selftest, copy_*_user by copy_user_selftest. No new selftest: the change is glue over an already-tested primitive + a boot-exercised happy path. 0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 47 selftests. RECORDED residual (pre-existing + kernel-wide, NOT introduced here -- sys_read has the same shape): the recv copy happens AFTER a blocking wait, so a concurrent munmap of the prefaulted buffer is a TOCTOU that could #PF; the _access_ok range check still permanently prevents the kernel-address write (the severe primitive), and the bounce-buffer pattern (as recvmsg already uses) is the fuller hardening for a later pass. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F52 FIXED: user_buf_prefault overflow defeated sys_read (arbitrary-kernel-WRITE LPE) + sys_write deref'd buf raw with no validation (kernel-READ leak) (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). The F51 read-leak follow-up turned up a DEEPER bug. (1) user_buf_prefault, the chokepoint every prefault-only caller relies on, computed `end = (addr + len + 0xFFF) & ~0xFFF`.  A huge len wraps addr+len so `end` falls BELOW `page`, the `for (; page < end; ...)` loop runs ZERO times, and the function returns 0 ("ok") having validated NOTHING.  That fully defeats the prefault for a prefault-ONLY caller -- sys_read (syscall.c:284) does `user_buf_prefault(buf, len)` with no preceding _access_ok -- so read(sockfd, KADDR, 0xFFFFFFFFFFFFFFFF) -> vfs_read -> tcp_recv_data writes the datagram bytes to KADDR = arbitrary kernel WRITE / LPE (the F51 primitive, but via read() + a huge len; F51 fixed sendto/recvfrom, not the generic read()).  copy_from_user/copy_to_user are NOT affected: they call _access_ok (overflow-safe via its ckd_add_u64, F19/F24) BEFORE the prefault, so the huge len is already rejected.  Root fix at the chokepoint (do-it-right): reject a wrapping addr+len with ckd_add_u64, then iterate by PAGE COUNT (npages = ((addr_end-1)>>12) - (addr>>12) + 1) so the loop bound can never overflow -- for a valid range this visits the identical page set (verified: addr=0x402000 len=0x1001 -> 2 pages both ways), so sys_read/copy/blit behaviour is unchanged for valid inputs while the overflow now returns -1.  This makes user_buf_prefault safe BY ITSELF, protecting every current + future prefault-only caller. (2) sys_write (syscall.c:198) passed the raw buf to vfs_write with NO validation, while sys_read prefaults; a direct-deref write_op (sock_write -> tcp_send reads buf raw) then reads from a kernel address -> write(sockfd, KADDR, n) leaks kernel memory onto the wire.  Fix: range-check buf with _access_ok (rejects kernel/non-canonical/overflowing pointers) -- NOT user_buf_prefault: a write READS the buffer, so prefault allocating + zeroing fresh pages for absent pages is the WRONG DIRECTION (prefault is for read syscalls, where the kernel WRITES the buffer).  DEBUGGING NOTE: my first attempt added user_buf_prefault to sys_write and the boot hung the instant userspace started (login's first write); I did NOT assume the known chaselev flakiness -- a revert-test (stash the change -> boot reaches DHCP in 10s; re-apply -> hangs) proved it was my change, and isolating (prefault-rewrite-only boots fine; +sys_write-prefault hangs; +sys_write-_access_ok boots fine) pinned it to the wrong-direction prefault.  The fix is _access_ok-only.  VERIFICATION: clean SELFTESTS boot mounts ext2, runs all selftests, spawns userspace, and the net program gets its DHCP lease over read/write + sendto/recvfrom (`ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15`) -- every read/write/copy/socket path exercises the hardened prefault, so a regression would lose the lease or wedge login (as the buggy attempt did); ckd_add_u64's overflow boundary is covered by checked_selftest.  0 FAILED/PANIC, login reached, 47 selftests.  RECORDED residual (pre-existing, kernel-wide): a raw-deref write_op reading an absent-but-valid user page relies on the normal demand-fault path; the F51/recvmsg bounce-buffer is the fuller hardening.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F53 FIXED: ioctl TIOCGSERIAL did a raw 60-byte memset on an unvalidated user pointer = arbitrary-kernel-address write / #PF panic (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). HIGH severity, unprivileged. The tty0 ioctl fallback in sys_ioctl handled TIOCGSERIAL by zeroing a 60-byte serial_struct stub DIRECTLY through the raw user pointer: `case TIOCGSERIAL: if (arg) { uint8_t* p = (uint8_t*)arg; __builtin_memset(p, 0, 60); }`. arg is the third syscall argument, passed unfiltered through the dispatcher (no global syscall-arg sanitization). EVERY other struct-carrying case in the same switch (TIOCGWINSZ, TIOCSWINSZ, TIOCGPGRP, TIOCSPGRP, TCGETS, TCSETS/W/F) correctly uses copy_to_user / copy_from_user; TIOCGSERIAL alone deref'd arg raw with only a `!NULL` check. So ioctl(fd, TIOCGSERIAL, KADDR) writes 60 zero bytes to ANY kernel address -> zero a cred (uid/euid 0 = root) / a function pointer / a lock / a refcount = LPE, and an unmapped or non-canonical KADDR -> kernel #PF in memset -> "kernel #PF unrecoverable" panic = DoS. Reachability is maximal: tty0 fds (stdin/stdout/stderr of every console process) have f->ioctl == NULL (tty.c:397, by design -- handled by this fallback), and any fd whose file has ioctl == NULL also falls through here, so it is reachable on fd 0/1/2 of any process with no privilege. Found by a read-only fan-out audit, confirmed against the real code (the switch + the raw memset) and a kernel-wide grep proving this was the ONLY raw-arg deref in any ioctl handler (drm/pty/evdev/tty0 all copy_*_user; evdev read is prefaulted + bounded by len/sizeof; sys_sigreturn reads its frame via copy_from_user with canonical rip/rsp checks; uname/times/getrusage/gettimeofday all copy_to_user). Fix: route the 60-byte zero struct out through copy_to_user (which validates via _access_ok + user_buf_prefault, rejecting kernel/non-canonical/overflow/unmapped) exactly like the sibling cases; a valid arg gets the identical zeroed struct, a bad arg returns -EFAULT, NULL arg returns 0 as before. VERIFICATION: clean SELFTESTS boot reaches the DHCP lease (`ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15`), 0 FAILED/PANIC, login -- no regression (the change is one ioctl case, glue over copy_to_user whose bad-pointer rejection is already covered by copy_user_selftest; TIOCGSERIAL is not on the boot path so the boot proves the build/no-regression). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F54 FIXED: ext2 dir_add_entry slack underflow -> heap OOB write from a corrupt on-disk dirent (kernel/fs/ext2.c, kernel/main.c). When adding a directory entry, dir_add_entry walks the directory block's on-disk dirents looking for slack to split into: `actual_len = align4(8 + de->name_len); slack = de->rec_len - actual_len;` (unsigned u32), then `if (slack >= new_rec_len) { ... new_de = (ext2_dirent_t*)(dae_buf + off + actual_len); ... write new entry + name ... }`. de->rec_len (on-disk uint16) and de->name_len (on-disk uint8) are UNTRUSTED and were never validated -- the walk only bounded `off + 8 <= blk_bytes` (the header), never `off + rec_len <= blk_bytes` (the whole entry) nor `actual_len <= rec_len` (the name fits the entry). A corrupt entry with actual_len > rec_len -- e.g. name_len = 255 -> actual_len = 264 but rec_len = 16 -- makes slack = 16 - 264 = 0xFFFFFF08 (~4.29e9), so `slack >= new_rec_len` is ALWAYS true; the split then writes new_de = dae_buf + off + 264 with off legally as high as blk_bytes-8 (~4088), i.e. at ~4352, plus an 8-byte header and up to name_len bytes of the new filename -- a few hundred bytes PAST the 4096-byte kmalloc'd dae_buf = heap OOB write of attacker-influenced bytes into the adjacent slab object -> kernel memory corruption / LPE. Reached by ANY create that adds a dir entry (open O_CREAT / mkdir / rename / link) in a directory whose on-disk block is crafted or corrupt (same threat model as F46/F50 -- untrusted on-disk data; the FS mounts from a fixed device but the dirent contents are attacker-controllable via a crafted image / prior corruption). The READ-side walks (dir_lookup, ext2_readdir) already guard exactly this with ext2_dirent_namelen_clamp (comment: "a corrupt dirent near the block tail could claim a name that runs past the 4096-byte bcache slot"); the WRITE-side dir_add_entry + dir_remove_entry had NO equivalent. Found by a read-only fan-out audit, confirmed against the real code (the slack math + the new_de pointer + the dae_buf kmalloc(4096)). Fix (do-it-right + the whole class): extract a tagged primitive ext2_dirent_in_block(off, rec_len, name_len, blk_bytes) = (off + rec_len <= blk_bytes) && (align4(8+name_len) <= rec_len), and break the walk on a malformed entry in BOTH dir_add_entry (the OOB write) and dir_remove_entry (whose kmemeq name compare is the OOB-read sibling). dir_add then appends to a fresh block; dir_remove fails to find. With the invariant: actual_len <= rec_len so slack cannot underflow, and new_de = off + actual_len <= off + rec_len <= blk_bytes, the new entry [new_de, new_de+new_rec_len) subseteq [off, off+rec_len) subseteq block, and the name copy stays in bounds; the reuse path (de->rec_len >= new_rec_len) is also in-bounds (off + 8 + name_len <= off + new_rec_len <= off + rec_len <= blk_bytes). A well-formed dirent always passes, so valid directories are unaffected. VERIFICATION: clean SELFTESTS boot mounts ext2, reaches the DHCP lease (`ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15`), 0 FAILED/PANIC, login -- valid create/remove unchanged (the guard is a no-op for well-formed entries); the underflow (name_len=255/rec=16), past-block (off+rec>blk), and rec<8 reject cases are covered by a new deterministic ext2_dirent_in_block_selftest -- `[ext2_dirent] SELF-TEST PASSED`. 48 selftest calls, 0 fail. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F55 FIXED: unveil sandbox escape -- sys_open created the file BEFORE the unveil check (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). sys_open checked unveil_ok only at the got_file label, which runs AFTER ext2_create. Every other path syscall (sys_unlink:1800, sys_rename:1845, sys_mkdir:1999, the stat/access paths) gates unveil_ok right after fs_lookup, BEFORE the operation; sys_open was the lone outlier. So a process that has unveil()'d a subtree can open("/outside/evil", O_CREAT|O_RDWR): fs_lookup returns -ENOENT (file absent), the parent-directory write+exec check (a CREDENTIAL check, separate from unveil) passes on ordinary uid, ext2_create allocates the inode + adds the dir entry on disk, ext2_open reopens it, and only THEN does the got_file unveil_ok deny -> it vfs_close()'s the fd (drops the handle) but does NOT unlink the on-disk file. The file persists outside the unveiled subtree: the confined process escapes its filesystem confinement on the CREATE side (plant a predictable file another component later reads/execs; the caller even gets -ENOENT while the file now exists = deny-by-side-effect). Unprivileged, deterministic, single syscall (pledge stays PLEDGE_ALL so O_CREAT passes the pledge gate as CPATH). Found by a read-only fan-out audit, confirmed against the real code (ext2_create at sys_open:480 vs unveil_ok at got_file:500; cross-checked that unlink/rename/mkdir gate before their op). Fix (do-it-right, match the other syscalls): move the unveil gate to right after fs_lookup, BEFORE any open or create; `path` is already normalize_path'd in place by fs_lookup (so a trailing .. cannot escape), and unveil_ok keeps the virtual-mount (/dev,/proc) + no-rules exemptions internally. Removed the now-redundant got_file check: the early gate dominates every path to got_file (all flow through fs_lookup at the top), and it also avoids the wasted ext2_open of a denied EXISTING file. The early check is before `f` is assigned, so no vfs_close is needed on denial. DEBUGGING NOTE: my first verify boot stalled at userspace-start (no DHCP) -- the SAME shape as the chaselev flakiness AND the F52 regression. Per the contract I revert-tested (stash -> baseline DHCP in 10s; re-apply -> 100s stall), which POINTED at my change -- but a single flaky sample is not conclusive. The decisive check was a denial-tracing debug build (print path+comm+count on every unveil deny): it booted to DHCP with ZERO denials, proving the early gate is a NO-OP for the un-unveiled boot processes (count==0 -> unveil_ok returns 1), so my change cannot break the boot; the stall was flakiness. Lesson: for a flaky boot, a 1-sample revert-test can mislead -- confirm the mechanism (here, that nothing is actually denied) before blaming the change. VERIFICATION: clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (`ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15`), 0 FAILED/PANIC, login -- opens unaffected (zero boot denials); unveil_ok's prefix/boundary correctness is covered by the [unveil] + [virtfs_unveil] selftests. The fix is a reordering (gate before mutation), proven by the boot (no regression) + code (the gate now precedes ext2_create); the denied-create outcome needs a full unveil+FS harness to unit-test (not added). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F56 FIXED: ext2_write_file overwrite freed + reallocated blocks with NO inode lock held -> same-file write race -> cross-file block corruption (kernel/fs/ext2.c). The overwrite branch (existing file) read the inode as a read_inode SNAPSHOT -- read_inode takes inode_lock, copies, and RELEASES the lock -- then ran free_inode_blocks(&snapshot) + the alloc_block / write_block / inode_set_block loop with NO lock held, taking inode_lock only for the final writeback (`leaf->inode = old_inode; inode_writeback; inode_unlock`). So two concurrent writers to the SAME file (two open(O_TRUNC), or ftruncate + write, or write + create-overwrite) both snapshot the same i_block[] and both run free_inode_blocks: writer A frees X then re-allocs it (alloc_block returns the just-freed X, or hands X to another file), and writer B -- still holding A's stale snapshot -- ALSO frees X, returning a LIVE block to the free bitmap to be re-allocated to a third file = two inodes sharing one physical data block (cross-file data corruption). The bitmap_test guard in free_block stops a pure double-free (freeing an already-free block is a no-op) but NOT this free-of-a-reallocated-block. Reachable by any two threads/processes writing the same file (LOCKS.md says the ext2 inode lock is a per-inode mutex; the overwrite path simply did not hold it across the mutation). Found as a fan-out runner-up, confirmed against the real code (read_inode releases the lock at 803-812; the overwrite branch holds nothing across free->realloc). Fix (do-it-right, ROOT at the lock): take inode_lock(existing_ino) at the START and hold it across the ENTIRE free -> realloc -> writeback, operating on a LOCAL copy of leaf->inode so a mid-way error (alloc/write failure) discards cleanly exactly as the snapshot did (commit `leaf->inode = work` + writeback ONLY on success). VERIFIED the lock discipline first (no-assumptions): inode_lock = seq_write_begin, which DOES take the per-leaf write_lock spinlock (seqlock.h:106-108), so it serialises writers (not a pure seqlock); the bitmap (group locks) / bcache / slot-wait ops under it never call inode_lock, and this is the SAME lock order the pre-existing final writeback already used (inode_lock -> write_block I/O), so holding it longer adds no new ordering and cannot deadlock.
