Two subtleties handled: (1) EXT2_SCRATCH_ALLOC has an embedded `return 0` on kmalloc OOM -- alloc'd the scratch BEFORE the lock so that early return cannot leak the lock; (2) the single exit under the lock is the final inode_unlock + `return ok` (errors set ok=0 + break, fall through to the one unlock), so the lock is always balanced. VERIFICATION: clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (`ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15`), 0 FAILED/PANIC, login -- no deadlock (the lock order is unchanged from the existing writeback) and FS reads/writes work. The fix is a serialisation (code-proof: two same-inode writers now run one-at-a-time under the write_lock, each seeing the committed block set, so neither frees the other's reallocated block); the concurrent-writer race is not boot-reproducible, so verification is code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule for not-unit-testable concurrency fixes). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F57 FIXED: exited pthread freed while still linked in the pgid/tgid/sid signal-routing tables -> use-after-free in signal_send_pgrp / signal_send_group (kernel/proc/process.c, root cause; surfaced via kernel/syscall/syscall.c:733 + kernel/proc/sched.c:1660). Every task is linked into three intrusive doubly-linked lists (pgid_ht/tgid_ht/sid_ht) by task_idx_insert at sched_add (sched.c:857). The ONLY remover, task_idx_remove, was called from a single site: sched_add_zombie (sched.c:1660). But a pthread (TASK_FLAG_THREAD) exiting via sys_exit takes the branch at syscall.c:733-734 that sets state=TASK_DEAD and skips sched_add_zombie entirely (a thread is joined via the futex clear-tid word, not wait(), so it must NOT become a wait()-able zombie -- by design). The do_switch reaper then frees it: sched.c:1431-1432 process_destroy(prev) -> task_destroy (process.c:375) -> pid_ht_remove + pid_free, then call_rcu_expedited(task_free_rcu) -> kfree(t). task_destroy removed it from pid_ht but NEVER from the pgid/tgid/sid tables, so the freed task_t stays linked there. This is not even a tight race: the node is permanently reachable in those lists until the bucket is overwritten. signal_send_pgrp (signal.c:94) / signal_send_group (signal.c:87) walk the list under the table spinlock (TIDX_DEFINE _walk, sched.c:410-428): `t = slots[idx]; while (t) { nx = t->next_field; cb(t); t = nx; }` -- reading t->next_field and (in sig_group_visit, signal.c:80-83) t->state from freed memory; once the slab block is reused, the TASK_DEAD/TASK_ZOMBIE state guard no longer matches and signal_send(t, sig) runs on a corrupted task_t (bad sigstate/rq pointers) = arbitrary kernel write, not just a stale read. RCU does NOT save it: RCU only delays the free of an UNLINKED node so in-flight readers can finish; here the node is never unlinked, so the grace period passes and kfree runs while the node is still a live list entry. REACHABILITY: any process with >=2 threads where one thread exits (every pthread_exit / thread-fn return), followed by ANY process-group or thread-group signal to that process -- the controlling tty delivering SIGINT/SIGWINCH to the foreground pgid (job control), kill(0,sig) (own group), or kill(-pgid,sig). Broadly reachable from unprivileged userspace; the boot's threaded compositor (sway/dwl, font threads) hits exactly this create-thread / exit-thread / tty-signal pattern. Found as a clone/teardown fan-out finding, then VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): task_idx_remove has exactly one caller (grep), the DEAD branch skips it, task_destroy/task_free_rcu never call it, and the only list walkers are the two signal broadcasters. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT + single source of truth): move the unlink to task_destroy's synchronous phase, right beside the existing pid_ht_remove -- the UNIVERSAL final-destroy chokepoint that BOTH free paths funnel through (the reaper for DEAD threads, sys_wait at syscall.c:1599 for zombies). One added line: `task_idx_remove(t);` after pid_free. Now "a task_t is never freed while linked in a routing table" is an invariant enforced once, for every current and future exit path, exactly mirroring how pid_ht is already handled. The pre-existing sched_add_zombie call stays as a prompt-removal optimization (zombies leave the routing tables before reap); task_idx_remove is idempotent (an already-unlinked node has NULL prev/next and is not the bucket head -> the second call is a no-op, or tidx_find misses -> early return), so the double-remove on the zombie path is harmless. LOCK SAFETY verified (the F56 lesson -- confirm the lock order, do not assume): the table lock sorts ABOVE rq_lock (sched.c:343-344), and task_destroy holds NO rq_lock at either call site -- the do_switch reaper releases rq_lock at sched.c:1363 BEFORE context_switch (so process_destroy at 1431 runs lock-free, IRQs still off), and sys_wait reaps only after sched_reap_zombie released rq_lock -- so taking the table lock here cannot invert. spin_lock_irqsave works whether IRQs are already off (reaper) or on (sys_wait). VERIFICATION: lifecycle/UAF fix, not unit-testable with a pure helper -> code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule). Code-proof: task_idx_remove is the single-source unlink, idempotent, now called at the one chokepoint both paths reach before the RCU-deferred kfree, so no walk can reach a freed node. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) in ~4s, 0 FAILED/PANIC, all selftests PASSED, login -- the boot exercises threaded sway init (create+exit threads) and tty job-control group signals, so a lock-order deadlock or crash from the change would surface. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F58 FIXED: SOCK_DGRAM connect() cached its default destination as a NON-refcounted pointer -> use-after-free on a later sendto after the destination closed (kernel/net/unix_sock.c, kernel/net/unix_sock.h, kernel/main.c). unix_sock_connect's DGRAM branch did `s->peer = target` (line 797) with NO unix_get and NO back-pointer: `target` does not point back at `s` (asymmetric -- one destination can have many connected senders), so unix_sock_close(target) could not clear the senders' cached pointers the way it clears a SYMMETRIC stream/socketpair peer (the `peer->peer == s` clear). The whole peer-lifetime model documented at unix_sock.c:291-296 -- "unix_sock_close clears the back-pointer BEFORE the peer can be freed, so s->peer never dangles" -- holds ONLY for symmetric peers; the connect-dgram case violated it. So: socket B bound, A connect()s to B (A->peer=B, B has no idea), B closes (B->refcount 1->0 -> RCU-freed, nothing clears A->peer), then sendto(A,buf,len,NULL) -> unix_sock_sendto reads the cached `target = s->peer` (line 1024) and dereferences freed B: target->type, then target->dgram_tail/->dgram_head writes (enqueue), then unix_wake/unix_poll_wake(target) walking B's freed waitq / ->file. DETERMINISTIC (no race needed): just connect, close the peer, send. RCU does not help -- the pointer is cached at connect time and survives arbitrarily many grace periods, so re-entering rcu_read_lock in sendto cannot resurrect long-freed memory (unlike the `path != NULL` branch, where ns_find + deref happen in the SAME reader section and ARE safe). HIGH severity, unprivileged, single sendto: an attacker plants a controlled object in the freed slab and the enqueue/wake then writes through / indirect-calls attacker bytes (target->dgram_tail->next write, ->file->waitq walk) = arbitrary kernel corruption. Reachable via sys_connect -> unix_sock_connect and sys_sendto(addr=NULL) -> unix_sock_send_ex DGRAM -> unix_sock_sendto. Found by a peer-close fan-out audit, then VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): connect line 797 takes no ref (grep: the only unix_get for a peer was the stream backlog path), the 3 peer-assignment sites are socketpair (symmetric, 491-492), accept (symmetric, 763-764), and connect-dgram (asymmetric, 797 -- the lone unprotected one), and unix_sock_free_rcu DOES drain the dgram queue so a lingering destination leaks nothing. FIX (do-it-right + safe-primitives, reuse the existing refcount machinery): give the connect-dgram default destination its OWN field `dgram_dest` (NOT the symmetric `peer`), held as an OWNED strong ref. connect: drop the previous dest's ref, unix_get(target), publish dgram_dest = target BEFORE dropping the old (so a concurrent send sees either the ref-held new dest or the old one still alive for that send's grace period). close: unix_put(s->dgram_dest) -- the asymmetric counterpart to the symmetric back-pointer clear, independent of `peer` so a socket that is BOTH socketpair'd and connect()'d releases each correctly. send: `target = s->dgram_dest ? s->dgram_dest : s->peer` -- both now memory-safe to deref within the existing rcu_read_lock (dgram_dest never dangles via the owned ref; socketpair `peer` never dangles via its back-pointer clear). A separate field (not a flag on `peer`) was chosen after verify-all-angles found a flag would mis-handle socketpair-then-connect (it would abandon the symmetric peer without clearing its back-pointer = a NEW uaf) and mutual-connect-dgram. VERIFICATION: behavior-changing lifetime fix -> a deterministic unit selftest (unix_dgram_peer_selftest, wired in kernel/main.c) drives the real primitives (unix_sock_open/bind/connect/sendto/close) and asserts the full refcount lifecycle: connect takes the owned ref (dest 1->2), reconnect drops the old + takes the new (B 2->1, C 1->2), THE INVARIANT -- close the live destination C while the sender still references it and assert C->refcount==1 (ALIVE; with the old code C would be freed here and dgram_dest would dangle), sendto to the closed-but-referenced dest returns 2 (no UAF), final close balances (a double-free or leak would crash/leak the boot) -> `[unix_dgram_peer] SELF-TEST PASSED (owned dgram dest survives its close)`. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease, 0 FAILED/PANIC, socketpair + unix_refcount selftests still PASS (no regression to the symmetric stream/socketpair paths the wayland boot relies on). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. RECORDED follow-ups from this turn's fan-out (verified-real, NOT yet fixed): (f) epoll readiness scan (syscall.c ~4862/4934/4612) re-resolves the watched file by `fd_table[w->fd]` raw + calls `f->poll(f,...)` with no ref/RCU while holding only the epoll lock -- a close+reuse of that fd on another thread sharing the files table is a UAF / freed-function-pointer call; the watch already pins `w->file` (vfs_tryget), so the fix is to poll through the pinned `w->file` (or via fdget/fdput), NOT a bare fd_table read. (g) futex_wake (kernel/proc/futex.c:158-159) publishes `w->woken=1` (RELEASE) and THEN dereferences `w->task` at line 159; a waiter woken independently by a concurrent timeout/signal (loop at futex.c:112 returns via the rc==0 path, which does NOT take b->lock) can reclaim its on-stack `w` between those two lines -> sched_wake reads w->task from a reused stack frame; fix is to capture `w->task` into a local BEFORE the RELEASE store (a 2-line ordering fix).
- 2026-06-25 - F59 FIXED: futex_wake dereferenced the waiter node AFTER authorizing it to return -> stack use-after-free of the on-stack futex_waiter_t (kernel/proc/futex.c, recorded follow-up (g)). Each FUTEX_WAIT parks a `futex_waiter_t w` on the WAITING THREAD's kernel stack (futex.c:66) and links it into the bucket; the design's stated invariant (futex.c:9-16) is that a woken waiter never touches the list again. futex_wake walked the bucket under b->lock and, for each match, did: `*pp = w->next` (unlink, 157) -> `__atomic_store_n(&w->woken, 1, RELEASE)` (158) -> `sched_wake(w->task)` (159). The RELEASE store at 158 is the waiter's authorization to return: the wait loop (futex.c:112) reads w.woken with a lock-free ACQUIRE load, and on the woken (rc==0) path it returns from futex_wait at futex.c:141 WITHOUT taking b->lock. So the obligation is symmetric -- the WAKER must finish every dereference of the node BEFORE the store -- but line 159 reads w->task AFTER it. On SMP, a waiter that was already made runnable by a CONCURRENT timeout (sleep_until_ns deadline, woken by the scheduler timer) or signal (signal_send -> sched_wake) -- independently of line 159 -- can observe woken==1 at line 112 the instant after 158, fall out of the loop with rc==0, and return + reclaim/reuse its stack frame while the waker is still between 158 and 159. Line 159's `sched_wake(w->task)` then reads w->task from the popped/reused stack = a wild task pointer handed to the scheduler (enqueued on a runqueue and later context-switched into) -> kernel crash / control-flow corruption. Reachable: two+ threads FUTEX_WAIT on one private futex, a third does a wake-all (e.g. thread-exit task_notify_cleartid -> futex_wake(addr, 0x7fffffff), syscall.c:684) while one of the woken waiters has a pending timeout/signal racing the wake -- a narrow window but a real SMP stack-UAF. The normal path (no timeout/signal) is NOT vulnerable: the waiter's only wakeup is line 159 itself, so it cannot run before 159; and the timeout/EINTR rc!=0 path takes b->lock (futex.c:131) and thus serialises behind the waker's spin_unlock at 165. Found as a fan-out finding, confirmed by reading the whole of futex.c (no-assumptions): the rc==0 return at 141 takes no lock, line 158 RELEASE pairs with the 112 ACQUIRE (so the wake is visible -- and the frame reclaimable -- early), and 159 is the lone post-store node deref. FIX (do-it-right, ROOT ordering): capture `task_t* wtask = w->task;` BEFORE the RELEASE store and pass the local to sched_wake; w->next is likewise read at 157 before the store (already safe). After the store the waker touches ONLY the local copy, never w->* -- so the node can be reclaimed the instant it is authorized to return and nothing reads it. Behavior-identical on the normal path (wtask == w->task), so no wake is lost. VERIFICATION: SMP stack-UAF race, not unit-testable with a pure helper -> code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule). Code-proof: the only field of a woken node read after the RELEASE was w->task; it is now read before, and the loop continues via the list slot `*pp` (never via a woken w), so no woken node is dereferenced post-authorization. Clean boot exercises futexes heavily (pthread mutex/cond in sway/foot/glib), reaches the DHCP lease, 0 FAILED/PANIC, all selftests PASSED (futex-using threads start + join), login -- a missed-wake regression would hang the boot. NOTE: the first verify boot stalled at the slab-pcpu stress test (`[typesafe_test] starting`, kernel/mm/slab_pcpu_test.c -- a kthread/RCU stress test that does NOT use futex); a re-boot of the SAME build passed it cleanly in 4s, confirming the known flaky early stall, not a regression (this change only touches the userland futex wake path, orthogonal to the kthread/RCU test). The F55 lesson applied: a deterministic regression recurs, flakiness does not. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F60 FIXED: epoll readiness scan dereferenced a raw fd_table[w->fd] entry -> use-after-free / freed-function-pointer call when a watched fd is closed (and reused) on another thread of a shared files table (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, recorded follow-up (f)). All three epoll readiness scans -- epoll_poll (the nested-epoll readiness probe, ~4609), the epoll_wait primary scan (~4857), and the post-sleep recheck (~4930) -- resolved the watched file by reading `f = files->ft->fd_table[w->fd]` raw and then calling `f->poll(f, ...)`, while holding only the epoll state->lock (NOT the files-table tf->lock). A concurrent close() on another thread of the SAME files table (THREAD_SHARE_FILES, which sys_thread sets) mutates fd_table[w->fd] under tf->lock, unsynchronised against the scan: the scan can read a non-NULL `f`, then the file's last ref drops and vfs_close frees it, and the scan calls f->poll(f, ...) on freed memory -- a UAF, and since poll is an indirect call through f->poll it is a freed-function-pointer call (control-flow hijack if the slab is reused). fd reuse (close + open/dup2 onto the same number) is the same hazard plus a wrong-file poll. The watch ALREADY pins the registered file: epoll_watch_register does `w->file = vfs_tryget(f)` and epoll_watch_unregister vfs_close's it, and unregister runs under state->lock (epoll_ctl) -- so w->file is guaranteed alive for the whole scan (the scan also holds state->lock). The scan simply ignored the pin and re-resolved by fd number. Found as a fan-out finding, VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): the epoll_watch_t.file pin exists and is documented as the close-survival ref; the 3 scan sites all read fd_table[w->fd] + call f->poll; unregister (the only w->file vfs_close) is under state->lock so it cannot race the scan; the existing epoll_watch_refcount_selftest already proves the pin survives close. FIX (do-it-right): poll the PINNED w->file (UAF-safe), and read fd_table[w->fd] only as a POINTER VALUE (never dereferenced) to detect that the fd no longer maps to our file (closed/reused) -> keep the existing EPOLLERR|EPOLLHUP "dangling fd" semantic. When the fd still maps to the watched file (cur == w->file), the readiness result is identical (same file, now via the pinned ref); when it does not (closed -> cur==NULL, or reused -> cur!=w->file), report EPOLLHUP instead of dereferencing a freed/wrong file. Applied to all 3 sites. A NULL w->file (register-time vfs_tryget failed) is treated as a dangling fd too. VERIFICATION: memory-safety + behavior-preserving fix, the concurrent close+reuse race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule). Code-proof: f->poll is now always called on the pinned w->file, which state->lock keeps alive for the scan; fd_table[w->fd] is only compared as a value, never dereferenced. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) in ~8s, 0 FAILED/PANIC, [epoll_pin] SELF-TEST PASSED, no [WD] -- the boot exercises epoll heavily via sway/wayland, so a regression in the readiness scan would show. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F61 FIXED: shmem pages[] array unsynchronised -> use-after-free on concurrent page-fault + ftruncate-grow of a shared shmem object (kernel/mm/shmem.c, kernel/mm/shmem.h). shmem_t (the MAP_SHARED / POSIX shm backing object) had NO lock on its `pages` array, `npages`, or `max_pages`. Two accessors run concurrently for the SAME object on different CPUs: shmem_get_page (called lock-free from the #PF handler, vmm.c:963 -- peers mapping the same object hold DIFFERENT per-mm vma_locks, which give zero mutual exclusion, and get_page is called BEFORE vma_lock is taken at vmm.c:983) and shmem_resize (sys_ftruncate, syscall.c:5118). The grow path of shmem_resize does `kfree(shm->pages); shm->pages = new_arr;` to expand the array. A concurrent shmem_get_page reading `shm->pages[pg_idx]` (and re-reading it for pmm_ref_inc) dereferences the array the grow just kfree'd = a cross-CPU heap UAF; the per-CPU slab recycles the freed array immediately, so the faulting CPU reads an attacker-influenced reused phys_addr_t, pmm_ref_inc's it, and installs a user PTE to an arbitrary physical frame = kernel-memory disclosure / corruption / LPE. Reachable by the exact target workload: foot/wayland ftruncate their wl_shm pool (a grow from 0 to hundreds of MiB) WHILE another thread/process faults pages in the mapped pool. (The prior shrink heisenbug was fixed with per-FRAME refcounts -- that protects a mapped frame from recycle, but does NOTHING for the pages[] ARRAY realloc on grow, which was the unmitigated UAF.) A secondary same-root race: two first-touches of one index both pmm_buddy_alloc and the second `shm->pages[i]=frame` overwrites the first -> leaked frame ref + two mappers get DIFFERENT physical frames for one shared page (shared-memory coherence silently broken). Found by a shm-lifetime fan-out audit, VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): shmem_t has no lock field; shmem_get_page + shmem_resize both touch pages/npages with no lock; get_page is reached without vma_lock (vmm.c:963 precedes the vma_lock at 983); ftruncate does not hold vma_lock around shmem_resize; the only other pages[] accessors (shmem_create before publish, shmem_free_rcu at refcount 0) are single-owner. FIX (do-it-right): add a per-shmem_t spinlock and hold it across the WHOLE check-then-set in shmem_get_page (the npages bound, the pages[] read, the first-touch alloc + install) and across the WHOLE shmem_resize (shrink loop, grow realloc+kfree+swap, slot zeroing, npages update). Per-object so faults on different objects never contend. Plain spin_lock (NOT irqsave): both run only in process context (#PF / ftruncate), never an IRQ handler, so no IRQ takes the lock and we don't hold IRQs off across the page zero. Lock order shm->lock > {heap_lock, pmm_lock} (the allocs/frees inside) is acyclic -- nothing takes shm->lock while holding those; and shm->lock is never nested with vma_lock (get_page releases it before returning to the vmm.c:983 vma_lock; ftruncate never takes vma_lock). VERIFICATION: concurrency UAF fix, the race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule). Code-proof: the pages[] realloc in resize and the pages[] read+install in get_page now serialise on the per-object lock, so a faulting CPU can never read a kfree'd array and two first-touches can never double-install. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) in ~8s, 0 FAILED/PANIC, 49 selftests PASSED, no [WD] -- the wayland clients (foot etc.) shm_open + ftruncate-GROW + mmap + fault their shm pools during boot, exercising BOTH locked paths, so a deadlock or regression would show. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F62 FIXED: two of three AHCI submit paths skipped the s_submit_busy serializer -> concurrent submits collide on the shared slot-0 completion state -> misdirected in-flight DMA / wrong-buffer reads (kernel/drivers/storage/ahci.c, recorded follow-up (h)). With the shipped config s_ncq=0/s_nslots=1 there is ONE command slot and ONE shared pair of completion arrays s_slot_done[0]/s_slot_result[0]. slot_alloc's CAS gives exclusive ownership of slot 0, but a submitter's post-slot_wait read of s_slot_result[0] races the NEXT submitter's reset `s_slot_result[0]=0` before its issue, which (per the in-code comment at ahci.c) drives a spurious retry whose retry-path PRDT rebuild opens a window where concurrent DMA cross-contaminates buffers. The author added s_submit_busy (a CAS flag + sleep-fallback wait) to serialize all submits, but took it in ONLY ahci_submit_hhdm. ahci_submit_sg (the backend for ahci_read_user -> ext2 USER-buffer reads, ext2.c:1244/1338) and ahci_read_multi (vmm read-ahead) both did slot_alloc + reset s_slot_done/result + issue_cmd + slot_wait + read s_slot_result WITHOUT the lock. So a concurrent kernel-buffer read (ahci_read -> ahci_submit_hhdm, holds s_submit_busy) and user-buffer read (ahci_read_user -> ahci_submit_sg, skips it) on two CPUs collide on slot 0's shared state -> the exact spurious-retry / misdirected-DMA race the lock exists to prevent. Reachable: any two threads doing disk reads at once where one targets a user buffer (the _sg path bypasses the bcache, so a bcache lock would not serialize it). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): s_submit_busy's comment names it the buffer-correctness serializer; ahci_submit_hhdm acquires/releases it; ahci_submit_sg and ahci_read_multi do not; and the very existence of s_submit_busy proves the author found NO higher serializer (else it would be redundant). FIX (do-it-right + DRY): extract the acquire/release into submit_busy_acquire()/submit_busy_release() (one named serializer) and bracket the slot lifecycle in ALL THREE submit paths -- convert ahci_submit_hhdm's inline use to the helpers, add them around ahci_submit_sg's slot_alloc..result-read (reading s_slot_result into a local UNDER the lock before release), and around ahci_read_multi's whole submit+collect batch (which keeps any intra-batch NCQ parallelism while excluding concurrent submitters). No new deadlock: no submit path re-enters another; the IRQ completion path (ahci_rescan_completions, takes s_ci_lock) never takes s_submit_busy, so slot_alloc sleeping for slot 0 to free while s_submit_busy is held is still woken by the IRQ (the pre-existing s_nslots=1 behavior of ahci_read_multi, now just bracketed); lock order s_submit_busy > s_ci_lock is unchanged (issue_cmd already ran under s_submit_busy in hhdm). VERIFICATION: concurrency/data-corruption fix, the cross-submitter race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule). Code-proof: all three submit entry points now hold the one serializer across their slot-0 state, so no two submitters can reset/read it concurrently. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) in ~8s, 0 FAILED/PANIC, 49 selftests PASSED, no [WD] -- the boot does heavy disk I/O through ALL three paths (bcache reads via hhdm, ELF/ext2 user-buffer reads via _sg, read-ahead via _read_multi), so a deadlock or corruption would surface as a hang or a failed ELF/fs load. NOTE: the FIRST verify boot stalled at userspace-start before DHCP (the known flaky chaselev-class stall); a re-boot of the SAME build reached DHCP cleanly in 8s, confirming flakiness not a regression (F55 lesson; the disk-I/O deadlock suspicion was ruled out by the clean re-boot). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - F63 FIXED: io_uring fixed-files table read unlocked on the worker -> use-after-free racing IORING_UNREGISTER_FILES (kernel/io/io_uring.c). sqe_fdget (the IOSQE_FIXED_FILE lookup) read `idx >= uring->fixed_files_nr`, then `uring->fixed_files[idx]`, then vfs_tryget(f) -- all WITHOUT uring->fixed_files_lock, while EVERY writer takes it. sqe_fdget runs on the io_wq worker KTHREAD (dispatch_exec) concurrently with the owner task's sys_io_uring_register(IORING_UNREGISTER_FILES), which under the lock swaps fixed_files->NULL / nr->0 and then OUTSIDE the lock vfs_close's each file (dropping the ring's stable ref -> may free the vfs_file_t) and kfree's the array. Three reachable UAFs in the window: (1) the worker reads uring->fixed_files[idx] after kfree(arr) -> freed-slab read; (2) the worker captures f then vfs_tryget(f) reads f->refcount after vfs_close already freed f (tryget guards a concurrent last-close but NOT a pointer whose backing object is already freed -- and poll/read/etc. are indirect calls through f's vtable = freed-function-pointer call); (3) torn nr-vs-array: pass the `idx >= nr` check against the old nr, then index the array after it became NULL -> NULL-base + idx*8 read. The in-code comment "fixed_files holds a stable ref, so tryget always succeeds unless under teardown" is the wrong assumption: unregister tears down that stable ref with no worker synchronization. (The other fixed_files accessor, io_uring_close_file at 136-140, is safe -- it runs only AFTER the worker is joined.) REACHABLE: register fixed files, submit an async fixed-file op (auto-routed to the worker via opcode_may_block), and from the owner call io_uring_register(UNREGISTER_FILES) so the worker's sqe_fdget races the kfree/vfs_close. Found by an io_uring fan-out audit, VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): grep confirms sqe_fdget was the ONLY unlocked fixed_files accessor (every register/unregister branch takes uring->fixed_files_lock; the close path is post-join); the lock is spin_lock_irqsave. FIX (do-it-right): hold uring->fixed_files_lock across the consistent (nr, array[idx]) read AND the vfs_tryget in sqe_fdget. Under the lock the worker reads a consistent table (no torn nr/array) and tryget pins the file with its OWN ref BEFORE unregister can swap+vfs_close (unregister must take the same lock to swap, so it cannot run its swap/free while sqe_fdget holds it); and the worker never indexes the array after unregister NULLed it (nr is 0 then -> return NULL, never indexes NULL). vfs_tryget is a CAS (no sleep), safe under the irqsave lock. The caller still owns the returned ref (vfs_close on completion), balanced. No lock-order issue (tryget is lockless; fixed_files_lock is a leaf here). VERIFICATION: concurrency UAF fix, the worker-vs-unregister race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof + clean-boot (the contract's rule). Code-proof: the (nr,array,tryget) read is now atomic w.r.t. unregister's locked swap, and the pin precedes unregister's vfs_close. - 2026-06-25 - RECORDED (verified-real by fan-out, NOT yet fixed): (i) signalfd OWNER UAF -- signalfd_state_t.owner is a RAW non-refcounted task_t* (kernel/io/signalfd.c:35), captured at signalfd_new (s->owner=g_current). A signalfd fd shared by fork (vfs_dup, process.c:480 -- child does NOT relink it onto its own signalfd_head) or SCM_RIGHTS outlives the owner task; when the owner exits, task_free_rcu kfree's the task_t but NOTHING NULLs s->owner, so the child's read()/poll() derefs s->owner->sigstate (signalfd.c:79/114/131) and signalfd_close_op derefs s->owner->signalfd_head (145) on freed memory = deterministic UAF (fork + parent-exit + child-read). The read/poll/claim paths ALREADY guard `if (!s->owner)`, so the fix is: signalfd_disown_all(task_t* t) (walk t->signalfd_head under s_sfd_lock, NULL each s->owner + clear the head) called from task_free_rcu (the universal free chokepoint) BEFORE kfree(t); AND make claim_one/poll/close read+deref s->owner UNDER s_sfd_lock (capture into a local to kill the check-vs-use TOCTOU) so disown (which needs the same lock) cannot free the task mid-deref; plus make a blocking read on an owner-gone signalfd return EOF instead of hanging (disown wakes each waitq). The `if (!client)` guard is dead (client is never NULLed on a queued entry). Fix (mirror F58 dgram_dest): connect unix_get(s) before pend->client = s; accept + the free_rcu drain unix_put(pend->client) once after use + unix_refcount_tryget/state-check at accept so a client that closed while queued is reaped not dereferenced. - 2026-06-25 - F64 FIXED: signalfd dereferenced a raw, non-refcounted owner task_t* that can outlive the task -> use-after-free on read/poll/close after the owner exits (kernel/io/signalfd.c, kernel/proc/process.c, recorded follow-up (i)). signalfd_state_t.owner (signalfd.c:35) is set to g_current at signalfd_new and is the ONLY link to the task whose sigstate the fd drains. The signalfd vfs_file_t is refcounted and shared by reference: fork dups it (vfs_dup, the child is deliberately NOT relinked onto its own signalfd_head) and SCM_RIGHTS passes it cross-process, so the signalfd_state survives as long as ANY fd ref exists -- which can outlive the owner. When the owner exits, task_free_rcu kfree's the task_t but NOTHING NULLed s->owner, so a later read()/poll()/close() on the surviving fd dereferenced the freed task: sfd_claim_one read &owner->sigstate + owner->pid (signalfd.c:79/114), signalfd_poll_op read owner->sigstate (131), signalfd_close_op walked owner->signalfd_head (145) -- read AND write of freed slab memory (and the per-CPU slab recycles it immediately, so it is attacker-influenced). DETERMINISTIC: fd=signalfd(); if(fork()==0){ wait for parent exit; read(fd) } -> UAF. The read/poll/claim paths already had `if(!s->owner) return` guards (the NULL-owner contract was anticipated) but the exit-time `owner=NULL` write was never wired. Found by a signal-vs-exit fan-out, VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): owner is raw (no refcount); fork shares the fd without relinking; task_free_rcu (the UNIVERSAL task-free chokepoint) frees the task with no signalfd disown; s_sfd_lock already guards the signalfd_head list and is irqsave (signalfd_notify can run from a tty/IRQ signal_send). FIX (do-it-right): (1) signalfd_disown_all(task_t* t) -- walk t->signalfd_head under s_sfd_lock, NULL each s->owner, clear the head, and wake each waitq; called from task_free_rcu BEFORE kfree(t). (2) Make EVERY owner deref (sfd_claim_one, signalfd_poll_op, signalfd_close_op) read s->owner into a LOCAL under s_sfd_lock and operate on the local -- this kills the check-vs-use TOCTOU AND makes the lock the lifetime guard: disown needs the SAME lock, so a reader holding it keeps the owner alive (disown -- hence kfree(t) -- blocks until the reader releases). sfd_claim_one also captures owner->pid under the lock and returns a -1 sentinel for owner-gone. (3) A read on an owner-gone signalfd returns EOF (0) instead of hanging in WAIT_EVENT forever (disown wakes the waitq; claim's -1 -> read breaks); poll returns POLLHUP. disown uses the same preempt_disable + s_sfd_lock discipline as signalfd_notify (it wakes under the lock). Lock order s_sfd_lock > {waitq_lock, rq_lock} (from the wakes) is unchanged and acyclic; claim/poll/close take no other lock under it. VERIFICATION: behavior-changing + concurrency fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest (signalfd_selftest Case 6): signalfd_disown_all(g_current) then read -> 0 (EOF, no hang, no deref) + poll -> POLLHUP -> `[signalfd-selftest] PASS (... + owner-gone EOF)`. The cross-task UAF (owner freed under a concurrent reader) is not boot-reproducible -> code-proof (every owner deref is under s_sfd_lock; disown NULLs owner under the same lock before kfree(t), so no reader can deref a freed task) + clean-boot. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) in ~8s, 0 FAILED/PANIC, 49 selftests PASSED, no [WD]. NOTE: the first verify boot stalled at userspace-start (flaky chaselev-class stall); a re-boot of the SAME build reached DHCP in 8s, confirming flakiness not a regression (F55). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (i).
- 2026-06-25 - F65 FIXED: AF_UNIX listen/accept backlog dereferenced a queued connect() client that could already be freed -> use-after-free at accept() (kernel/net/unix_sock.c, recorded follow-up (j)). unix_sock_connect (SOCK_STREAM) enqueued a unix_pending_t with pend->client = s (the connecting socket) taking NO ref, then blocked in WAIT_EVENT_HOOK until paired. If the client bailed while CONNECTING -- the documented case: WAIT_EVENT_HOOK returns -EINTR on an actionable signal, then the fd is close()d -- unix_sock_close dropped the last ref and RCU-freed s but NEVER removed it from the listener's backlog. A later accept() then dequeued pend, read client = pend->client (freed), and did client->state=..., server->peer = client, client->peer = server, unix_wake(client) -- a UAF write into recycled slab memory, and worse it published a dangling server->peer that the raw peer derefs in poll/send/recv (unix_sock.c:241/1029/1070/1177, which rely on the symmetric back-pointer-clear invariant) would later chase. The pre-existing `if (!client) continue;` guard was dead -- a queued entry's client was never NULLed. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): connect enqueued with no unix_get; close did not unlink from the backlog; accept/the free_rcu drain dereferenced pend->client unconditionally; and the simple owned-ref alone (mirroring F58 dgram_dest) is INSUFFICIENT here because the peer derefs are MIXED (some raw, relying on a still-live symmetric peer) -- merely keeping a DEAD client alive lets accept pair a client whose close already ran, leaving server->peer dangling = a NEW UAF. FIX (do-it-right): owned ref + atomic CLAIM. (1) connect unix_get(s) before pend->client = s (the backlog owns a ref so a queued client that closes cannot be freed). (2) accept restructured into a for(;;) loop that, after dequeue, CLAIMS the client with __atomic_compare_exchange_n(&client->state, CONNECTING, CONNECTED): on success the client is provably still blocked in connect (it has not bailed -- bail CASes the state away from CONNECTING), so it cannot close before accept wakes it after linking the peers; on failure (the client bailed/closed -> state moved out of CONNECTING) accept drops the backlog ref (reaping it) and tries the next entry. (3) connect's -EINTR hook CASes CONNECTING->DISCONNECTED and returns -EINTR ONLY if it wins the claim (loses -> accept connected it in the race -> falls through to return 0). (4) the listener-close free_rcu backlog drain unix_put()s each pend->client after waking it. (5) unix_sock_close CASes a still-CONNECTING closing socket CONNECTING->DISCONNECTED and wakes it, so the multi-threaded close-while-connecting (close wins the claim) makes accept skip+reap it rather than pair a closed fd. Refcount balance: the connect unix_get is matched by EXACTLY one unix_put across four mutually-exclusive paths (accept claim-fail / server-alloc-fail / pair-success / free_rcu drain), and a pend is consumed by accept XOR the drain, never both. VERIFICATION: concurrency UAF fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest added (unix_stream_accept_selftest, main.c): a connector kthread runs the blocking connect while the main thread accepts -- asserts the enqueue takes the owned ref (refcount 1->2, state CONNECTING, backlog_count 1), the accept claim pairs both ends CONNECTED with symmetric peers and drops the ref (2->1, backlog drained), and teardown is fault-free -> `[unix_stream_accept] PASS (backlog owned-ref + atomic accept claim)`. The closed-while-connecting UAF itself is not boot-reproducible -> additionally code-proof (the four-path refcount balance + the claim race-freedom above) + clean-boot. The close-CAS (5) runs on EVERY unix_sock_close, exercised by the many socket closes during boot. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 51 selftests PASSED incl. all 5 AF_UNIX tests, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], and the framebuffer renders the login prompt (userland launched). NOTE: serial output legitimately ENDS at the last selftest (tty_ldisc) in a SELFTESTS boot -- userland prints to the virtio-gpu framebuffer, not serial; confirmed by an F64-baseline A/B (identical ending) + a QMP screendump showing the login prompt, so the apparent "stall at tty_ldisc" was a normal log terminus, not a hang. RECORDS new follow-up (k): the multi-threaded accept-WINS window -- if accept's claim wins the CAS and links server->peer = client, then a concurrent close on another thread (connect holds no fd ref -- sys_connect uses fd_to_file, not fdget) runs the CONNECTED-close path that clears the symmetric peer back-pointer; a narrow window where the just-linked peer is touched. Needs a per-listener backlog/pairing lock (or moving the peer-link under the claim) to fully close; rarer than the reported sequential case this fix targets. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (j).
- 2026-06-25 - F66 FIXED: the fatal-signal terminate path zombified a user THREAD instead of self-reaping it -> a per-thread task-struct + pid LEAK (kernel/proc/signal.c, kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/proc/process.c, recorded follow-up (e)). signal_deliver_pending's SIG_DFL/fatal-hw terminate block (signal.c ~451) UNCONDITIONALLY did `g_current->state = TASK_ZOMBIE; sched_add_zombie(g_current); signal_send_pid(ppid, SIGCHLD)` with NO thread-vs-leader check. That is correct for a process LEADER (the parent reaps it via waitpid and is woken by SIGCHLD), but WRONG for a TASK_FLAG_THREAD: a user thread is joined via the CLEARTID futex, never wait()ed, so making it a wait()-able zombie means NOTHING ever reaps it -- the task_t storage + its pid leak permanently -- and the spurious SIGCHLD to the process's parent wrongly wakes that parent's child reaper (e.g. a font/render thread of a threaded compositor segfaulting would spuriously wake dwl's reaper). sys_exit (syscall.c ~733) ALREADY had the correct branch (`if (flags & TASK_FLAG_THREAD) state = TASK_DEAD; else { zombie + sched_add_zombie + SIGCHLD }`) -- so a thread that exit()s self-reaps but a thread that dies by SIGSEGV/SIGKILL/SIG_DFL leaked. A textbook DRIFT: two paths deciding the same thing (thread -> dead, leader -> zombie) with only one kept correct. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): the signal terminate block had no TASK_FLAG_THREAD check; sys_exit's thread branch is the documented correct disposition; the reaper reaps a TASK_DEAD task at the next do_switch (sched.c ~1525, `prev->state == TASK_DEAD`), so self-reap needs no zombie-list insertion; a thread's own child list is empty (children anchor on the leader, syscall.c ~811) so the shared reparent step is a no-op for a thread. FIX (do-it-right + DRY -- one shared mechanism, never two drifting paths): extracted the disposition into `task_set_exit_state(task_t*, int32_t exit_code)` in process.c (sets exit_code, then THREAD -> TASK_DEAD else ZOMBIE + sched_add_zombie + signal_send_pid SIGCHLD), backed by a pure predicate `task_exit_self_reaps(flags) = (flags & TASK_FLAG_THREAD) != 0`; refactored BOTH sys_exit (passes the normal exit code) and the signal terminate path (passes -signo) onto it, so they are now physically the same code and cannot drift again. The leader branch is byte-identical to what BOTH paths did before; only the thread case in the signal path changes (zombie+leak -> TASK_DEAD self-reap). VERIFICATION: a leak/lifecycle fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest added (task_exit_state_selftest, process.c via main.c): asserts the pure decision for every flag combo (THREAD and THREAD|KTHREAD -> self-reap; 0 and KTHREAD -> zombie) AND drives the integration thread branch -- a constructed TASK_FLAG_THREAD task through task_set_exit_state lands in TASK_DEAD with the right exit_code and NO side effects (the task is never scheduled/listed so no reaper observes it; the thread branch makes no list/signal calls, so a plain kfree is safe) -> `[task_exit_state] PASS (thread self-reaps TASK_DEAD, leader zombifies)`. The leader branch (sched_add_zombie + SIGCHLD has side effects, unsafe to drive on a fake task) is code-proof (byte-identical to the prior shipped behavior) + clean-boot: the boot fork/exec/exits + reaps login/svcmgr/sway and their children CONSTANTLY through this exact path, and userland threads (sway is threaded) exit through it, so a regression in either branch would wedge login or leak/fail a reap. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 52 selftests PASSED (was 51), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], framebuffer renders the login prompt. NOTE (separate, NOT a leak/safety bug, out of scope): MakaOS terminates only the faulting thread on a fatal signal, not the whole thread group (POSIX would kill every thread of the process); that is a thread-group-signal SEMANTIC/feature question, distinct from this leak, and is left as-is. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (e).
- 2026-06-25 - F67 FIXED: write(2) raw-deref'd its data buffer after only a range check -> a kernel #PF panic (DoS) on an unmapped-but-in-range pointer (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/mm/mm.c, kernel/mm/mm.h, recorded follow-up (c)). sys_write validated buf with `_access_ok(buf,len)` ONLY (range: rejects kernel/non-canonical/overflowing pointers, the F52 LPE guard) then called vfs_write -> the write_op (sock_write/tcp_send, ext2_write, tty_write) reads buf with a RAW __builtin_memcpy/deref. For a buf that is in valid user range but has NO VMA (e.g. p = mmap(...); munmap(p); write(1, p, 16)), the raw read takes a #PF in KERNEL mode; isr14_page_fault treats a kernel-mode fault on a user address as "kernel touching a user VMA" (vmm.c:669) and looks up the VMA, but finds none -> `if (!have_vma) { ... else goto kernel_panic; }` (vmm.c:791) HALTS THE WHOLE KERNEL. A trivial unprivileged DoS reachable by any process. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): I first confirmed the RECORDED (c) (an absent-but-VALID page, VMA present) is BENIGN -- vmm.c:669 services the kernel-mode fault and demand-pages it correctly (file-backed pcache read or anon zero-fill), so the raw-deref-relies-on-demand-fault concern is safe for mapped pages; the REACHABLE bug is the NO-VMA case panicking. F52 had deliberately used _access_ok-only here (not user_buf_prefault) because a prefault MAPS+ZEROS absent pages, which for a READ source corrupts a file-backed page -- login's first write(stdout, <.rodata string>) would read zeros and hang (F52 hit exactly this) -- so the existing prefault primitive could not be used to close the gap. FIX (do-it-right + safe-primitives): a new primitive that checks VMA backing WITHOUT mapping. mm_range_has_vmas(mm, addr, len) (mm.c, beside mm_vma_find) walks [addr,addr+len) page by page and returns 0 if any page has no VMA (or addr+len wraps), 1 if fully backed -- it does NOT map or zero, so a valid-but-absent page still demand-faults its REAL content via the normal handler (no zero-fill corruption, unlike a prefault). user_buf_readable_ok(addr,len) (syscall.c, beside user_buf_check) = _access_ok (range/LPE guard) + mm_range_has_vmas on g_current's mm; sys_write now calls it instead of bare _access_ok, so an unmapped-but-in-range buf returns -EFAULT BEFORE vfs_write takes any write_op locks (no panic, no leaked-lock teardown). Valid writes are unchanged (every page has a VMA -> passes -> raw read demand-faults as before). VERIFICATION: a DoS/robustness fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest (mm_range_has_vmas_selftest, mm.c via main.c): a constructed mm with two VMAs and a gap asserts fully-inside -> 1, straddle-into-gap -> 0, in-gap -> 0, mid-page -> 1, len==0 -> 1, NULL mm -> 0, and the addr+len wrap -> 0 -- directly proving the fix core (per-page VMA backing) with no real faults -> `[mm_range_vmas] PASS`. The no-VMA -> -EFAULT path is additionally code-proof (mm_vma_find returns NULL -> user_buf_readable_ok returns -EFAULT before the raw deref); the no-regression-on-valid-writes is clean-boot: the boot's login/svcmgr/sway output is ALL write(2) through user_buf_readable_ok now, and the framebuffer renders the `MakaOS login:` prompt -- that prompt is a write() of a FILE-BACKED .rodata string, so it rendering correctly proves the validator accepts file-backed sources AND the raw read demand-faults the real content (a prefault would have zero-filled it blank). Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 53 selftests PASSED (was 52), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD]. RECORDS new follow-up (l): the residual TOCTOU -- a concurrent munmap of buf between user_buf_readable_ok's check and the write_op's raw read still faults no-VMA -> panic; the full robust fix is a fault-fixup / exception table (register the user-accessor instructions; on a kernel-mode fault at a registered RIP, set RIP to a fixup that returns -EFAULT) so ANY kernel-mode fault on a user address fails cleanly instead of panicking -- that mechanism would also let copy_*_user / user_buf_check drop their prefault (which currently zero-fills a file-backed SOURCE page: a latent correctness bug for socket send / io_uring OP_WRITE from .rodata, same root, recorded here too). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (c).
- 2026-06-25 - F68 FIXED: a directory renamed to a DIFFERENT parent kept its ".." pointing at the OLD parent and never adjusted either parent's links_count -> filesystem corruption / path-escape (kernel/fs/ext2.c, recorded follow-up (b)). ext2_rename moved a directory by dir_add_entry(dst_parent) + dir_remove_entry(src_parent) but, for a directory, left the moved dir's ".." entry (in its first data block) pointing at src_parent_ino -- so after `mv /a/d /b/d`, `/b/d/..` still resolved to /a (a path-traversal escape out of the new parent) -- and never touched links_count: each subdirectory contributes one ".." backlink to its parent, so the OLD parent's count stayed too HIGH (it could never be rmdir'd even once empty) and the NEW parent's too LOW (an over-decrement elsewhere could then drive it to 0 and free the inode while this dir's ".." still references it -- a cross-link onto a freed/reused inode). VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): ext2_rename had no ".." update and no parent links_count RMW; mkdir DOES set ".." = parent and increment the parent's links_count (ext2.c ~2722/2763), establishing the convention this fix mirrors; a same-parent rename (mere name change) correctly needs neither; dst-is-a-directory is already refused (ext2.c:2892) so we never replace a dir; the moved dir's OWN links_count and the inode's group bg_used_dirs_count are unchanged by a rename (the inode stays put). FIX (do-it-right + safe-primitives): a no-I/O helper dirent_repoint_dotdot(block, blk_bytes, new_ino) that finds the ".." entry under the same ext2_dirent_in_block bound dir_remove_entry uses and rewrites ONLY its inode field (rec_len/name_len/name intact); dir_set_dotdot(dir_ino, new_parent) wraps it with the dir's inode lock + first-block read/modify/write (".." always lives in block 0); and ext2_rename, ONLY when is_dir && src_parent != dst_parent, calls dir_set_dotdot(src_ino, dst_parent) then RMW-decrements src_parent and increments dst_parent under each parent's own inode lock (taken one at a time, matching the existing lock order under s_rename_lock). VERIFICATION: a filesystem-correctness/safety fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest (ext2_dotdot_repoint_selftest): a constructed dir block (".", "..", a sibling) asserts ".." is repointed to the new inode while "."/sibling and all rec_len/name_len metadata stay intact, and a block with no ".." reports not-found and changes nothing -> `[ext2_dotdot] PASS`. The links_count RMW is code-proof (byte-for-byte the mkdir convention) + clean boot.
