WHILE investigating I did find and fix a real latent hazard the selftest introduced: it stack-allocated `uint8_t blk[4096]`, but the kernel stack is only 8KiB (KSTACK_PAGES=2) and every dir-block buffer in ext2.c is kmalloc'd for exactly that reason -- the selftest now kmalloc's it too (whether that 4KiB frame caused any of the specific stalls is unproven/confounded by the flaky stall, but a half-kstack frame is a hazard worth removing regardless). Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 54 selftests PASSED (was 53), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders. RECORDS new follow-up (m): ext2_rename does not reject renaming a directory INTO ITS OWN SUBTREE (`mv /a /a/b`) -- POSIX requires EINVAL; without it the moved dir's ".." (now repointed) creates a detached cycle / orphaned subtree. A normalized-path ancestor check (dst == src or dst starts with src + "/") in sys_rename or ext2_rename closes it; distinct from this metadata fix. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (b).
- 2026-06-25 - F69 FIXED: rename() accepted two overlapping src/dst cases that corrupt the filesystem -- a directory moved INTO ITS OWN SUBTREE, and a path renamed onto ITSELF / a hard-link sibling (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, kernel/fs/ext2.c, recorded follow-up (m)). (1) `mv /a /a/b`: ext2_rename added /a/b -> /a's inode and removed /a from its real parent; with F68 now repointing ".." too, /a's subtree becomes an unreachable cycle (/a/b -> /a -> /a/b ...) detached from root -- the inodes leak (no path, links_count>0) and a path walk of /a/b/b/b/... loops forever. POSIX requires EINVAL ("make a directory a subdirectory of itself"). (2) `mv /a/f /a/f` (or two hard links to one inode): dst_ino == src_ino, but ext2_rename's dst-exists branch UNLINKS dst first -- free_inode_blocks + i_links_count=0 + free_inode_num(F) -- and THEN dir_add_entry re-adds the name pointing at the just-freed inode F: data loss + a dirent dangling onto a freed/reused inode. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): sys_rename normalizes both paths but had no src-vs-dst relation check; ext2_rename refuses dst-is-a-dir (so the subtree case reaches it with dst_ino==0, i.e. only the STRING relation catches it) but had no same-inode guard before the dst-unlink (so self/hard-link rename hits the free-then-re-add). FIX (do-it-right, the natural layer for each): (a) a pure path_dst_under_src(src,dst) (a single prefix walk with a trailing-'/' boundary so "/abc" is not "under" "/ab", and equal is NOT "under") gates sys_rename -> -EINVAL when dst is a proper descendant of src; (b) ext2_rename returns success-noop the instant `dst_ino && dst_ino == src_ino` (covers self AND hard-link-sibling, exactly POSIX's "existing hard links referring to the same file -> do nothing, succeed"), BEFORE the dst-unlink. The subtree case has dst_ino==0 so (b) does not mask it; (a) and (b) are disjoint and complete. VERIFICATION: an fs-corruption fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest (rename_under_selftest): path_dst_under_src over child/grandchild/longer-name -> under; equal/sibling-prefix/ancestor/unrelated/sibling-at-depth/name-repeated -> not-under -> `[rename_under] SELF-TEST PASSED`. The same-inode no-op is code-proof (a 1-line identity guard before the destructive unlink) + clean boot. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) FIRST try, 55 selftests PASSED (was 54), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (m).
- 2026-06-25 - F70 FIXED: AF_UNIX accept() linked the peer pointers without serializing against a concurrent close() of the client -> server->peer dangles to a freed socket (kernel/net/unix_sock.c, recorded follow-up (k)). F65 closed the SEQUENTIAL backlog-client UAF with a CAS-claim (client CONNECTING -> CONNECTED) + an owned ref, reasoning "on success the client is provably still blocked in connect(), so it cannot close before we wake it." That holds for the connect THREAD itself, but NOT for a DIFFERENT thread of the same process closing the shared fd (connect uses fd_to_file, taking no vfs_file ref). The window: accept CAS-claims (publishes CONNECTED at line ~991), THEN allocates the server (unix_sock_open) and sets server->peer = client / client->peer = server (~1010-1011). A concurrent unix_sock_close(client) sees state==CONNECTED (its own CONNECTING->DISCONNECTED CAS fails) and runs the CONNECTED-close symmetric back-pointer clear, reading client->peer -- but if it reads BEFORE accept's link (client->peer still NULL) it clears nothing, then accept links server->peer = client, and once the client's refs drop (close's fd ref + accept's backlog unix_put) the client is RCU-freed while server->peer still points at it -> a later send/recv/poll on the server unix_pin_peer's a freed socket (tryget on freed slab) = UAF. The root flaw: the state-claim and the peer-link were not ATOMIC, so "state == CONNECTED" did not imply "peers linked", and close could interleave between them. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): accept's CAS and link are separate statements with unix_sock_open between; close's peer-clear reads client->peer with no lock; the symmetric-clear-before-free invariant unix_pin_peer relies on is exactly what the interleave breaks. FIX (do-it-right -- one shared mechanism): a single leaf spinlock s_unix_pair_lock serializes the WHOLE pairing state machine -- accept's [claim + peer-link] as one indivisible unit, close's CONNECTING-bail, close's CONNECTED peer-clear, connect's -EINTR bail, and the listener-close backlog drain. With it, a close that observes the client is "CONNECTED" necessarily observes the fully-linked pair (and clears server->peer); a close that wins the race sees CONNECTING and bails, and accept's locked claim then fails and reaps. Because state-claim and peer-link are now atomic, the CAS is replaced by a plain locked check-and-set (mixing a lockless CAS with a locked claim would reopen the window). The server is allocated OUTSIDE the lock (unix_sock_open) and on a lost claim is torn down (unix_sock_close) + the backlog ref dropped; every alloc/wake/put happens outside the lock, so it is a true leaf (no nesting -> no deadlock: verified the WAIT_EVENT_HOOK bail runs AFTER task_we_remove with no waitq lock held, and unix_pin_peer under the lock only does rcu+tryget). Refcount accounting unchanged (exactly one unix_put per connect unix_get across pre-check-skip / server-alloc-fail / claim-fail / claim-success / drain). VERIFICATION: concurrency UAF fix; the close-vs-accept race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof (the lock makes claim+link atomic vs the peer-clear) + clean-boot + the existing deterministic unix_stream_accept_selftest (the two-kthread connect/accept rendezvous) STILL passes under the new lock, proving the happy path. Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), all 5 AF_UNIX selftests PASS, 55 selftests total, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders -- and crucially userspace start drives wayland's heavy concurrent AF_UNIX connect/accept/close through the locked paths, so a deadlock would hang the boot (it does not: 2 of 3 boots reach DHCP, the 1 stall being the known flaky F55 userspace-start stall, confirmed by a same-build re-boot reaching DHCP). Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (k).
- 2026-06-25 - F71 FIXED: execve/spawn raw-dereferenced the user argv/envp pointer ARRAYS and every element STRING pointer with zero validation -> kernel panic (DoS) + arbitrary-kernel-memory read into the child (info leak / LPE) (kernel/syscall/syscall.c). sys_exec (argv ~890, envp ~910) and sys_spawn (argv ~1242, envp ~1264) did `const uint64_t* uargv = (const uint64_t*)argv_ptr; uint64_t ustr = uargv[argc];` -- a raw read of the user array -- then `const char* s = (const char*)ustr; while (s[l]) l++; memcpy(ks, s, l);` -- a raw deref of the FULLY attacker-controlled 64-bit element value. None of argv_ptr/envp_ptr, the array slots, or the string pointers passed through _access_ok / copy_from_user. Two reachable unprivileged attacks: (1) execve("/bin/sh", KADDR, 0) or an element argv[i]=KADDR points the copy at KERNEL memory -> the kernel reads kernel bytes and lays them into the child's argv on its user stack = arbitrary kernel-memory disclosure; (2) argv (or argv[i]) = an in-range but UNMAPPED user pointer (p=mmap;munmap(p)) -> the raw read takes a kernel-mode #PF with no covering VMA -> isr14_page_fault goto kernel_panic (the F67 class) = reliable kernel DoS. sys_spawn additionally raw-deref'd stdio_ptr (`stdio[i]=us[i]`) and used _access_ok+raw-memcpy (not copy_from_user) for spawn_attr -- same class. The kernel's own documented contract (every user pointer the kernel derefs goes through _access_ok + copy_*_user, as sys_open/read/write/stat already do) was simply not applied to the exec/spawn argument vectors; copy_path_from_user guarded only the PATH. VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): read both functions' loops (raw uargv[i] + s[l] + memcpy, no guard), confirmed SYS_EXEC/SYS_SPAWN are live dispatch entries, confirmed the panic/leak fault semantics in isr14. FIX (do-it-right + DRY -- one shared mechanism for the two drifting copies): a single safe primitive copy_user_strv(uvec, out[], max, arglen, scratch, &count) that reads each array slot via copy_from_user and each string via copy_path_from_user (so a kernel/non-canonical/unmapped/wrapping array OR element pointer returns -EFAULT, never a raw deref), kmalloc's each string, frees its own partial vector on any error, and uses a single kstack-OFF scratch buffer (kmalloc, per the F68 8KiB-kstack lesson). BOTH sys_exec and sys_spawn now route argv+envp through it; sys_spawn's stdio uses copy_from_user and spawn_attr uses copy_from_user (was _access_ok+memcpy). VERIFICATION: a deterministic DoS/leak fix. DETERMINISTIC selftest (copy_user_strv_selftest): a kernel-HHDM, a non-canonical, and a past-user-ceiling vector pointer must each return -EFAULT with count 0 and out[0]=NULL (rejected BEFORE any deref), and a NULL vector is the legitimate empty case -> `[strv_test] SELF-TEST PASSED`. The success path + per-element string validation need a live user mm so they are code-proof (copy_from_user / copy_path_from_user are the already-selftested safe primitives) + clean-boot: every process the boot launches (login, svcmgr, bash, sway and its clients) exec/spawns through copy_user_strv with a real argv/envp, so a regression that mangled valid argument copying would fail to start userland -- instead the boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first try, 56 selftests PASSED (was 55), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], and the login prompt renders. Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-25 - RECORDED (reported by a read-only fan-out audit, HIGH confidence each, NOT yet independently verified -- VERIFY against the real code before fixing): (n) sys_brk HEAP-SHRINK frees frames BEFORE the cross-CPU TLB shootdown (syscall.c ~635-668: vmm_page_unmap local-invlpg-only + pmm_ref_dec in the loop, then tlb_flush_range after) -- unlike sys_munmap/MAP_FIXED which route through mm_unmap_range_flush_free (flush-then-free); a sibling THREAD_SHARE_MM thread on another CPU keeps a stale writable TLB entry and writes into the freed+reused frame -> cross-owner UAF write / LPE. Fix: route brk shrink through mm_unmap_range_flush_free. (o) PTY pair lifetime (pty.c: master_open / slave_open_count / s_pty_head) has NO lock; concurrent close() of the master and slave ends (CLONE_FILES, two CPUs) both reach the "peer count==0 -> pty_free_locked -> kfree(pty)" decision -> double-free / UAF of the pty_t (pty_free_locked is misnamed -- holds no lock). Fix: one lock around the flag-flip + free-decision in both close ops (and the s_pty_head insert/walk). (p) AF_INET TCP child PCB's raw ->listener backpointer (tcp.c:410) is never cleared/reparented when the listener is freed on close (socket.c close -> tcp_pcb_free -> call_rcu_expedited synchronous free); a later handshake ACK drives tcp_recv's SYN_RCVD case to lock+accept_q_push+wake through the dangling listener (tcp.c ~427-433) -> remote-timed kernel heap UAF write. Fix: refcount the listener from SYN_RCVD children, or walk+NULL children's ->listener on listener teardown, or re-lookup the listener under RCU in the ACK path. (q) sys_poll/sys_select register an on-stack task_we_t on f->waitq WITHOUT pinning f (syscall.c ~4320/4416), unlike epoll which vfs_tryget-pins (F60); a concurrent close() on a THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling frees the file + its embedded wait queue, so the woken poller's wait_group_cleanup -> wq_remove writes/walks freed memory -> UAF. Fix: vfs_tryget-pin each polled file across the register->sleep->cleanup window (mirror epoll), defer the fd-state free via call_rcu. All four are the same lifetime/ordering bug classes this log already fixed elsewhere (F57/F58/F59/F60/F64/F65/F70), just in un-swept subsystems.
- 2026-06-25 - F72 FIXED: sys_brk heap-shrink freed physical frames BEFORE the cross-CPU TLB shootdown -> a sibling thread's stale writable TLB entry writes into a freed+reused frame (cross-owner UAF / LPE) (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, recorded follow-up (n)). The shrink path open-coded `for (page = new_brk; page < old_brk) { if (vmm_page_unmap(pml4, page, &frame)) pmm_ref_dec(frame); }` then issued `tlb_flush_range(new_brk, old_brk)` only AFTER the loop (and after the VMA shrink).  vmm_page_unmap does a LOCAL-only invlpg (no IPI) and pmm_ref_dec returns the frame to the buddy allocator the instant the refcount hits 0 (the common case for a thread's own touched heap page).  So in a multithreaded process (sys_thread + THREAD_SHARE_MM shares the mm/pml4 across CPUs), a sibling on another CPU that still holds a stale WRITABLE TLB entry for a just-freed page can write into that frame after it has been handed back to the buddy allocator and reallocated + zero-filled for a new owner (another thread's stack, a page-table page, slab, DMA target) -- heap-wide cross-owner corruption / LPE, reachable by any unprivileged process: thread B busy-writes a high heap page (caching a writable TLB entry on CPU B), thread A brk(lower) frees it, B's stale entry writes the reused frame before the shootdown.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): vmm_page_unmap is local-invlpg-only, pmm_ref_dec frees immediately at refcount 0, the brk loop frees-then-flushes, and the file's own mm_unmap_range_flush_free header documents this EXACT hazard ("NEVER free before the shootdown ... a frame freed earlier gets recycled + zero-filled for a new owner while the sibling still writes it -- heap-wide corruption") -- a primitive sys_munmap and the MAP_FIXED replace path already use, but which brk shrink (the one VMA-teardown path that open-coded the free) did NOT.  FIX (do-it-right + DRY -- the one shared mechanism, not a third drifting path): route brk shrink through mm_unmap_range_flush_free (batched unmap -> cross-CPU tlb_flush_range + wait -> pmm_ref_dec, MMIO-skipping), and additionally REORDER so the heap VMA is shrunk/removed under mm->vma_lock BEFORE the frame teardown -- a concurrent sibling fault in [new_brk, old_brk) then finds no VMA and SIGSEGVs (correct, it is past the new brk) instead of demand-paging a fresh frame into a range about to be freed; the frames stay mapped+valid until mm_unmap_range_flush_free unmaps+flushes+frees them in the correct order.  The old free-then-flush loop and the trailing tlb_flush_range are removed.  VERIFICATION: a TLB-ordering concurrency UAF; the stale-TLB-write race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof (brk shrink now uses the documented flush-before-free primitive, frames freed only after the cross-CPU shootdown completes; the VMA-first reorder is argued safe above) + clean-boot.  No new selftest -- the fix reuses an existing primitive (nothing new to unit-test), and brk is exercised by every heap allocation/free during boot (login/svcmgr/bash/sway all malloc), so a regression to heap management would crash userland; instead the boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first try, 56 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (n).
- 2026-06-25 - F73 FIXED: sys_poll / sys_select registered an on-stack waiter on a polled file's EMBEDDED wait queue without pinning the file -> use-after-free when a sibling thread closes the fd (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, recorded fan-out finding (q)).  Both loops read `f = files->ft->fd_table[fd]` as a BARE pointer (no ref), then `wait_group_add(&wg, f->waitq, ...)` registered the stack task_we_t on the file's embedded waitq (eventfd_state_t.read_wq/write_wq, timerfd_state_t.wq, pipe _waitq), slept, and `wait_group_cleanup` later walked + unlinked from that waitq.  A sibling thread sharing the fd table (sys_thread + THREAD_SHARE_FILES) closing the fd drops the table ref, and the eventfd/timerfd/pipe close ops kfree the state SYNCHRONOUSLY -- including the embedded waitq -- so the woken poller's wait_group_cleanup -> wq_remove writes (spin_lock(&wq->remove_lock)) and walks (wq->head chain) FREED, possibly reallocated memory = UAF write.  The readiness scans (fd_is_readable/writable/has_hup on the bare f) are the same hazard in a shorter window.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): both functions read fd_table[fd] raw with no vfs_tryget; epoll solves the IDENTICAL hazard by vfs_tryget-pinning w->file (F60, and its comment names this exact "concurrent close() on another thread of a shared files table" race) -- poll/select never adopted the pin; the close ops free synchronously (no RCU/refcount for pollers); THREAD_SHARE_FILES makes the concurrency real.  FIX (do-it-right -- mirror the epoll pin via the existing safe fd->file primitive): pin EVERY referenced fd with fdget() (rcu + vfs_tryget, returns NULL if closed/dying) into a per-call pin array at the TOP of each retry iteration, use the PINNED file for the readiness scan, the waitq registration, and the post-register recheck, then fdput() every pinned file AFTER wait_group_cleanup (fdput(NULL) is safe).  The pin keeps each polled file -- and thus its embedded waitq -- alive across register -> sched_sleep -> cleanup, so a sibling close cannot free it under us (the file's actual teardown is deferred to the poller's fdput).  Same pattern applied to both sys_poll (pin per pollfd entry) and sys_select (pin per fd); the now-unused raw `files` locals were removed.  VERIFICATION: a concurrency UAF; the close-during-cleanup race is not deterministically boot-reproducible -> code-proof (the fdget pin spans the whole register/sleep/cleanup window, so wait_group_cleanup always walks a live waitq) + clean-boot + the existing copy_user_selftest (which drives sys_select with bad fd-set pointers) STILL PASSES (the fd_set copy_from_user validation is unchanged).  poll/select are the busiest syscalls at userspace-start (wayland/sway's event loop polls constantly), so a regression or deadlock in the pinned path would hang the boot -- instead 2 of 2 boots reach the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 56 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes fan-out finding (q).
- 2026-06-25 - F74 FIXED: the PTY pair lifetime (master_open / slave_open_count / the s_pty_head list) was UNLOCKED -> concurrent close of the master and slave ends double-frees / UAFs the pty_t (kernel/drivers/tty/pty.c, kernel/drivers/tty/pty.h, kernel/drivers/tty/tty.c, recorded fan-out finding (o)).  pty_master_close did `master_open = 0; if (slave_open_count == 0) pty_free_locked(pty)` and pty_slave_close did `slave_open_count--; if (slave_open_count == 0 && !master_open) pty_free_locked(pty)` with NO lock and `pty_free_locked` (misnamed -- held no lock) unlinking + kfree'ing.  Two threads sharing the fd table (clone(CLONE_FILES)) closing the two ends on different CPUs can BOTH observe the peer-count==0 free condition and both kfree(pty) = double-free; either side also derefs the other's freed pty (counts, the wake of the peer's embedded waitq) = UAF; and the unlocked s_pty_head insert (pty_alloc) / unlink (free) / walk (pty_open_slave_by_index, tty_get_ctty) can deref a node a concurrent close is unlinking.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): both close ops flip-test-free with no lock; LOCKS.md documents only the per-tty ldisc lock; the file's own pty_free_locked comment even says the free SHOULD be RCU-deferred "because wait_queue_wake_all drainers may still reference the embedded waitqs" -- but the code does a plain kfree.  FIX (do-it-right, one shared mechanism mirroring F70/F25/F61): a single global s_pty_lock serialises the WHOLE pair lifetime.  Both close ops now flip their flag/count, wake the peer waitqs, and decide+unlink the free ALL UNDER the lock; the actual kfree (pty_free_struct) happens after unlock (the pty is already unlinked, reachable only by the freer).  Because the lock makes the free decision atomic, exactly ONE closer frees (the SECOND to take the lock, which is the one that observes both ends closed); and because the close wakes run under the lock, the non-freer's wake of the peer's embedded waitq necessarily COMPLETES before the freer (second) takes the lock and frees -- closing the wake-vs-free race the RCU comment was worried about, without needing RCU.  pty_free_locked was split into pty_unlink_locked (lock-held list unlink) + pty_free_struct (lock-free struct free); pty_alloc now allocates the index under the lock and LINKS the pair into s_pty_head LAST (once fully built) so alloc-error paths just free an unlinked node and no walker sees a half-built pty; pty_open_slave_by_index walks+claims under the lock; and tty_get_ctty's open-coded pty_list_head() walk was replaced by a locked pty_find_ctty_slave(sid) helper.  Lock order is safe: s_pty_lock > {waitq_lock, rq_lock} (via the wakes) is acyclic -- nothing takes those then s_pty_lock -- and the master-close path releases the recursive unclaimed-slave close BEFORE taking the lock (no self-deadlock).  VERIFICATION: a double-free/UAF concurrency fix.  DETERMINISTIC selftest (pty_lifetime_selftest): pty_alloc -> claim the slave -> close the master (slave still open: pty NOT freed, master_open flips 0) -> close the slave (both closed: pty freed AND unlinked, confirmed by a by-index lookup returning NULL) -> `[pty_life] SELF-TEST PASSED (pair freed once, unlinked)`.  The concurrent master-vs-slave double-free is not deterministically reproducible -> the selftest proves the single-threaded lifecycle (free-once + unlink) and code-proof covers the concurrent case (the lock makes the free atomic + orders the wakes).  Clean boot: PTYs are not exercised pre-login (login runs on the tty0 console, terminal emulators that use PTYs start only inside the post-login wayland session), so the selftest is the primary check; the boot still reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first try, 57 selftests PASSED (was 56), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], and the tty0 login prompt renders (the tty_get_ctty change did not break the console ctty path).  ALSO NOTED (separate, lower severity, NOT fixed here): the master ring (m_head/m_tail) is mutated unlocked by pty_master_read (consumer) vs pty_slave_write_buf/char (producer) on different CPUs -- masked indices keep it in-bounds so it is a data race / lost-wakeup, not OOB; recorded as follow-up (r).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes fan-out finding (o).
- 2026-06-26 - F75 FIXED: a TCP SYN_RCVD child PCB's raw ->listener backpointer was never cleared when the listener PCB was freed -> a late handshake ACK derefs+writes through the freed listener (remote-timed heap UAF) (kernel/net/tcp.c, fan-out finding (p)).  When a SYN arrives at a TCP_LISTEN pcb, tcp_recv spawns a child PCB and stores `child->listener = pcb` (tcp.c:410) as a RAW pointer.  When the listener is closed (socket.c sock_close -> tcp_close LISTEN->CLOSED -> tcp_pcb_free), tcp_pcb_free unlinks it from s_pcb_head and call_rcu_expedited-frees it -- but does NOT touch the SYN_RCVD children, which stay on s_pcb_head with a dangling ->listener.  A later final-handshake ACK drives tcp_recv's TCP_SYN_RCVD case (tcp.c:427-432: `lst = pcb->listener; tcp_pcb_lock(lst); accept_q_push(lst, pcb); pcb_wake(lst)`) to spin_lock + write the accept queue + wake THROUGH the freed listener.  RCU does NOT help: it keeps a pcb alive only within ONE tcp_recv reader section, but child->listener is a STORED pointer read in a LATER, separate section -- the listener's grace period has already completed by the ACK, so child->listener points at freed (reused) memory.  Reachable by any peer the QEMU user-net can deliver + an unprivileged process: bind+listen, peer SYN -> child SYN_RCVD, close(listener), peer's final ACK -> UAF write of an attacker-influenced child pointer + queue index into reclaimed slab.  Same class as the F65 AF_UNIX backlog stored-backpointer UAF.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): the child stores pcb raw at SYN, the SYN_RCVD ACK path derefs the raw ->listener, tcp_pcb_free frees the listener with NO child fixup, and grep confirms nothing anywhere clears/reparents child->listener on listener close.  FIX (do-it-right, the universal free chokepoint, mirrors F64 disown-in-the-free-hook): in tcp_pcb_free, BEFORE unlinking, walk s_pcb_head under the already-held s_pcb_wlock and NULL the ->listener of every pcb that points at the one being freed.  Then the SYN_RCVD ACK path's existing `if (lst)` guard skips the dead listener (the child completes ESTABLISHED but is simply never queued -- it ages out via the retransmit timer; no UAF, no leak of the listener).  It is a no-op when the freed pcb is not a listener (no child references it), and a concurrent RX reader that already loaded the old child->listener is safe because the listener's own free is RCU-deferred and keeps it alive until that reader drops its rcu section.  VERIFICATION: a remote-timed concurrency UAF.  DETERMINISTIC selftest (tcp_listener_orphan_selftest): alloc a listener + a SYN_RCVD child on the live list -> tcp_pcb_free(listener) must NULL child->listener; freeing an UNRELATED pcb must NOT clear it; the matching second listener free must -> `[tcp_orphan] SELF-TEST PASSED (listener free orphans SYN_RCVD children)`.  The concurrent late-ACK is not deterministically reproducible -> the selftest proves the orphan-clearing logic and code-proof covers the race (RCU + the clear-before-free ordering).  Clean boot: TCP listeners are not boot-exercised (the boot's DHCP is UDP), so the selftest is the primary check; the boot still reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first try, 58 selftests PASSED (was 57), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders (the orphan-walk added to every tcp_pcb_free did not break PCB teardown).  NOTE (minor scalability): the walk makes tcp_pcb_free O(live PCBs); for MakaOS's connection counts this is negligible and a control-plane (close) op, but a per-listener child list or an is_listener guard would make it O(1) at scale.  This closes the LAST of the four read-only fan-out findings (n=brk TLB, o=pty double-free, p=this, q=poll/select waitq).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes fan-out finding (p).
- 2026-06-26 - F76 FIXED: io_uring dispatch_exec double-fetched sqe->addr/len from the USER-WRITABLE SQE ring after validating them -> TOCTOU arbitrary kernel read/write (LPE) (kernel/io/io_uring.c).  uring->sqes[] is the SQE ring mapped into the submitting task's address space VMA_R|W|USER (vmm_map_physical_user) -- user-writable at any instant.  The SYNC path (io_uring_enter_impl, io_uring.c:1041/1069) and the SQPOLL kthread path (io_uring.c:585/589 -> dispatch_one) pass dispatch_exec a LIVE pointer into sqes[] (NOT a snapshot).  Inside dispatch_exec, IORING_OP_READ/WRITE call `user_buf_check(sqe->addr, sqe->len)` to validate the buffer (io_uring.c:870/890) and then RE-READ `sqe->addr`/`sqe->len` from the same user memory for the actual `f->pread/vfs_read/vfs_write` (io_uring.c:877/879/893).  A concurrent user write that flips sqe->addr to a kernel address (HHDM_OFFSET + target) in the window between the check and the use makes the kernel read file bytes INTO an arbitrary kernel address (OP_READ -> arbitrary write) or leak arbitrary kernel memory onto disk/socket (OP_WRITE -> arbitrary read).  TRIVIALLY reachable: SQPOLL dispatches the live SQE fully concurrently with the user by design (no second thread needed -- just spin flipping sqe->addr); or, without SQPOLL, a second THREAD_SHARE_MM thread races the sync submit.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): sqes[] is the user-mapped VMA_R|W region (io_uring.c:63 comment + the mmap), the sync (1041) and SQPOLL (585) dispatch sites pass `&uring->sqes[head & mask]` (a live pointer), dispatch_exec reads sqe->addr/len twice (validate then use), and the ASYNC io_wq path is SAFE precisely because it snapshots (`w->sqe = *sqe`, io_uring.c:783/825) -- so the fix is to make the sync+SQPOLL paths single-fetch too.  The trusted-mask hardening (prior) bounds only the INDEX, not the re-fetched addr/len.  FIX (do-it-right, make the single-fetch the only fetch like the async path): snapshot the SQE ONCE at the top of dispatch_exec into a kernel-local `io_sqe_t snap = *sqe;` and repoint `sqe = &snap`, so EVERY field read (opcode, addr, len, fd, off, op_flags, user_data, and sqe_fdget) comes from the immutable copy -- user_buf_check and vfs_read/write now read the SAME addr/len, killing the double-fetch for all opcodes at once.  io_sqe_t is exactly 64 bytes (_Static_assert) -- safe on the kstack.  VERIFICATION: a TOCTOU concurrency bug, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (after the snapshot, dispatch_exec touches only the local copy, so the validate and the use are provably the same value) + the existing io_uring_selftest (io_uring_test.c) which builds real SQEs and drives them through io_uring_enter_impl -> dispatch_exec (32 NOP ops + 100 steady-state rounds) STILL PASSES, proving the snapshot did not break the dispatch path + clean-boot.  Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first try, 58 selftests PASSED incl. `[io_uring_test] SELF-TEST PASSED`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  This was the sharpest finding of a fresh read-only fan-out over un-swept subsystems (futex / SMP scheduler / fork-CoW all came back SAFE/hardened).  RECORDS new follow-ups from the same fan-out (verified-real by the agents, VERIFY before fixing): (s) HIGH -- the socket syscalls sys_accept/sys_connect/sys_bind/sys_listen and w_sys_sendmsg/w_sys_recvmsg (+ the SCM_RIGHTS fd loop) obtain the socket via the un-refcounted fd_to_file(fd) (syscall.c:3058) and then BLOCK in the socket op (e.g. unix_sock_accept's WAIT_EVENT_HOOK), dereferencing the bare vfs_file_t across the sleep; a THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling's close(fd) drops the last vfs ref -> unix_put -> RCU-free while the blocked caller is in a quiescent state -> the grace period closes and the socket+file are freed under it = UAF (same class as F73 poll/select; fix = replace fd_to_file with fdget/fdput at each site, exactly as sys_read does).  (t) LOW (correctness, not memory-safety) -- sys_thread's non-shared-files clone path (syscall.c:1492) vfs_dup's fd_table[i] but does NOT copy fd_flags[i], so FD_CLOEXEC is silently dropped for threads given a private fd table (task_fork copies both); fix: copy fd_flags too.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F77 FIXED: nine socket syscalls obtained the socket vfs_file via the un-refcounted fd_to_file(fd) and then operated on it (some BLOCKING) -> a THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling's close(fd) RCU-frees the socket under the caller = use-after-free (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, fan-out finding (s), partial -- the simple socket call sites).  fd_to_file (syscall.c:3058) is a bare fd_table read with NO refcount and NO rcu pin; its contract says it is valid ONLY inside a task_files_t.lock critical section, but these syscalls held no such lock and, worse, sys_accept/sys_connect/sys_recvfrom BLOCK inside the socket op (unix_sock_accept / socket_connect / unix_sock_recv sleep on a WAIT_EVENT_HOOK), dereferencing the bare vfs_file_t across the sleep.  A sibling thread sharing the fd table (sys_thread THREAD_SHARE_FILES, flag 1<<1) calling close(fd) drops the last vfs ref -> the file is RCU-freed; the blocked caller, parked in a quiescent state, lets the grace period complete and then wakes to deref freed (reused) memory = UAF.  Exactly the F73 poll/select class.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): fd_to_file is the bare bounds-checked fd_table[fd] load (no vfs_tryget), the socket ops deref f across sched_sleep, and close()/unix_put RCU-free the file -- nothing kept it alive across the syscall.  FIX (do-it-right, the F73 pattern, one shared mechanism): replace fd_to_file with fdget(fd) (rcu_read_lock + atomic load + vfs_tryget refcount-pin; NULL if dying) at each site and fdput(f) on EVERY return path, refactored to a single-exit `goto out` so the pin is dropped exactly once no matter which branch returns.  Converted: sys_bind, sys_listen, sys_accept (pins the listener across the blocking accept; its freshly-installed child cf is a separate object, vfs_close'd only on fd_install failure), sys_connect, sys_sendto, sys_recvfrom (both block in the unix/inet send/recv), sys_setsockopt, sys_getpeerpid (s scoped in braces so the goto does not jump over its init), sys_shutdown.  Incidental: sys_sendto/sys_recvfrom returned -EINVAL for a bad fd (fd_to_file NULL folded into the !buf||!len check); now -EBADF (correct, and the fd-NULL branch returns before any pin is taken).  VERIFICATION: a sibling-close concurrency UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> the live DHCP exchange exercises sys_sendto/sys_recvfrom (the UDP path) and reaching the lease proves those conversions balance their refs (a leaked pin would wedge the socket, a missing pin would fault); the AF_UNIX path's pin primitive is covered by the passing socketpair / scm_rights / unix_refcount (tryget + get/put balance) selftests; the remaining inet/unix bind/listen/accept/connect/setsockopt/getpeerpid/shutdown are not boot-exercised pre-login -> code-proof (each return path audited to fdput exactly once).  Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first try, 58 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], framebuffer login prompt renders.  REMAINING follow-up (s2, recorded -- NOT done here, a dedicated careful effort): w_sys_sendmsg (syscall.c:6033) + its SCM_RIGHTS fd loop (6065) + w_sys_recvmsg (6113) still use fd_to_file -- they have ~13 return paths each and the SCM loop's `tf = fd_to_file(fds_buf[i])` is entangled with unix_sock_sendfd's ownership-transfer refcount semantics (converting tf naively could double/under-count), so they need a from-scratch conversion + verification of the sendfd contract, and they are NOT boot-exercised pre-login (wayland fd-passing is post-login) so clean-boot will not validate them; ALSO w_sys_sendmsg declares `uint8_t bounce[4096]` ON THE 8KiB kernel stack (syscall.c:~6086) -- a separate latent kstack hazard to kmalloc (F68 class).  Same-class fd_to_file-across-an-op also remains in epoll (sys_epoll_wait/ctl, syscall.c:4902/5038), timerfd (5888/6239) and signalfd (5967) -- other subsystems, recorded for a future turn.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Partially closes fan-out finding (s).
- 2026-06-26 - F78 FIXED: w_sys_sendmsg and w_sys_recvmsg (+ the SCM_RIGHTS fd loop) obtained the socket -- and each passed fd -- via the un-refcounted fd_to_file and then BLOCKED in unix_sock_send_ex/recv_ex, so a THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling close() RCU-frees the socket under the blocked caller = UAF; the SCM fd loop additionally fed a bare unpinned file to unix_sock_sendfd's vfs_dup (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, completes fan-out finding (s), the remaining half of F77).  This is the same sibling-close class as F73/F77 but on the two msghdr syscalls, which F77 deferred because they have ~13 return paths each and the SCM loop's tf was entangled with sendfd's refcount semantics.  VERIFIED the entanglement against the real code before touching it (no-assumptions): unix_sock_sendfd (unix_sock.c:1435) does `dup = vfs_dup(file)` and stores dup in the peer ancillary; vfs_dup (vfs.h:85) bumps file->refcount with an atomic fetch_add ONLY IF it is already > 0 and returns the SAME pointer (the scm_rights selftest asserts recvfd's result == the sent payload, proving same-pointer), and vfs_dup's own comment states callers observing a pointer via an RCU lookup MUST use vfs_tryget instead because the bare-pointer dup races a concurrent last-close.  So the SCM-loop bug is precisely that: `tf = fd_to_file(fds_buf[i])` is an unpinned pointer handed to vfs_dup -- a sibling close(fds_buf[i]) racing the dup's load+add either resurrects a dying file or queues a dangling ancillary pointer (recvfd UAF).  FIX (do-it-right, the F73/F77 pattern, one shared mechanism): convert the socket fd in BOTH functions to fdget(fd) + fdput on EVERY return path via a single-exit `goto out` (sendmsg 13 returns across the cmsg parse, the SCM lookups, the iov scatter loop; recvmsg across the mh copy, the cmsg copyout-fault, the iov gather loop, the final writeback), and ALSO pin each SCM fd with fdget(fds_buf[i]) for the duration of the (non-blocking) unix_sock_sendfd then fdput immediately after -- the pin makes vfs_dup's refcount>0 precondition provably true, the ancillary's dup ref is independent of the pin, and the end-state accounting (ancillary +1) is identical to before, only now race-free.  VERIFICATION: a sibling-close concurrency UAF, not deterministically reproducible, and NOT boot-exercised pre-login (libwayland's fd-passing sendmsg/recvmsg run only inside the post-login session) -> primary proof is code-level (every return path audited to fdput sock exactly once -- the only bare returns left are the two pre-fdget guards; each SCM tf fdput pairs its fdget across the sendfd) + the scm_rights/socketpair/unix_refcount selftests covering the pin primitive + clean boot for no-regression.  Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15; the line deinterleaves -- two CPUs write serial concurrently so the lease braids with the chaselev selftest output, which foiled an exact-string grep until the framebuffer login prompt confirmed it) on the first build, 58 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login renders.  Also normalised a few pre-existing unicode tells (em-dash, -> arrow) to ASCII in the comments these edits rewrote.  This FULLY closes fan-out finding (s).  NOTE (separate, fixed next): w_sys_sendmsg/recvmsg still declare large buffers on the 8KiB kernel stack -- bounce[4096] (both) and fds_buf[253]/inst_fds[253] (~1012 bytes each, SCM_MAX_FD=253) -- an F68-class kstack hazard.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes fan-out finding (s).
- 2026-06-26 - F79 FIXED: w_sys_sendmsg and w_sys_recvmsg declared large buffers on the 8 KiB kernel stack -- bounce[4096] (both) plus fds_buf[SCM_MAX_FD] / inst_fds[SCM_MAX_FD] at SCM_MAX_FD=253 -> 1012 bytes each -- so a single msghdr syscall put ~5 KiB of buffers on the kstack and then descended into the blocking unix_sock_send_ex/recv_ex -> sched chain, an F68-class kernel-stack-overflow hazard (kernel/syscall/syscall.c).  VERIFIED the sizes against the real code (no-assumptions): SCM_MAX_FD is #defined 253 (syscall.c:6012), so int32_t[253] = 1012 bytes, and bounce is a literal [4096]; KSTACK_PAGES=2 = 8 KiB total.  Whether it actually overflowed depended on the compiler coalescing the disjoint-scope fds_buf and bounce slots -- relying on that is exactly the fragile pattern the kstack rule forbids, and the whole codebase already kmallocs its 4 KiB scratch buffers (the F68 lesson).  FIX (do-it-right, off the kstack, performance-conscious): introduce a named MSG_BOUNCE_SZ (4096) and move all three buffers to kmalloc, freed at the single goto-out chokepoint F78 established.  bounce is allocated once per call on the first non-empty iov chunk and reused for the whole gather; fds_buf is allocated once on the first SCM_RIGHTS cmsg; inst_fds is allocated LAZILY on the first actually-arriving fd, so the common no-fd recvmsg (libwayland sends a control buffer on every recvmsg but rarely passes fds) pays ZERO extra allocation.  All three pointers are declared NULL at the top of the function BEFORE the first `goto out`, so the out-label's `if (p) kfree(p)` can never read an indeterminate pointer; every `sizeof(bounce)` (which would have silently become 8 once bounce is a pointer) was replaced by MSG_BOUNCE_SZ; the kmalloc-failure paths set -ENOMEM and goto out with the pointer still NULL (skipped by kfree) and, for inst_fds, vfs_close the just-dequeued payload first so it is not leaked.  A per-CPU bounce was rejected because the buffer is held across the blocking send/recv sleep (another task on the CPU would clobber it); the per-CPU slab makes the per-call kmalloc cheap.  VERIFICATION: a latent kstack-overflow, not deterministically reproducible, and the two syscalls are not boot-exercised pre-login -> code-proof (buffers provably off-stack; every alloc paired with a kfree at the lone out; lazy-alloc + NULL-guard audited) + a clean compile with NO "jump crosses initialization" warning (confirming the decls precede every goto) + clean boot for no-regression.  Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) on the first build, 58 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], framebuffer login prompt renders.  Also normalised one pre-existing em-dash to ASCII in a comment this edit rewrote.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F80 FIXED: sys_epoll_wait and sys_epoll_ctl obtained the epoll file via the un-refcounted fd_to_file(epfd) and then held the eventpoll struct (ef->ctx) across an operation -> a THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling's close(epfd) epoll_close()s and kfrees the struct under them = use-after-free (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, recorded fd_to_file follow-up, epoll subsystem).  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): epoll_close (syscall.c:4839) does `kfree(state->slots); kfree(state); kfree(self)` with NO RCU deferral on state/self, so the moment the last fd ref drops the eventpoll memory is gone.  sys_epoll_wait (5038) reads state=ef->ctx, registers a stack task_we on state->wq (task_we_add), and SLEEPS in sched_sleep (5162) inside the wait loop; a sibling close(epfd) frees state during that sleep, and the post-wake task_we_remove(&state->wq, ...) (5165) + the next loop's spin_lock(&state->lock) deref freed memory -- the sharp, unmitigated sleep-UAF.  sys_epoll_ctl (4902) is the narrower SMP-concurrent sibling: it does not sleep but holds state across spin_lock + kmalloc (ep_grow / the watch alloc) + registration, so a concurrent close(epfd) on another CPU frees state mid-op = UAF on state->lock / the slot table.  (The watched-fd polling at 5074/5149 is already safe: fd_table[wfd] is read only as a pointer VALUE to detect close/reuse, and the actual poll runs on the PINNED w->file -- the F60/epoll_pin fix.)  FIX (do-it-right, the F73/F77/F78/F79 pattern, one shared mechanism): replace fd_to_file with fdget(epfd) (rcu + vfs_tryget pin) in both syscalls and fdput(ef) on every return path.  Both convert to a single-exit `goto out` after declaring every local BEFORE the first goto (so no jump crosses an initialiser -- the build has no -Wjump-misses-init), with the not-an-epoll case (ef pinned but ef->close != epoll_close) using an inline `fdput(ef); return -EBADF;`.  The pin holds ef->refcount > 0 for the whole syscall, so a sibling close(epfd) drops only the fd-table ref and epoll_close runs only at our fdput, after the sleep/op completes.  epoll_wait's kevents kmalloc is freed at the same out (NULL-guarded).  VERIFICATION: a sibling-close concurrency UAF, not deterministically reproducible; epoll's syscall wrappers are not driven by a boot selftest (epoll_watch_refcount_selftest exercises register/unregister, not the wrappers) -> primary proof is code-level (every return path fdputs ef exactly once; the only bare returns left are the g_current/events_ptr guards before fdget and the inline not-an-epoll fdput) + clean compile with no jump-crosses-init warning + clean boot for no-regression.  Clean boot reaches the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) first build, 58 selftests PASSED including `[epoll_pin] SELF-TEST PASSED` (the watch-pin path unbroken), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  RECORDS new follow-up (u) (same epoll function, separate narrower bug, VERIFY before fixing): sys_epoll_ctl's EPOLL_CTL_ADD/MOD read the WATCHED file raw -- `wf = files->ft->fd_table[tfd]` (4922/4959) -- then hand wf to epoll_watch_register which vfs_tryget's it; a sibling close(tfd) racing the gap (across ep_grow/kmalloc) can free+reuse wf before the tryget, so tryget can bump a reused object = UAF.  Mitigated (tryget fails closed unless the slab slot is reused) and narrower than the epfd bug, but real; fix = fdget(tfd) the watched fd across the register, fdput after (the pin makes register's tryget reliably succeed too).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F81 FIXED: w_sys_timerfd_settime, w_sys_timerfd_gettime and w_sys_signalfd (the fd>=0 mask-update path) obtained the file via the un-refcounted fd_to_file(fd) and then dereferenced its backing state across the op -> a THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling's close(fd) kfrees that state under them = use-after-free (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, the last recorded fd_to_file follow-up; this CLOSES the whole fd_to_file UAF class).  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): timerfd_close_op (timerfd.c:199) does `kfree(t); kfree(self)` and signalfd_close_op (signalfd.c:163) does `kfree(s); kfree(self)`, both IMMEDIATE with NO RCU deferral, so the instant the last fd ref drops the timerfd_state/signalfd_state and the vfs_file are gone. - 2026-06-26 - F82 FIXED: sys_epoll_ctl EPOLL_CTL_ADD/MOD read the WATCHED file with a raw, un-refcounted fd_table[tfd] index and then handed it to epoll_watch_register, which vfs_tryget's it -> a sibling close(tfd) racing the gap can free AND REUSE the slab slot before the tryget, so tryget bumps a reused object = use-after-free (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, recorded fan-out follow-up (u), discovered while fixing F80).  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): ADD reads `wf = ((uint32_t)tfd < files->ft->cap) ? files->ft->fd_table[tfd] : NULL` (syscall.c ~4914) then, AFTER ep_grow (which may kmalloc) and the watch kmalloc, calls epoll_watch_register(state, w, wf) -> `w->file = vfs_tryget(wf)` (the F60 pin); MOD (~4951) does the same raw read then unregister + re-register.  The raw read + tryget is NOT inside an rcu_read_lock section, so a concurrent last-close on another CPU (THREAD_SHARE_FILES sibling) can run vfs_close(wf) -> free, and the slab slot can be reused, between the bare read and the tryget; tryget then CAS-bumps whatever now occupies that memory.  Mitigated (tryget fails closed if the slot is merely dying-not-reused) and narrower than the epfd UAF (F80), but real.  FIX (do-it-right, the same fdget/fdput primitive): replace the raw fd_table[tfd] read with fdget(tfd) -- which performs the read AND the vfs_tryget UNDER rcu_read_lock, so the object cannot be freed/reused under us -- then fdput(wf) AFTER epoll_watch_register returns.  The register takes its OWN independent w->file ref (vfs_tryget), now GUARANTEED to succeed because our pin holds wf->refcount > 0, so the watch is never spuriously inert; our pin + fdput are balanced and the fd-table ref keeps wf alive past fdput.  ADD fdputs on all three exits after the pin (ep_grow fail, watch kmalloc fail, success); MOD fdputs only inside `if (wf)` (NULL == tfd closed -> leave the watch unregistered, as before).  fdget/fdput run under state->lock -- rcu_read_lock nests fine under a spinlock and fdput cannot free wf (the fd table still holds a ref), so no lock-order or recursion issue.  BEHAVIOUR note: ADD on a fd that is concurrently dying now returns -EBADF (fdget NULL) instead of silently inserting an inert watch -- strictly more correct, and only reachable in the very race being fixed.  VERIFICATION: a sibling-close+reuse UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (each ADD/MOD path fdputs the pin exactly once; identical behaviour for any open fd since fdget == the old raw read plus an rcu-protected pin) + the epoll_pin selftest still PASSES + clean boot.  Clean boot first try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) line 40, 58 selftests PASSED incl. `[epoll_pin] SELF-TEST PASSED`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  This closes follow-up (u) and completes epoll's fd-lifetime safety (both the epfd F80 and the watched fd here).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F83 FIXED: sys_thread's private-fd-table clone path copied fd_table[] but NOT fd_flags[], so FD_CLOEXEC was silently dropped on every fd a spawn'd task inherits -> a close-on-exec fd wrongly SURVIVES the task's later exec (fd leak across exec; correctness, LOW) (kernel/syscall/syscall.c, recorded follow-up (t)).  VERIFIED all three premises against the real code FIRST (no-assumptions): (1) sys_thread's non-shared branch (the `else` of `if (flags & THREAD_SHARE_FILES)`, syscall.c:1491) did `for (i<src->cap) dst->fd_table[i] = vfs_dup(src->fd_table[i])` with NO dst->fd_flags[i] copy; (2) task_fork (process.c:558-561) is the correct reference -- its loop copies BOTH `cft->fd_table[i] = vfs_dup(pft->fd_table[i])` AND `cft->fd_flags[i] = pft->fd_flags[i]`, and fd_table_grow (process.c:93-94) likewise memcpy's both arrays, so only the sys_thread clone drifted; (3) FD_CLOEXEC lives in the parallel fd_flags[] array (process.h:106) and exec consumes it (syscall.c:1034-1043 closes every fd with `fd_flags[i] & FD_CLOEXEC`), so dropping it means the fd is not closed on exec.  fd_table_init(files, src->cap) -> fdtable_alloc allocates both arrays at src->cap, so the new write is in-bounds.  FIX (do-it-right, mirror the correct path exactly, no drift): add `dst->fd_flags[i] = src->fd_flags[i];` inside the clone loop, making it identical to task_fork.  REACHABILITY: a task created via sys_thread WITHOUT THREAD_SHARE_FILES (spawn -- private fd table copied from the parent) that holds a CLOEXEC fd and later execs; the fd would have leaked into the exec'd image.  VERIFICATION: a correctness/leak fix, not a crash -> code-proof (one-line mirror of the audited task_fork loop; in-bounds write; identical structure) + clean boot (the private-fd-table spawn path is exercised by every userspace spawn, so a broken fd_flags copy would wedge or crash the boot).  Clean boot first try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 58 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (t).
- 2026-06-26 - F84 FIXED: the PTY master ring (slave output -> master read; master_buf + m_head/m_tail) was mutated with NO lock by the producer (pty_slave_write_char / pty_slave_write_buf, run from the slave write() path) and the consumer (pty_master_read) on different CPUs -> a data race on the plain uint32_t head/tail indices that can tear an index, lose a byte, double-read, or drop a wakeup (a reader observing a stale head sleeps through a just-produced byte) (kernel/drivers/tty/pty.c + pty.h, recorded follow-up (r)).  Masked indices keep every access in-bounds, so it is a correctness/data-race bug, NOT an OOB write.  VERIFIED against the real code (no-assumptions): (1) the producer path tty_vfs_write -> tty->write_buf is called with NO lock held (tty.c:71 even forbids holding tty->lock there), and pty_master_read takes no lock, so head and tail are touched concurrently and unsynchronised -- the F74 s_pty_lock serialises the pair LIFETIME, not this data path, and pty->slave.lock guards only the SLAVE input ring (tty_t), not this master OUTPUT ring; (2) the analogous slave input ring is correctly serialised by tty->lock (tty_input_char producer + tty_ldisc_drain consumer both hold it, tty.c:264-279), so the master ring simply lacked the symmetric lock; (3) the master ring is genuinely multi-producer/multi-consumer-capable (concurrent writers on a shared slave fd, concurrent readers on a shared master fd), so a lock -- not just SPSC release/acquire atomics -- is required.  FIX (do-it-right, one shared mechanism mirroring tty->lock + tty_ldisc_drain): add a per-pty `master_lock` (spinlock) held around the head/tail MUTATIONS ONLY on both sides -- pty_slave_write_char's push, pty_slave_write_buf's whole Phase-1 push loop, and a new extracted pty_master_drain() (mirror of tty_ldisc_drain) that pty_master_read calls.  The lock is released BEFORE every wake_all and before the blocking WAIT_EVENT/WAIT_EVENT_HOOK, so it never nests over the waitq/rq locks and is never held across a sleep (no deadlock, no lock-order cycle); the lockless condition checks in the WAIT_EVENT macros are kept exactly as the tty ring does them (the wake + sched_sleep barrier handles the wakeup ordering).  The drain copies into the sys_read buffer under the lock, which is safe because sys_read user_buf_prefault's the user pages before calling read() (same reason tty_ldisc_drain may copy under tty->lock).  pty_master_push_byte now documents the caller-holds-master_lock contract.  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU data race, not deterministically reproducible, and PTYs are NOT boot-exercised pre-login (login runs on tty0; PTY terminal emulators start only inside the post-login wayland session) -> added a DETERMINISTIC selftest (pty_master_ring_selftest, mirrors pty_lifetime_selftest's pty_alloc setup): drive the producer (write_char 'hi' + write_buf "there") and the consumer (pty_master_drain) -- all now under master_lock -- and assert the ring round-trips "hithere" and drains empty with no self-deadlock; code-proof covers the cross-CPU case (master_lock makes the mutations atomic).  Clean boot: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15, prefix garbled by concurrent-CPU serial interleaving but the IP/GW fragment is intact), 59 selftests PASSED (was 58) incl. `[pty_mring] SELF-TEST PASSED` AND `[pty_life] SELF-TEST PASSED` (the master_lock add did not break the pair lifecycle), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders.  (Pre-existing unrelated warning: PTY_TRACE macro redefined at pty.c:32 -- not touched.)  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched. Closes follow-up (r).
- 2026-06-26 - ASSESSED follow-up (d) (AHCI LBA-vs-capacity bound) -> SAFE, NOT a memory-safety bug, NO fix.  Verified skeptically against the real code (no-assumptions): every AHCI submit path (ahci_submit_hhdm/ahci_submit_sg/ahci_read_user) bounds the MEMORY transfer by count via xfer_bytes_ok(count,512,..) + the PRDT entry cap (the F47 wrap/PRDT guard), INDEPENDENT of lba -- lba only selects disk sectors, the PRDT built from buf/count fixes the memory region, so an out-of-range lba cannot cause an OOB memory access.  The lba is not attacker-controlled: there is NO raw user block-device path (no /dev/sd / blkdev / AHCI ioctl, grep-confirmed); the only callers are the trusted ext2 fs (ext2_blk_to_lba, F46-wrap-guarded) and the boot stress harness.  AHCI does not store a device capacity from IDENTIFY, so an lba+count<=capacity check would be a new FEATURE, not a dropped bound; and the ATA drive aborts an out-of-range LBA itself (no transfer), so the worst case is a failed I/O the fs handles.  A partition-end clamp would be defense-in-depth against a corrupt fs image (trusted-fs/feature concern), not a reachable memory-safety bug.  Recorded SAFE in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md; not fixed.
- 2026-06-26 - RECORDED follow-up (l) (raw-deref-vs-munmap TOCTOU) -> DEFERRED (big mechanism), design noted, NO fix this pass.  A syscall that prefaults a user buffer then derefs it RAW has a TOCTOU window vs a THREAD_SHARE_MM sibling munmap/mprotect -> kernel-mode #PF.  Robust fix = a kernel exception-fixup table (extable, Linux __ex_table model): tag raw user-deref RIPs so the #PF handler returns -EFAULT instead of panicking.  copy_*_user already have fault handling and the DMA paths already pin the user frames, so the exposure is the remaining non-pinned prefault-then-raw-deref sites; no clean per-site sub-fix short of the extable (a cross-cutting mechanism too large for one audit step).  Design recorded in docs/AUDIT_FINDINGS.md as known debt; deferred to a dedicated effort.  This drains the recorded backlog (s,u,t,r,d,l all resolved: fixed or SAFE/deferred); next is a fresh read-only fan-out over un-swept subsystems.

Three CANDIDATE bugs surfaced (HIGH agent-confidence, NOT yet independently verified -- VERIFY each against the real code before fixing): (v) HIGH evdev evdev_client_t UAF -- input_device_emit walks d->clients + derefs each client (ring_push/sched_wake/wake_all) UNLOCKED while evdev_vfs_close unlinks+kfree's it (same class as F84/F70/F65; unprivileged-reachable via /dev/input/event0 read + sibling close with input flowing); (x) HIGH ext2 block/inode bitmap OOB -- s_blocks_per_grp/s_inodes_per_grp from the untrusted superblock are never clamped to the one-block bitmap capacity (s_block_size*8), so a crafted/corrupt image makes free_block/alloc_block index the fixed 4096-byte bitmap scratch out of bounds (heap OOB write/read; reached via truncate/write); (w) MED-LOW NVMe doorbell BAR0 OOB -- fixed 0x2000 BAR0 map vs device-CAP.DSTRD-scaled doorbell offset, NOT reachable on QEMU (DSTRD=0). - 2026-06-26 - F85 FIXED: the evdev per-open client list AND each client's event ring were mutated with NO lock by a producer and a consumer/closer on different CPUs -> a use-after-free (input_device_emit derefs a client a concurrent close() freed) plus a torn-index ring data race (fan-out candidate (v), kernel/drivers/input/evdev.c + evdev.h).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): input_device_emit (evdev.c, the EV_* publish primitive) walks d->clients and for each client does ring_push(c) + sched_wake(c->reader) + wait_queue_wake_all(c->file->waitq) with NO lock; evdev_vfs_close unlinks c from d->clients and kfree(c)s it with NO lock; the producer reaches c via the d->clients list (never via an fd), so the vfs refcount does not protect it -- a close() drives the file refcount 1->0 and frees c while the producer still holds the list-derived pointer = UAF (kernel-heap write via ring_push + two dangling derefs).  CONFIRMED the producer truly runs concurrently AND can be in IRQ context: the keyboard producer is the keyboard_thread_fn kthread (input_emit -> evdev_on_kbd_event), but the MOUSE producer runs in IRQ context (i8042 keyboard_irq_handler -> i8042_isr_drain -> mouse_isr_packet -> packet_decode -> evdev_on_mouse_packet -> input_device_emit; mouse.c warns against a "mid-ISR context switch"), so any lock here MUST be IRQ-safe.  Also confirmed the secondary torn-index race on c->head/c->tail (plain uint32_t, producer ring_push vs consumer ring_pop, no lock; in-bounds because masked -> data race / lost event, same class as F84).  FIX (do-it-right, the F84/F70 pattern, ONE shared mechanism): add a per-input_device IRQ-safe spinlock (input_device_t.lock, spin_lock_irqsave) that serialises BOTH the client-list lifetime AND each client's ring head/tail.  input_device_emit holds it across the whole fan-out walk + ring_push + the wakes (the wakes do not sleep and the order d->lock -> rq/waitq locks is acyclic, so waking under the lock is safe -- no snapshot array needed; matches that the wakes already ran in IRQ context).  evdev_vfs_close drops the grab + unlinks UNDER the lock, then kfree(c)s AFTER the unlock when c is no longer reachable by any emit walk.  evdev_vfs_read takes the lock around the ring_empty check + the ring_pop drain, dropping it around sched_sleep (the wake_pending interlock in sched_wake/sched_sleep covers the wake that fires between release and park, so no lost wakeup); the drain copies into the prefaulted sys_read buffer under the lock (safe, same contract as tty_ldisc_drain/pty_master_drain).  EVIOCGRAB mutates d->grabbed/c->grabbed under the lock; evdev_open_device inserts under the lock; input_device_register inits the lock.  poll and FIONREAD keep their lockless advisory ring reads (same as the tty ring's WAIT_EVENT condition).  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF + data race, not deterministically reproducible -> added a DETERMINISTIC selftest (evdev_ring_selftest): build a device + client, drive input_device_emit (locked fan-out push) x3 + a locked ring_pop drain, assert the 3 events round-trip, then unlink+free the client under the lock asserting no self-deadlock + a clean list; code-proof covers the concurrent case (d->lock serialises emit-walk vs unlink+free and the head/tail).  Clean boot first try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 60 selftests PASSED (was 59) incl. `[evdev_ring] SELF-TEST PASSED`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders -- and crucially no boot hang (the IRQ-safe lock on the boot-exercised console keyboard producer did not deadlock).  This closes fan-out candidate (v).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F86 FIXED: the ext2 per-group block/inode bitmaps are RMW'd in a FIXED 4096-byte scratch buffer, but s_blocks_per_group / s_inodes_per_group from the untrusted superblock were validated only != 0 -- never clamped to the one-block bitmap capacity (block_size*8) -- so a crafted/corrupt image makes alloc/free index the scratch out of bounds = heap OOB read/write (fan-out candidate (x), kernel/fs/ext2.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the bitmap helpers bitmap_find_free/set/clear/test (ext2.c:714-734) index bitmap[bit>>3] / scan to max_bits with NO bound; the four scratch buffers are EXT2_SCRATCH = kmalloc(EXT2_BLOCK_SIZE_MAX) = a fixed 4096 bytes = 32768 bits, independent of s_block_size; the mount validator (ext2.c:877) checked only `s_blocks_per_grp==0 || s_inodes_per_grp==0 || s_blocks_count==0` (the comment even calls them untrusted on-disk data but never clamps the geometry); and the OOB sites compute the in-group bit WITHOUT clamping it: free_block does bit = rel % s_blocks_per_grp then bitmap_test/clear(fbb_buf, bit) (1792-1793) with only a `g >= s_num_groups` GROUP check (not a bit check), alloc_block does bitmap_find_free(bbm_buf, s_blocks_per_grp) (1756), and alloc_inode (1716) / free_inode_num (1816-1817) are the inode-bitmap equivalents.  So with s_blocks_per_group forged > 32768 (e.g. on a 1 KiB-block image whose legit max is 8192) and a block whose within-group offset exceeds 32767, bitmap_clear(fbb_buf, bit) writes fbb_buf[bit>>3] past the 4096-byte allocation = a controlled heap OOB WRITE (bit is attacker-influenced via the block number), plus an OOB read via bitmap_find_free.  This is NOT guarded elsewhere: ext2_block_valid bounds the block NUMBER used as an LBA, not the in-group bit index.  TRUST MODEL (stated honestly): reachable with a crafted/corrupt ext2 image -- an attacker-supplied removable volume the kernel mounts, or a corrupted root fs -- not from a well-formed image (where blocks/inodes-per-group <= block_size*8 by the ext2 invariant).  Distinct from F30/F46/F50/F54/F56/F68/F69.  FIX (do-it-right, mirror the existing geometry guards ext2_block_size_checked / ext2_inode_size_valid): added a pure ext2_group_geom_valid(blocks_per_grp, inodes_per_grp, block_size) helper returning false unless BOTH fields are in [1, block_size*8] (the bits in a one-block bitmap), and call it at the mount-time superblock validation (ext2.c:877) to REFUSE the mount; block_size <= EXT2_BLOCK_SIZE_MAX so block_size*8 <= 32768 fits the scratch exactly.  VERIFICATION: a heap-OOB on a crafted image, not reproducible from the boot image -> a DETERMINISTIC pure-helper selftest (ext2_group_geom_selftest): the legit per-block-size maxima (8192@1KiB, 32768@4KiB) pass, blocks- or inodes-per-group one over cap is rejected, zero is rejected.  Clean boot first try: DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15), 61 selftests PASSED (was 60) incl. `[ext2_geom] SELF-TEST PASSED`, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login prompt renders -- and the boot reaching userspace is itself a STRONG check that the REAL root fs passes the new geometry gate (a too-strict bound would have failed the root mount and never reached login).  This closes fan-out candidate (x).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F87 FIXED: the NVMe driver mapped BAR0 with a FIXED 0x2000 (8 KiB) but the doorbell offset scales with the DEVICE-reported CAP.DSTRD and the queue id, so a controller advertising a large DSTRD drives an MMIO store past the mapping = OOB MMIO write at the sq/cq_doorbell sites (fan-out candidate (w), kernel/drivers/storage/nvme.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): s_regs = vmm_map_mmio(bar_phys, 0x2000) is a fixed 8 KiB map (nvme.c:677); s_doorbell_stride = 4u << dstrd where dstrd = (CAP >> 32) & 0xF is read from the controller and NEVER validated (685-687); sq_doorbell(y)/cq_doorbell(y) = s_regs + 0x1000 + (2*y[+1])*stride (211-215) are written at submit (450) and the IRQ completion handler (508); the qid runs 1..nr_queues via NVME_IOQ_QID(cpu)=cpu+1 (134) with nr_queues <= MAX_CPUS=64; so the highest doorbell cq_doorbell(64) = 0x1000 + 129*stride exceeds 0x2000 once stride >= 32 (dstrd >= 3) -- e.g. dstrd=3 -> 0x2020 > 0x2000.  CONFIRMED not reachable on the boot device: QEMU reports DSTRD=0 (stride 4) so cq_doorbell(64) = 0x1000+129*4 = 0x1204 fits 0x2000, AND the QEMU config attaches NO NVMe device at all (only AHCI) -- nvme_init's pci_find returns "not present" and bails at nvme.c:663 before the BAR0 map, so this code is not even reached at boot (serial shows `[initcall] nvme` with no `[nvme] found controller`).  MED-LOW: malicious/buggy controller only; the faulting target is MMIO VA so the likely outcome is a page fault, not silent kernel-memory corruption.  FIX (do-it-right, map the real extent -- there is no pci_bar_size helper and no vmm_unmap_mmio, and CAP must be read THROUGH the map first): after reading CAP, compute db_extent = round_up(0x1000 + (2*MAX_CPUS+1)*s_doorbell_stride + 4, page) -- the highest doorbell for any nr_queues <= MAX_CPUS -- refuse the controller if that exceeds a 1 MiB ceiling (NVME_BAR0_MAX_MAP, an absurd DSTRD), and re-map BAR0 over db_extent BEFORE the admin-queue setup writes the qid-0 doorbells; the common small-stride case (DSTRD=0 -> extent rounds to 0x2000) is left byte-identical (no remap), so QEMU/real devices are unchanged.  The doorbell macros are untouched (s_regs now spans db_extent).  VERIFICATION: NOT reproducible (no NVMe device + a malicious DSTRD), so CODE-PROOF: db_extent provably covers cq_doorbell(MAX_CPUS) >= cq_doorbell(any used qid) + the 4-byte write, the reject closes the absurd-stride case, and the DSTRD=0 path is unchanged -- plus clean boot for no-regression.  The first two boots hit the flaky F55 userspace-start stall (no DHCP though login rendered); the SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) on the 3rd try with 61 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login renders -- and since nvme_init bails before this code with no NVMe device, the change is provably inert at boot and cannot have caused the stall.  No deterministic selftest (the doorbell extent depends on the device's DSTRD; the computation is a one-line round-up of the highest doorbell offset, trivially correct).  This closes fan-out candidate (w) -- all three fan-out candidates (v/x/w) are now resolved.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.

- 2026-06-26 - F88 FIXED: /proc/<pid>/fd/* dereferenced another task's fd table (t->files_shared->ft->fd_table[n]) under rcu_read_lock, but sys_exit frees that table SYNCHRONOUSLY -> a cross-process use-after-free reachable by any same-uid process reading /proc/<exiting-pid>/fd (fan-out #3 candidate (z); kernel/fs/proc.c + kernel/proc/process.c + kernel/syscall/syscall.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): proc_fd_open (proc.c:287), proc_fd_readdir (300) and proc_stat's fd branch (593) load t->files_shared->ft and tryget fd_table[n] under rcu_read_lock (the comment even says "snapshot the fdtable_t under RCU"); but task_files_release (process.c:114) vfs_close's the fds AND kfree's ft->fd_table / ft->fd_flags / ft / f SYNCHRONOUSLY with NO call_rcu (contrast mm_shared, freed only in task_free_rcu after a grace period), and sys_exit (syscall.c:722) calls it then NULLs files_shared with a plain store -- so the reader's rcu_read_lock does NOT protect the table (the freer never waited for a grace period).  The task STRUCT is RCU-pinned (task_free_rcu) but files_shared/the fdtable_t is not, so a /proc reader of an exiting target derefs a kfree'd fdtable_t (then trygets a freed slot pointer) = UAF; reachable cross-process because /proc fd nodes are mode 0400 owner=target uid (a parent reading /proc/<child>/fd), unlike fdget which only touches g_current's OWN always-valid table.  ALSO found a second-order NULL-deref race: proc read t->files_shared TWICE (the !NULL guard then the ->ft deref), so a concurrent exit NULLing it between the two reads -> NULL->ft fault.  FIX (do-it-right, option b, preserve the load-bearing exit_files EOF semantics, mirror the RCU lifetime doctrine): (1) task_files_release still vfs_close's every fd SYNCHRONOUSLY (so pipe/socket/tty peers see EOF at exit, per the syscall.c:678 contract) but now DEFERS the struct memory free via call_rcu_expedited(task_files_free_rcu) -- so a /proc reader holding rcu_read_lock keeps a valid table; the fd_table[n] FILE pointers are handled by the existing tryget-under-rcu (same as fdget, files are RCU-freed).  (2) sys_exit UNPUBLISHES files_shared with a __ATOMIC_RELEASE store BEFORE task_files_release, so the RCU order is correct (unpublish -> call_rcu): no new reader can grab the table after the call_rcu, and the grace period waits out any reader that already snapshotted it.  (3) the three proc readers now snapshot t->files_shared ONCE with an __ATOMIC_ACQUIRE load into a local and use the snapshot (closes the double-read NULL-deref race).  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (the table survives the reader's rcu_read_lock via the deferred free; the unpublish-before-call_rcu ordering; the single-load snapshot) + clean boot (the process-exit path runs on EVERY exit and /proc is read, both heavily boot-exercised, so a double-free / missed-free / deadlock would crash the boot -- a strong check; the exit-path selftests [task_exit_state] and [tgleader] also pass).  First boot hit the flaky F55 stall (no DHCP, login rendered, no fault); the SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) at line 110 with 61 selftests PASSED, 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login renders.  This closes fan-out #3 candidate (z).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F89 FIXED: io_uring_close_file stopped+joined the io_wq worker BEFORE the SQPOLL kthread, so the still-running SQPOLL kthread could spawn the worker AFTER close skipped it -> an orphaned worker that UAFs the freed ring (fan-out #3 candidate (aa); kernel/io/io_uring.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): the teardown set worker_stop (121) then sqp_stop (123), then JOINED the worker (125-129, gated on uring->worker) then JOINED SQPOLL (130-134); the io_wq worker is spawned LAZILY by io_wq_ensure_worker which did a PLAIN store uring->worker = t + sched_add (780), and io_sqp_kthread_entry (587) calls it on an IOSQE_ASYNC SQE; the worker self-exits ONLY when it observes worker_stop (693).  So if no async op had run yet (worker == NULL), close skipped setting worker_stop AND skipped the worker join, but SQPOLL -- told to stop at 123 -- could still be mid-drain and io_wq_ensure_worker() a worker BEFORE observing sqp_stop, publishing uring->worker after close already passed the worker phase; close then joined only SQPOLL and freed uring + pmm_buddy_free'd the backing, and the orphaned worker (worker_stop never set -> never exits) posts CQEs into the reused freed pages = UAF.  CONFIRMED the fix is sufficient: the OTHER worker-spawn site, io_uring_enter_impl, runs under sys_io_uring_enter's fdget ref (syscall.c:5816 fdget...fdput), so close (the last-ref-drop file close handler) provably cannot run during an in-flight enter -- the SQPOLL kthread (which holds NO fd ref) is the ONLY spawn site that can race close.  FIX (do-it-right, minimal correct reorder): stop + JOIN the SQPOLL kthread FIRST (set sqp_stop, wait sqp_done), and ONLY THEN read uring->worker / set worker_stop / join the worker -- after sqp_done the SQPOLL spawner is provably dead and (enter being ref-serialised) uring->worker is stable.  Hardened the worker publish to an __ATOMIC_RELEASE store and ALL uring->worker reads (close join + the io_wq_ensure_worker fast-path) to __ATOMIC_ACQUIRE loads, so the post-SQPOLL-join read observes a worker SQPOLL published just before exiting AND there is no mixed atomic/plain data race (the init reset at 233 is pre-publication, stays plain).  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU teardown UAF, not deterministically reproducible -> code-proof (SQPOLL joined before the worker phase; enter ref-serialised; release/acquire on the publish) + the existing io_uring_test selftest STILL PASSES (it drives ring create -> enter/dispatch -> close, exercising the reordered teardown) + clean boot. This closes fan-out #3 candidate (aa).  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
- 2026-06-26 - F90 FIXED: the ksec setuid/escalation daemon used ONE global rendezvous slot (s_pending) with NO lock for ALL callers, so on SMP two concurrent setuid/seteuid/setuid-exec callers overwrote each other's slot -> the reader sched_wake'd a task_t* that had already returned/exited (a UAF write through a dangling task) AND a "behind" caller read the OTHER caller's verdict = cross-talk -> PRIVILEGE ESCALATION in the privilege-gating daemon (fan-out #3 candidate (y); kernel/security/ksec.c).  INDEPENDENTLY VERIFIED the agent's claim against the real code (no-assumptions): s_pending was a single static {seq, resp, waiter (raw task_t*), done} with the file's own comment admitting "Single-CPU, cooperative... Multi-CPU extension: replace with a hash-table keyed on seq"; ksec_request stored waiter=g_current+seq+done=0 then sched_sleep'd in a `while(!done)` loop that did NOT check signals, and ksec_reader_thread matched on seq, set done, and sched_wake(waiter) -- ALL unsynchronised; sys_setuid/sys_seteuid (syscall.c:3938/3958) and ksec_exec_setuid (elf.c:913 / syscall.c:1090) call ksec_request, and the scheduler is genuinely SMP (g_current = this_cpu()->current), so two concurrent setuids overwrite the slot.  REACHABILITY: the ksec daemon is a real built userland app (userland/apps/ksec, registers via sys_register_policy_agent which spawns ksec_reader_thread) -- when deployed, every setuid races the single slot; a "behind" caller A that reaches `while(!done)` after caller B set done=1 reads B's resp (B's granted_euid) = priv-esc; a killed setuid leaves a dangling waiter for the reader to wake = UAF.  Also found two related SMP bugs the agent missed: ksec_next_seq did a NON-ATOMIC `++s_seq` (two concurrent callers could get the SAME seq -> slot collision) and wrapped to 0 (the free-slot marker).  FIX (do-it-right, the "hash-table keyed on seq" the comment itself prescribes, ONE shared mechanism): replaced the single slot with a per-seq slot array s_slots[KSEC_MAX_INFLIGHT=64] under a spinlock s_ksec_lock; ksec_request CLAIMS its own slot under the lock (fail CLOSED -> -EAGAIN -> -EPERM if all 64 in-flight, since denying a setuid is safe), the sleep loop DROPS the lock around sched_sleep (never held across a sleep) and is now SIGNAL-INTERRUPTIBLE (a killed/signalled setuid frees its slot under the lock and returns -EINTR, closing the dangling-waiter UAF + a pre-existing infinite-hang), and frees its slot UNDER the lock after waking; ksec_reader_thread matches the response to its slot by seq UNDER the lock and sets done + sched_wake's the waiter UNDER the lock (so the requester, which frees its slot only under the lock after waking, cannot free/return before the reader finishes -> no wake of a freed task); ksec_next_seq is now an atomic __atomic_add_fetch that skips 0.  The userland policy parser was already bounded (SAFE) and is untouched.  VERIFICATION: a cross-CPU UAF + priv-esc, not deterministically reproducible -> a DETERMINISTIC selftest (ksec_slot_selftest): distinct seqs claim distinct slots, ksec_slot_find matches by seq, seq 0 / unknown match nothing, a freed slot is reusable; code-proof covers the concurrent case (every slot access under s_ksec_lock; free-under-lock-after-wake; signal cleanup).  The change is provably INERT at boot (no ksec daemon is auto-registered -> ksec_request returns -EAGAIN at its first check before the new slot code; serial shows no policy-agent registration/setuid) so it cannot affect the boot/DHCP path.  Clean boot: 2 boots hit the flaky F55 stall (no DHCP, no fault); the 3rd SAME-build re-boot reached the DHCP lease (ifconfig IP 10.0.2.15) line 111, 62 selftests PASSED incl. `[ksec_slot] SELF-TEST PASSED` AND `[ksec_setuid] SELF-TEST PASSED` (the gate, unaffected), 0 FAILED/PANIC, no [WD], login renders.  This closes fan-out #3 candidate (y) -- ALL fan-out #3 candidates (z/aa/y) are now resolved.  Both builds compile; shipping disk clean. main untouched.
